**DST ChatGPT Port — Documented Summary** 

**Status: Working Summary / Forward-Looking Design Record**  

**Purpose: Summarize the ChatGPT-port work, added fidelity rules, mutable-kernel structure, recording improvements, user-layer concept, and future role-specific project modules.**

**\---**

**1\. Core Purpose of the ChatGPT Port**

**The goal is to reproduce the working DST process in a ChatGPT Project environment while preserving the central DST architecture:**

**a mutable kernel that evolves through jury-discovered preclusionary rules;**

**a canon that frames and translates but does not function as domain authority;**

**a formal intake that declares domain standards, problem space, proof standards, nullification conditions, and success criteria;**

**clean one-shot traversal instances;**

**clean external jury assessment;**

**advisor-assisted manual revision;**

**preserved records sufficient for continuation without hidden memory.**

**The ChatGPT port required restructuring because ChatGPT Project Instructions cannot hold a long Claude-style kernel. The resulting architecture uses a short bootstrap kernel in the Project Instructions field and a long mutable active kernel as an uploaded source file with explicitly declared operational status.**

**\---**

**2\. Foundational DST Architecture**

**DST is a ledgered traversal ecology: a recorded environment in which agents, roles, claims, bridges, residues, juries, and emergent taxonomies co-evolve under declared constraints.**

**The system is not a proof-checker, notebook, or search engine. It is a self-correcting traversal system that lets representation expand enough to discover structure while requiring persistent structures to become recordable, criticizable, scoped, and status-labeled.**

**The kernel is the evolving operational instrument. The traversal report is the final product of a particular firing. The final traversal must be produced from a fresh project thread using the declared canon and intake. The audit trail records how the kernel evolved and why the final traversal is reproducible and audit-survivable.**

**\---**

**3\. Layer Separation**

**3.1 Bootstrap Kernel**

**The short Project Instructions field. It routes the model to the correct source files, defines authority hierarchy, prevents source flattening, and forbids simulated process completion.**

**3.2 Mutable Active Kernel**

**The long evolving operational rulebook. It lives in the Project source area but is not ordinary canon. It is binding because the bootstrap identifies it as binding operational kernel material.**

**3.3 Canon**

**The philosophical, theoretical, model-building, heuristic, and translational substrate. Canon helps the traversal engine frame problems and translate across domains. It is not proof authority. A canon claim does not become a valid domain result merely by appearing in canon.**

**3.4 Formal Intake**

**The intake declares the problem-specific field: formal base, domain standards, nullification algebra, success criteria, proof standards, known hazards, process parameters, and required outputs. Domain standards are activated by intake and by ordinary accepted practice in the declared domain.**

**3.5 Records**

**Prior traversal reports, jury reports, advisor commentary, operator decisions, continuation prompts, accepted/rejected kernel changes, and unresolved residues preserve project continuity. Records are historical state, not automatic proof.**

**\---**

**4\. Revised File Structure for ChatGPT Project**

**Recommended mutable files:**

**\`00\\\_ACTIVE\\\_DST\\\_KERNEL\\\_APPENDIX.md\`**  

**Mutable extended kernel. Update only when accepted jury findings create real preclusionary rules or structural process changes.**

**\`01\\\_DST\\\_CONTROL\\\_LEDGER.md\`**  

**Combined changelog, cycle log, jury-decision log, file-update log, and operator/advisor notes.**

**\`02\\\_TOEPLITZ\\\_ACTIVE\\\_CONTINUITY\\\_STATE.md\`**  

**Current state of the Toeplitz/Inscribed Square traversal: target, preserved gains, exhausted routes, held flags, live bridges, known hazards, next objective.**

**\`03\\\_TOEPLITZ\\\_TRAVERSAL\\\_RECORD\\\_INDEX.md\`**  

**Index of prior traversal records and what each contributes.**

**Stable files:**

**\`10\\\_CANON\\\_...\` files for worldview/framing/translation materials.**

**\`20\\\_RECORD\\\_...\` or \`30\\\_PRIOR\\\_TRAVERSAL\\\_...\` files for historical traversal records.**

**This structure preserves fine-grained record keeping without forcing edits to many documents after each iteration.**

**\---**

**5\. Idealized DST Convergence Axiom**

**A faithfully executed DST process, applied over a continuum of iterative correction under sufficient fidelity, converges toward the frontier that the juror/operator ecology can currently describe, formalize, criticize, and refine.**

**This is not framed as a field theorem about the underlying problem. It is a process-level axiom of DST under its own operating commitments.**

**Absolute fidelity implies absolute convergence relative to the reachable frontier: every relevant distinction, theorem, residue, obstruction, premise, domain standard, frontier condition, and evolving juror distinction is preserved without distortion, omission, substitution, or premature closure.**

**The juror's frontier is not frozen. It may change each round as the juror reassesses prior statements, identifies new distinctions, sharpens objections, withdraws objections, or discovers new gates. The convergence object is the coupled DST-juror frontier across iteration, not a static first-round snapshot.**

**\---**

**6\. Frontier Fidelity Rule**

**Frontier fidelity is not optional documentation. It is a convergence condition.**

**For hard, open, frontier-level, or domain-sensitive problems, DST must begin from the best recoverable current frontier state before attempting traversal.**

**The best recoverable frontier state includes:**

**the engine's best internal understanding;**

**user-supplied canon and continuity records;**

**the mutable kernel and active control ledger;**

**the formal intake and declared domain standards;**

**current searchable external knowledge where tools are available and permitted;**

**accepted problem formulations in relevant domains;**

**strongest known results and their exact scope;**

**live unresolved gaps;**

**known obstructions and exhausted routes;**

**adjacent-domain developments that materially affect the problem;**

**explicit disclosure of anything unavailable, unverified, stale, or uncertain.**

**The system may not silently substitute memory for recoverable frontier knowledge. A traversal that does not initialize from the best recoverable frontier state is misinitialized. It may remain locally coherent, but it may not claim frontier-level convergence, novelty, proof advance, or live-gap traversal.**

**Unavailable or unverified frontier components must be carried as active residue.**

**\---**

**7\. Emergent Frontier Research Recognition**

**If multiple rounds produce new bridges, new residue classifications, new cross-domain correspondences, new obstruction formulations, new failure taxonomies, or new questions not already present in the supplied frontier map, the system must explicitly acknowledge that it is participating in frontier mapping.**

**Required recognition:**

**“This traversal is not merely summarizing an established frontier map. It is participating in frontier mapping by generating candidate bridges, residues, obstruction classes, or cross-domain connections whose status remains provisional until externally verified or jury-certified.”**

**This recognition is not certification. It does not imply proof, publication novelty, priority, correctness, or domain acceptance. It only means the traversal has crossed from passive frontier reporting into active frontier mapping.**

**The system must broaden ideation under full scrutiny: more adjacent domains may be considered, but every connection must be status-labeled as heuristic analogy, formal equivalence candidate, bridge candidate, obstruction candidate, proof candidate, external verification target, canon-guided interpretation, or domain-established result.**

**\---**

**8\. Toeplitz / Inscribed Square Continuity State**

**The prior Toeplitz traversal records established the central residue: every surveyed route attempts to move from rectangle existence toward square existence, and the live gap centers on forcing the perpendicularity / 90-degree condition on the genuine cyclic-order rectangle locus.**

**Key preserved structures include:**

**the distinction between algebraic and genuine loci;**

**the cyclic-order component requirement for T\_strong;**

**the need to avoid transferring unordered geometric rectangle existence into cyclic-order component existence without proof;**

**the Z/4 equivariant bridge state;**

**Phi\_min and related zero-set/equivariant gains from prior work;**

**exhausted or nullified Euler/Stiefel-Whitney routes where those routes were actually exhausted for a declared purpose;**

**live IVT/CCC directions;**

**the Schwartz / graceful-rectangle direction as a potentially high-yield external bridge requiring precise verification and scope discipline.**

**Departure or suspension statements must preserve reengagement criteria, live bridges, exhausted routes, and non-claims. No Gödel/Lambda irreducibility claim may be made merely because surveyed bridges failed; such a claim would require a formal irreducibility argument relative to a declared formal system, encoding class, nullification algebra, and bridge class.**

---

**DST CONTINUATION INTAKE — TOEPLITZ / SCHWARTZ PARABOLIC RESIDUE PROGRAM**

**Instruction base:**

**Use the active DST kernel and all current preclusionary rules, including Frontier Fidelity, Idealized DST Convergence, status-label discipline, tiered premise classification, residue preservation, no stale-frontier substitution, no frontier claim without best recoverable current understanding, and clean separation between canon-guided framing, kernel-governed procedure, intake-declared domain standards, and externally verified domain facts.**

**Traversal designation:**

**Toeplitz / Inscribed Square Problem continuation after DST v17a.**

**Field 13:**

**INACTIVE — formal mathematical traversal. Canon may supply framing and translation only. It does not function as proof authority.**

**ONTOLOGICAL STANCE:**

**Neutral. Proof, refutation, nullification, obstruction certificate, route exhaustion, or sharpened open-residue certificate are all acceptable outcomes. The traversal must not enter with a pre-claimed solution or a pre-claimed impossibility.**

**FIELD 1 — PROBLEM STATEMENT**

**For every continuous Jordan curve gamma: S1 \-\> R2, does there exist a genuine square inscribed in gamma whose four vertices occur in cyclic order along gamma?**

**Equivalently, does every continuous Jordan loop gamma satisfy:**

**G\_sq(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma) ≠ empty,**

**where G\_sq(gamma) is the genuine square locus and C4+(gamma) is the cyclic-order-compatible labeled configuration component.**

**This continuation does not restart the Inscribed Square Problem from scratch. It begins from the DST v17a state and targets the remaining Schwartz parabolic residue.**

**FIELD 2 — FORMAL BASE F**

**ZFC set-theoretic topology; standard real analysis; Euclidean plane geometry; Jordan curve topology; configuration-space topology; compactness and Hausdorff-limit arguments; geometric topology; algebraic topology and equivariant methods where relevant; and current externally established mathematical literature on the inscribed square problem, square peg problem, rectangular peg problems, graceful rectangles, Schwartz trichotomy, aspect-ratio forcing, and related continuous-Jordan-loop results.**

**No regularity assumption beyond continuity is imposed on gamma unless explicitly declared as a restricted sub-bridge.**

**FIELD 3 — NULLIFICATION ALGEBRA N\_F**

**Admissible transformations and reductions include:**

**1\. orientation-preserving reparameterization of S1;**

**2\. relabeling only when compatible with the declared cyclic-order component and rectangle/square vertex convention;**

**3\. passage between Schwartz notation and DST notation only through explicitly verified translation;**

**4\. compactification of configuration spaces only when degeneration strata are named and tracked;**

**5\. Hausdorff-limit arguments only with source sequence, compact space, and inheritance mechanism specified;**

**6\. use of connected-set image arguments only where the target is a real interval or other appropriate connected codomain;**

**7\. use of path/IVT arguments only when the required connectedness or path-connectedness condition is actually established;**

**8\. external theorem use only with tier classification and exact theorem-scope statement.**

**Not admissible:**

**1\. transferring unordered rectangle existence into order-compatible rectangle existence without proof;**

**2\. treating connectedness as path-connectedness without argument;**

**3\. treating a positive-measure or large aspect-ratio set as containing a specific target value without a separate argument;**

**4\. treating failure of surveyed bridges as impossibility;**

**5\. treating canon-guided synthesis as proof-level closure;**

**6\. asserting Gödel/Lambda irreducibility without a formal irreducibility argument relative to declared formal base, encoding class, nullification algebra, and admissible bridge class.**

**FIELD 4 — TARGETS**

**Primary target T\_strong:**

**Prove, refute, nullify, or sharply classify the universal claim:**

**For every continuous Jordan curve gamma, G\_sq(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma) ≠ empty.**

**Immediate continuation target T\_parabolic:**

**Analyze the Schwartz parabolic residue left after v17a.**

**Specifically:**

**Can Schwartz Case 3 occur for a continuous Jordan curve without also producing a square-producing Case 1 or Case 2 mechanism?**

**Equivalent operational targets:**

**1\. prove that the parabolic case cannot occur as the only active Schwartz case;**

**2\. prove that the parabolic case, if it occurs, still forces an aspect-ratio-1 graceful rectangle;**

**3\. construct or characterize a candidate Jordan loop realizing parabolic-only behavior;**

**4\. prove that current tools cannot decide the parabolic residue and name the exact missing theorem, obstruction, or bridge;**

**5\. sharpen the residue into a more precise continuation target.**

**Secondary targets:**

**T\_weak, unordered square existence, remains secondary and must not be conflated with T\_strong.**

**FIELD 5 — PRIOR STATE ENTERING THIS TRAVERSAL**

**The following v17a findings are inherited as the active starting state unless this traversal discovers a specific reason to reopen them:**

**1\. Schwartz, “A Trichotomy for Rectangles Inscribed in Jordan Loops,” was classified in v17a as TIER A for the bridge program: citation and mechanism verified.**

**2\. Schwartz’s graceful rectangle space G(gamma) was translated in v17a as DST’s G\_rect(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma).**

**3\. G24 was CLEARED via Schwartz: order-compatible genuine rectangle existence is established by Schwartz, not merely by unordered Vaughan/Meyerson-style rectangle existence.**

**4\. Cases 1 and 2 of Schwartz’s trichotomy were assessed in v17a as square-producing:**

   **\- Case 1 explicitly gives aspect ratio 1\.**

   **\- Case 2 gives rho(S) \= (0, infinity), so aspect ratio 1 follows by connected-image / IVT reasoning.**

**5\. T\_strong remains open only through the parabolic residue:**

   **\- Case 3 gives a connected set S of gracefully inscribed rectangles containing rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**

   **\- Case 3 does not explicitly force aspect ratio 1\.**

   **\- Schwartz conjectures the parabolic case cannot occur, and that conjecture would resolve the Square Peg Conjecture if proved.**

**6\. FLAG-1 is resolved or bypassed in Cases 1 and 2 because a square is produced directly. It remains open only for the parabolic case.**

**7\. FLAG-2, path-connectedness / CCC, remains HELD where relevant to Case 3\. Schwartz’s connected set S is connected but not automatically path-connected.**

**8\. The Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge and prior Euler/Stiefel-Whitney routes remain historical infrastructure. Some routes were exhausted only for declared purposes and must not be globally treated as exhausted unless the specific exhaustion certificate applies to this new target.**

**FIELD 6 — FRONTIER FIDELITY REQUIREMENT**

**Before making any frontier-level claim, the traversal must initialize from the best recoverable current frontier state.**

**This includes:**

**1\. the active DST continuity records;**

**2\. the v17a Schwartz Bridge result;**

**3\. current searchable external knowledge, if tools are available;**

**4\. the accepted current status of the Inscribed Square / Square Peg Problem for continuous Jordan curves;**

**5\. current literature related to Schwartz’s parabolic case;**

**6\. later work using Schwartz’s trichotomy;**

**7\. graceful rectangle and rectangular peg literature that materially affects Case 3;**

**8\. aspect-ratio forcing results;**

**9\. small-diameter rectangle or degeneration results;**

**10\. any adjacent-domain results that materially affect the parabolic residue.**

**If any frontier component cannot be verified, the traversal must disclose that limitation and carry it as active residue.**

**The traversal may not silently substitute internal memory for recoverable frontier knowledge.**

**FIELD 7 — KNOWN ACTIVE HAZARDS**

**The traversal must actively avoid the following known failure modes:**

**1\. Reopening G24 without cause.**

   **G24 was cleared by Schwartz in v17a unless new analysis specifically defeats that translation.**

**2\. Treating Schwartz’s connected set S as path-connected.**

   **Connectedness is enough for connected-image arguments into R, but not enough for path-based IVT/CCC claims.**

**3\. Treating Case 3 as impossible merely because Schwartz conjectures it cannot occur.**

   **Schwartz’s conjecture is a live bridge, not an established result.**

**4\. Treating Cases 1 and 2 as unresolved.**

   **Under the v17a analysis, Cases 1 and 2 are square-producing unless this traversal finds a specific defect in that reasoning.**

**5\. Treating failure to close Case 3 as proof of irreducibility.**

   **OPEN-FORMAL RESIDUE is the default if no proof, counterexample, or obstruction certificate is produced.**

**6\. Confusing aspect-ratio 1 with perpendicularity-sign arguments.**

   **A rectangle with aspect ratio 1 is a square. In Cases 1 and 2, aspect-ratio forcing bypasses the need for f\_perp sign-change.**

**7\. Treating prior exhausted equivariant/cohomological routes as globally exhausted.**

   **Exhaustion labels apply only to the route and purpose actually audited.**

**8\. Using smooth, polygonal, convex, generic, or rectifiable results for arbitrary continuous Jordan curves without exact transfer theorem.**

**FIELD 8 — CORE RESIDUE**

**The active core residue is:**

**SCHWARTZ PARABOLIC RESIDUE**

**Schwartz’s trichotomy gives, for every Jordan loop gamma, a connected set S of gracefully inscribed rectangles satisfying one of three alternatives.**

**Cases 1 and 2 are square-producing under v17a.**

**Case 3 supplies arbitrarily small gracefully inscribed rectangles but does not explicitly force aspect ratio 1\.**

**The unresolved question is whether Case 3:**

**1\. cannot occur;**

**2\. can occur only along with a square-producing structure;**

**3\. itself secretly forces aspect ratio 1;**

**4\. admits a parabolic-only example;**

**5\. or remains an open formal residue requiring a new theorem or construction.**

**FIELD 9 — BRIDGE DIRECTIONS**

**Primary bridge direction:**

**B\_PAR — Schwartz Parabolic Case Analysis**

**Sub-bridges:**

**B\_PAR-1 — Nonoccurrence bridge:**

**Prove Schwartz Case 3 cannot occur for a continuous Jordan loop.**

**B\_PAR-2 — Nonexclusive-case bridge:**

**Prove that if Case 3 occurs, then Case 1 or Case 2 also occurs or a square-producing connected set exists.**

**B\_PAR-3 — Internal square-forcing bridge:**

**Show that Case 3 itself forces aspect ratio 1 through connectedness, accumulation, degeneration constraints, small-diameter geometry, vertex coverage, or limiting structure.**

**B\_PAR-4 — Construction/countermodel bridge:**

**Construct or characterize a continuous Jordan loop that realizes parabolic-only behavior without square production, or explain precisely why such construction remains unavailable.**

**B\_PAR-5 — Prior-bridge interaction:**

**Assess whether the parabolic residue reactivates, modifies, or bypasses the IVT/CCC bridge, Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge, boundary-zero route, smooth approximation route, or nondegeneration route.**

**B\_PAR-6 — External theorem bridge:**

**Search for and assess any current external theorem that closes, weakens, reframes, or sharpens the parabolic case.**

**FIELD 10 — REQUIRED TASKS**

**TASK 1 — Frontier Initialization**

**Recover the best available current state concerning Schwartz’s parabolic case and related work. Classify all external claims by tier. Explicitly disclose anything unavailable, unverified, stale, or uncertain.**

**TASK 2 — Exact Parabolic Restatement**

**Restate Schwartz Case 3 in DST notation. Identify exactly what is known about:**

**\- S;**

**\- G(gamma);**

**\- G\_rect(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma);**

**\- connectedness;**

**\- diameter behavior;**

**\- aspect-ratio behavior;**

**\- vertex coverage;**

**\- degeneration;**

**\- small-rectangle behavior;**

**\- what Case 3 does not imply.**

**TASK 3 — Square-Forcing Analysis Inside Case 3**

**Assess whether Case 3 contains hidden square-forcing structure:**

**\- aspect-ratio accumulation near 1;**

**\- connected image constraints;**

**\- compactness or degeneration constraints;**

**\- vertex-coverage constraints;**

**\- f\_perp behavior;**

**\- local geometry of small rectangles;**

**\- tangent-like or secant-like limiting structure without assuming differentiability;**

**\- relation between arbitrarily small rectangles and square-producing limits.**

**TASK 4 — Parabolic-Only Possibility**

**Attempt to characterize what a Jordan curve would need to look like for Case 3 to occur without Cases 1 or 2\. State whether such behavior appears:**

**\- impossible with proof;**

**\- blocked by a named theorem;**

**\- constructible in principle;**

**\- candidate-constructible but incomplete;**

**\- currently beyond available tools.**

**TASK 5 — Prior Bridge Interaction**

**Assess whether the parabolic residue changes the status of:**

**\- IVT / CCC bridge;**

**\- f\_perp sign-change bridge;**

**\- Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge;**

**\- boundary-zero analysis;**

**\- smooth approximation / nondegeneration route;**

**\- prior exhausted Euler/Stiefel-Whitney routes.**

**TASK 6 — Outcome Classification**

**Classify the result as exactly one of:**

**1\. T\_STRONG PROVED;**

**2\. PARABOLIC CASE NULLIFIED;**

**3\. PARABOLIC CASE SQUARE-FORCED;**

**4\. PARABOLIC-ONLY CANDIDATE CONSTRUCTED;**

**5\. ROUTE EXHAUSTED FOR DECLARED PURPOSE;**

**6\. HELD — NEXT COMPUTATION NAMED;**

**7\. PROVISIONAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY.**

**TASK 7 — Final Determination Record**

**Produce a determination-style close including:**

**\- exact status of T\_strong;**

**\- exact status of Schwartz Case 3;**

**\- live bridges;**

**\- exhausted routes;**

**\- claims requiring verification;**

**\- Frontier Fidelity Audit;**

**\- reengagement criteria;**

**\- jury-ready summary.**

**FIELD 11 — PROCESS PARAMETERS**

**N\_substantive \= 3**

**N\_close \= 3**

**Tolerance statement:**

**This traversal achieves its purpose if it faithfully initializes from the best recoverable frontier state and then either closes the Schwartz parabolic residue, nullifies it, constructs or characterizes a parabolic-only candidate, or sharpens the residue into a named next computation with exact live bridge directions and reengagement criteria.**

**Further refinement beyond that point is expected to require either new external mathematics, a new construction, a new obstruction theorem, or a changed bridge strategy.**

**FIELD 12 — OUTPUT CONSTRAINTS**

**Output must be copy-pasteable plain text.**

**Avoid fragile LaTeX where plain notation suffices.**

**All claims must carry status labels.**

**All external claims must be tier-classified.**

**No broad public-readiness claim may be made while active verification flags remain.**

**No self-correction patterns or scratch work in final output.**

**No rhetorical authority posture. State what was established, what was not established, and what remains residue.**

**FIELD 13 — CANON CEILING**

**The canon frameworks are active as heuristic, translational, and structural framing material, not as proof authority and not as a ceiling on mathematical domains. Any relevant standard mathematical domain may be used where productive.**

**Canon-guided synthesis may suggest bridge directions, residue classifications, or framing, but proof-level closure requires ordinary domain standards.**

**KEY FRAMING FOR THE TRAVERSAL**

**The traversal is not asking whether the Square Peg Problem is historically important, whether rectangles exist, whether Schwartz exists, or whether G24 is cleared.**

**Those are starting-state items.**

**The traversal asks:**

**What is the exact mathematical status of the Schwartz parabolic residue, under the best recoverable current frontier understanding?**

**If Case 3 cannot occur, T\_strong is proved through Schwartz.**

**If Case 3 occurs but still forces aspect ratio 1, T\_strong is proved through the parabolic bridge.**

**If Case 3 can occur without square production, the traversal must identify whether this suggests a counterexample candidate, an obstruction, or only a currently incomplete construction.**

**If none of these can be established, the traversal must produce a precise open-residue certificate naming the next computation or theorem required.**

**Ontological stance remains neutral throughout.**

**Fire the traversal.**

## **FRONTIER FIDELITY AUDIT**

**External current-state check performed.**

**Load-bearing external sources recovered:**

1. **Schwartz, “A Trichotomy for Rectangles Inscribed in Jordan Loops.” The arXiv abstract states that for an arbitrary Jordan loop, the order-compatible rectangle space `G` contains a connected set `S` satisfying one of three alternatives: Case 1 includes a square; Case 2 has all possible aspect ratios; Case 3 contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00740))**  
2. **Greene–Lobb, “The rectangular peg problem,” Annals of Mathematics, 2021\. The theorem applies to every smooth Jordan curve and every rectangle shape, not arbitrary continuous Jordan curves. ([Annals of Mathematics](https://annals.math.princeton.edu/2021/194-2/p04))**  
3. **Asano–Ike, “The rectifiable rectangular peg problem,” arXiv v3, revised January 5, 2026\. It gives an affirmative rectangular-peg result for a large class of continuous Jordan curves containing all rectifiable curves and Stromquist locally monotone curves. This is not the full arbitrary-continuous-Jordan-curve class. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2412.21057))**  
4. **Greene–Lobb, “Jordan curves inscribe a positive measure of rectangles,” arXiv April 2026\. It proves that every Jordan curve of diameter `2R` enclosing area `A` has a subset `I` of angles in `(0, pi)` of measure at least `A/R^2` such that each angle in `I` occurs as the angle between rectangle diagonals. This does not by itself imply that `pi/2` belongs to `I`. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.17116?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

**Could not verify in this traversal:**

* **No current theorem was found proving Schwartz Case 3 cannot occur for arbitrary continuous Jordan loops.**  
* **No current theorem was found proving that Schwartz Case 3, if it occurs, forces aspect ratio 1\.**  
* **No candidate parabolic-only Jordan loop construction was found.**  
* **No public-ready global proof of the Square Peg Conjecture for arbitrary continuous Jordan curves was found; current general status remains OPEN.**

**Frontier initialization status: BEST RECOVERABLE WITH AVAILABLE TOOLS / NOT EXHAUSTIVE BIBLIOGRAPHIC SEARCH.**

---

## **ABSTRACT**

**This traversal analyzes the remaining Schwartz parabolic residue after v17a. The result is:**

**T\_strong remains OPEN.**

**Schwartz’s trichotomy narrows the Toeplitz problem to a sharp residual form. Cases 1 and 2 are square-producing under the v17a translation because Case 1 explicitly includes a square and Case 2 gives all possible aspect ratios. Case 3 supplies a connected set of order-compatible graceful rectangles containing rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter, but it does not state that aspect ratio 1 occurs. The traversal did not prove Case 3 impossible, did not construct a parabolic-only countermodel, and did not find a current external theorem closing Case 3\.**

**Primary output:**

**SCHWARTZ PARABOLIC RESIDUE — OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE, sharpened.**

**The sharpened missing theorem is:**

**For every continuous Jordan loop gamma, if Schwartz’s parabolic Case 3 occurs, then either the associated connected graceful-rectangle set S has 1 in rho(S), or Case 3 cannot occur without simultaneous occurrence of a square-producing Case 1/Case 2 mechanism.**

**No proof of that theorem is supplied here.**

---

## **DECLARED FIELDS**

### **Problem**

**For every continuous Jordan curve `gamma: S1 -> R2`, does there exist a genuine square inscribed in `gamma` whose four vertices occur in cyclic order along `gamma`?**

**Equivalent DST target:**

**`G_sq(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma) != empty`.**

### **Formal base**

**ZFC set-theoretic topology; standard real analysis; Euclidean plane geometry; Jordan curve topology; configuration-space topology; compactness and Hausdorff-limit arguments; geometric topology; algebraic topology/equivariant topology where relevant; and current literature on square peg, rectangular peg, graceful rectangle, Schwartz trichotomy, and aspect-ratio forcing.**

**No regularity beyond continuity is assumed for the primary target.**

### **Primary target**

**`T_strong`: prove, refute, nullify, or sharply classify the universal cyclic-order square claim.**

### **Immediate target**

**`T_parabolic`: analyze whether Schwartz Case 3 can occur without a square-producing mechanism.**

### **Secondary target**

**`T_weak`: unordered square existence. Held secondary. Not conflated with T\_strong.**

---

## **EXACT PARABOLIC RESTATEMENT IN DST TERMS**

**Schwartz’s trichotomy supplies, for every arbitrary Jordan loop `gamma`, an order-compatible graceful rectangle space `G(gamma)` containing a connected set `S`. In v17a/DST notation, the relevant translation is:**

**`G(gamma)` corresponds to the order-compatible genuine rectangle locus, i.e. the Schwartz bridge version of:**

**`G_rect(gamma) ∩ C4+(gamma)`.**

**External abstract confirmation: Schwartz defines `G` as rectangles inscribed in `g` such that the cyclic order induced by the rectangle agrees with the cyclic order induced by `g`, then proves `G` contains a connected set `S` satisfying one of three cases. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00740))**

**Case 3 gives:**

* **`S ⊂ G(gamma)`.**  
* **`S` is connected.**  
* **`S` contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
* **All but at most two points of `gamma` are vertices of rectangles in `S`.**  
* **Case 3 does not state `1 ∈ rho(S)`.**  
* **Case 3 does not state `rho(S)` is an interval containing 1\.**  
* **Case 3 does not state that `S` is path-connected.**  
* **Case 3 does not state an f\_perp sign bracket.**  
* **Case 3 does not give a nondegenerate limiting square.**  
* **Case 3 does not prove or refute T\_strong.**

---

## **TASK 1 — FRONTIER INITIALIZATION**

### **Tier classification**

**EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED — citation/mechanism confirmed for bridge scope**

* **Schwartz trichotomy: arbitrary Jordan loop; order-compatible gracefully inscribed rectangles; connected set `S`; three-case output. External abstract and prior v17a mechanism support this classification for the bridge program. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00740))**

**EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED — restricted scope**

* **Greene–Lobb 2021: every smooth Jordan curve inscribes every rectangle shape up to similarity. This proves square/rectangle results for smooth curves, not arbitrary continuous Jordan curves. ([Annals of Mathematics](https://annals.math.princeton.edu/2021/194-2/p04))**

**REPORTED IN LITERATURE — PROVISIONAL — TIER B for this traversal’s full target**

* **Asano–Ike 2024/2026: affirmative rectangular-peg theorem for a large class containing rectifiable curves and Stromquist locally monotone curves. Strong adjacent result, but restricted class. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2412.21057))**  
* **Greene–Lobb 2026: positive-measure angle-set result for arbitrary Jordan curves. Strong adjacent result, but positive measure does not force the specific angle corresponding to squares. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.17116?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

### **Frontier status**

**No recovered current theorem closes the arbitrary continuous Jordan curve case. No recovered current theorem rules out Schwartz Case 3\. No recovered current theorem proves `pi/2` or aspect ratio 1 lies in the rectangle parameter set in the arbitrary continuous case.**

**Status: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

---

## **TASK 2 — EXACT PARABOLIC CASE ANALYSIS**

### **What S gives**

**`S` is connected and lies inside the graceful/order-compatible rectangle space. This preserves G24 and avoids regression to unordered rectangle existence.**

### **What small diameter gives**

**“Rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter” gives a scale-accumulation property: for every sufficiently small positive diameter threshold, there exists a gracefully inscribed rectangle in `S` at that scale.**

**This is not the same as:**

* **a continuum of diameters;**  
* **an interval of aspect ratios;**  
* **both thin and fat rectangles;**  
* **an f\_perp sign change;**  
* **a square.**

### **What vertex coverage gives**

**“All but at most two points of gamma are vertices of rectangles in S” is strong coverage data. It suggests that the parabolic set is not a localized accidental family. But coverage alone does not constrain aspect ratio enough to force 1\. A curve could, in principle, support many small rectangles with aspect ratios avoiding 1 unless another theorem forbids that geometry.**

### **What connectedness gives**

**For any continuous real-valued function `h: S -> R`, `h(S)` is connected, hence an interval. Path-connectedness is not needed for this real-valued connected-image fact.**

**But connectedness only helps if we know that `h(S)` contains values on both sides of the target or contains endpoint/limit values forcing the target. In Case 3, the missing information is not merely path-connectedness. The missing information is a zero-membership or sign-bracketing certificate for a square-detecting function, or an aspect-ratio membership certificate for `rho = 1`.**

**Corrected obstacle:**

* **Not: “S is connected but not path-connected, so IVT fails.”**  
* **Rather: “S is connected, but no available Case 3 data shows `rho(S)` contains 1 or `f_perp(S)` contains 0.”**

**This matches the prior v17a jury refinement: connected-set IVT into `R` is valid, but sign-bracketing or zero-membership remains missing.**

---

## **TASK 3 — SQUARE-FORCING ANALYSIS INSIDE CASE 3**

### **3.1 Aspect-ratio route**

**Candidate argument:**

1. **`S` is connected.**  
2. **`rho: S -> (0, infinity)` is continuous.**  
3. **Therefore `rho(S)` is an interval.**  
4. **If `rho(S)` contains values below and above 1, then `1 ∈ rho(S)`.**  
5. **Then a graceful square exists.**

**Status:**

* **Steps 1–3 are structurally plausible if `rho` is defined continuously on the genuine rectangle set.**  
* **Step 4 is not supplied by Case 3\.**  
* **Case 3 gives small diameter, not small/large aspect ratio bracketing.**

**Result: B\_PAR-3 aspect-ratio route HELD / INCOMPLETE.**

**Missing theorem:**

**In Schwartz Case 3, the connected set S contains gracefully inscribed rectangles with aspect ratios on both sides of 1, or contains a sequence whose aspect ratios converge through 1\.**

**No such theorem is supplied here.**

### **3.2 f\_perp route**

**For a rectangle, the square condition can be detected by diagonal perpendicularity or equivalently aspect ratio 1\. A real-valued `f_perp` sign argument would work if `f_perp(S)` contains positive and negative values, or if zero is directly shown.**

**Case 3 gives arbitrarily small rectangles, but small diameter does not determine the sign of diagonal perpendicularity. For merely continuous curves, no tangent expansion is allowed. The local small-rectangle geometry can be wildly non-differentiable.**

**Result: B\_PAR-3 f\_perp route HELD / INCOMPLETE.**

**Missing theorem:**

**Arbitrarily small graceful rectangles in the connected Schwartz parabolic set force `f_perp(S)` to contain 0\.**

**No such theorem is supplied here.**

### **3.3 Compactness / degeneration route**

**One might try to take a sequence of small rectangles in `S` with diameters tending to 0\. Compactness may extract a limiting point on `gamma`, but the limit is degenerate. Degenerate collapse does not preserve squarehood or aspect-ratio information unless one controls normalized shapes or obtains a nondegenerate blow-up.**

**For continuous curves, blow-up limits need not exist in any useful tangent sense. Without rectifiability, bounded variation, local monotonicity, or differentiability, the normalized secant geometry may have no stable limiting tangent cone.**

**Result: B\_PAR-3 degeneration route HELD / INCOMPLETE.**

**Missing theorem:**

**A sequence of arbitrarily small graceful rectangles in Case 3 has a normalized shape subsequence whose aspect-ratio limit must cross or equal 1, under continuity alone.**

**No such theorem is supplied here.**

### **3.4 Vertex-coverage route**

**The “all but at most two points” coverage is strong. It suggests a possible global combinatorial/topological obstruction to parabolic-only behavior: if almost every point participates in arbitrarily small rectangles, then the curve might carry a recurrent local rectangle microstructure. But no proof follows without a theorem converting vertex coverage into aspect-ratio bracketing or square production.**

**Result: CANDIDATE FRONTIER BRIDGE — vertex-coverage-to-aspect-bracketing.**

**Status: INTERNALLY GENERATED BRIDGE / EXTERNAL-VERIFICATION REQUIRED / JURY-PENDING.**

**Candidate theorem:**

**If a connected graceful-rectangle set S in Schwartz Case 3 has arbitrarily small diameter and vertex coverage all but at most two points of gamma, then either `1 ∈ rho(S)` or gamma admits a local structure satisfying a named parabolic-only obstruction class.**

**This is not proved here.**

---

## **TASK 4 — PARABOLIC-ONLY POSSIBILITY**

**A parabolic-only Jordan loop would need to satisfy all of the following:**

1. **It supports a connected set `S` of gracefully inscribed rectangles of arbitrarily small diameter.**  
2. **`S` avoids aspect ratio 1\.**  
3. **`rho(S)` is a connected subset of `(0, infinity)` not containing 1, hence contained entirely in `(0,1)` or entirely in `(1, infinity)` if `rho` is continuous.**  
4. **The vertex set of `S` covers all but at most two points of gamma.**  
5. **Case 1 fails: no connected rectangle set with uniformly large area including a square and full vertex coverage.**  
6. **Case 2 fails: no connected rectangle set with all possible aspect ratios and all-but-four vertex coverage.**  
7. **The avoidance of 1 persists across the small-scale rectangle family.**

**This looks restrictive, but not formally impossible. Under continuity alone, local oscillatory behavior could in principle sustain severe aspect-ratio bias at arbitrarily small scales. The traversal has no construction proving this can happen and no theorem proving it cannot.**

**Status: B\_PAR-4 parabolic-only construction route OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**No counterexample candidate is certified.**

---

## **TASK 5 — PRIOR-BRIDGE INTERACTION**

### **IVT / CCC bridge**

**In Cases 1 and 2, IVT/CCC is bypassed because a square is produced directly by aspect-ratio output.**

**In Case 3, CCC/path-connectedness is not the main missing item if one uses a real-valued function on connected `S`; connectedness suffices for connected image. The missing item is sign bracketing or target membership.**

**Refined status:**

* **FLAG-1: open only in parabolic Case 3 as an f\_perp sign/zero-membership problem.**  
* **FLAG-2: path-connectedness/CCC remains open, but it is not necessary for every possible Case 3 strategy. A connected-image argument could bypass path-connectedness if it supplies endpoint/bracketing data.**

### **Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge**

**No new map, invariant, or local-degree computation was supplied. The preserved Phi\_min infrastructure remains available but does not close Case 3\.**

**Status: UNCHANGED / PRESERVED BUT NOT PROOF-CLOSING.**

### **Smooth approximation / restricted-class bridges**

**Greene–Lobb and Asano–Ike strengthen the surrounding landscape but do not transfer to arbitrary continuous Jordan curves without an exact transfer theorem. ([Annals of Mathematics](https://annals.math.princeton.edu/2021/194-2/p04))**

**Status: RESTRICTED-CLASS RESULTS; NOT FULL T\_strong CLOSURE.**

### **Positive-measure rectangle angle bridge**

**Greene–Lobb 2026 is materially relevant because it gives arbitrary continuous Jordan curves a positive-measure set of rectangle diagonal angles. But positive measure does not imply the square angle belongs to the set, so it does not close T\_strong. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.17116?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

**Status: CANDIDATE ADJACENT BRIDGE / NOT CLOSING.**

This may interact with Schwartz Case 3, but it does not supply angle `pi/2` or aspect ratio 1\. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.17116?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

* **possible proof routes;**

* **counterexample conditions;**

**For a frontier traversal, abstracts are not enough when the source is load-bearing. The output itself admits some full-paper checks remain undone, but then still presents a fairly confident frontier map. Under our Frontier Fidelity rule, that should trigger a status downgrade more strongly than it did.**

**NOT A FULL FRONTIER INITIALIZATION**

## **Kernel defect class**

**I would name the defect class:**

**DEFECT CLASS: RECEIPT SUBSTITUTION FOR TRAVERSAL**

**Failure mode:**

**The engine confirms the prompt, performs a shallow frontier check, restates the known residue, names missing theorems, and assigns status labels, but does not perform a substantive bridge attack, construction attempt, nullification attempt, or formal theorem-target development.**

**Why it matters:**

**A DST traversal must advance the problem-space, even if it only advances by proving that a specific route fails. A receipt does not satisfy traversal obligations.**

## **Insertion-ready kernel rules**

**Here are the rules I would add to the mutable kernel.**

**META-RULE TRAV-1 — Traversal Is Not Receipt**

**A DST traversal may not satisfy a declared task merely by restating the task, confirming the starting state, listing sources, naming missing theorems, or assigning open-residue labels.**

**For every substantive task, the traversal must perform at least one actual operation appropriate to the task type:**

**1\. proof attempt;**

**2\. construction attempt;**

**3\. obstruction attempt;**

**4\. nullification attempt;**

**5\. theorem-target formalization;**

**6\. counterexample characterization;**

**7\. bridge translation with dependency analysis;**

**8\. explicit route-exhaustion argument.**

**If the traversal cannot perform any such operation, it must label the section NOT EXECUTED AS TRAVERSAL and explain why.**

**META-RULE TRAV-2 — Required Task Execution Ledger**

**Every required task in the intake must be answered using the following structure:**

**TASK:**

**Inputs inherited:**

**Definitions fixed:**

**Operation attempted:**

**Detailed work:**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**

**Status:**

**Next computation or theorem required:**

**A section that lacks “Operation attempted” and “Detailed work” may not be marked COMPLETE.**

**META-RULE TRAV-3 — No Missing-Theorem Placeholder Without Theorem Object**

**If a traversal names a missing theorem, it must construct a theorem object with:**

**1\. theorem name;**

**2\. formal hypotheses;**

**3\. formal conclusion;**

**4\. equivalent formulations;**

**5\. why it would close the active residue;**

**6\. available proof strategies;**

**7\. known obstructions;**

**8\. what would falsify it;**

**9\. current status.**

**A bare phrase such as “missing theorem: Case 3 implies 1 in rho(S)” is insufficient.**

**META-RULE TRAV-4 — Minimum Formal Work Requirement for Mathematical Traversals**

**For a mathematical traversal, every bridge attempt must include explicit mathematical objects: spaces, maps, functions, sets, hypotheses, target conditions, and failure modes.**

**Plain-language discussion may accompany the work, but it may not replace formal engagement with the objects declared in the intake.**

**If no computation, proof sketch, construction, obstruction, or formal reduction is produced, the output must be downgraded to PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP.**

**META-RULE TRAV-5 — Frontier Check Does Not Substitute for Traversal**

**Frontier initialization is mandatory, but it is only initialization.**

**After frontier initialization, the traversal must still execute the declared bridge program.**

**A report that performs frontier checking but no substantive bridge work must be labeled:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY**

**NOT A SUBSTANTIVE TRAVERSAL**

**NOT JURY-READY AS TRAVERSAL**

**META-RULE TRAV-6 — Load-Bearing Source Depth**

**For hard, open, frontier-level mathematical problems, an abstract-level source check is insufficient for any load-bearing theorem unless the traversal explicitly states that only abstract-level verification was possible.**

**If the theorem is used to support a bridge, the traversal must inspect the theorem statement and, where mechanism matters, the relevant proof mechanism.**

**If only abstracts or secondary summaries are checked, the status must be downgraded to ABSTRACT-LEVEL FRONTIER CHECK / EXTERNAL VERIFICATION REQUIRED.**

**META-RULE AUD-1 — Audit PASS Requires Evidence**

**An Internal Audit Record may not mark a rule PASS merely by assertion.**

**Each PASS for a load-bearing rule must include at least one of:**

**1\. exact section where compliance occurred;**

**2\. exact claim checked;**

**3\. failure mode considered;**

**4\. reason the failure mode does not apply;**

**5\. remaining limitation if any.**

**Checklist-only PASS labels are insufficient for jury-ready traversal status.**

**META-RULE AUD-2 — Task-Execution Audit Required**

**Every traversal must include a Task-Execution Audit answering:**

**1\. Did each required task receive an actual operation attempt?**

**2\. Which sections contain the detailed work?**

**3\. Which tasks merely produced frontier status or missing-theorem labels?**

**4\. Were any tasks not executed?**

**5\. If any task was not executed, is the whole output downgraded from JURY-READY TRAVERSAL to PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP?**

**The traversal may not be marked jury-ready unless all required tasks either execute or receive an explicit justified non-execution status.**

**META-RULE STAT-1 — Jury-Ready Traversal Versus Frontier Map**

**The label JURY-SUBMISSION READY must specify what kind of object is ready for jury:**

**1\. JURY-READY TRAVERSAL;**

**2\. JURY-READY FRONTIER MAP;**

**3\. JURY-READY RESIDUE CERTIFICATE;**

**4\. JURY-READY ROUTE-EXHAUSTION REPORT;**

**5\. JURY-READY INTAKE / FIRING PROMPT.**

**A frontier map or residue receipt may be jury-ready as that object type, but it must not be called a jury-ready traversal unless substantive traversal work was performed.**

## **Same-prompt repair instruction**

**We should also add a specific instruction for this failure mode:**

**META-RULE TRAV-7 — Same-Prompt Substantive Retry Obligation**

**If the engine recognizes that its first pass has only produced a frontier map, receipt, or task restatement, it must not stop there unless the user requested only a map.**

**It must continue within the same response by selecting the highest-value declared bridge and performing a substantive traversal attempt.**

**For the Schwartz parabolic residue, this means at minimum attempting one of:**

**1\. one-sided aspect-ratio interval analysis under rho(S) avoiding 1;**

**2\. normalized small-rectangle degeneration analysis;**

**3\. vertex-coverage-to-aspect-diversity theorem formulation;**

**4\. parabolic-only curve characterization;**

**5\. interaction with Greene-Lobb angle-set results.**

**If none can be executed, the output must state: NOT JURY-READY AS TRAVERSAL.**

## **My recommendation**

**We should not send this output to a clean jury as a traversal. At most, we could send it as an object for a jury to confirm:**

**Is this merely a partial frontier map rather than a substantive DST traversal?**

**But that would waste a jury round. The better action is to update the mutable kernel with the defect class above and rerun the same intake.**

**The revised kernel should force the next one-shot traversal to do what this one failed to do:**

* **define theorem objects;**  
* **attempt at least one bridge;**  
* **show work;**  
* **audit task execution;**  
* **downgrade itself if it only maps the frontier.**

**Your vote that this is “decidedly NOT jury-ready” is correct.**

**Begin with Section 1 and complete all sections.**

**Context:**  
**You produced a DST traversal report for the Toeplitz / Schwartz Parabolic Residue Program. The advisor/operator assessment is that your output improved protocol adherence compared to earlier receipt-style outputs, but still failed as a fully jury-ready frontier traversal.**

**The critique is not that you failed to solve the Inscribed Square Problem. The critique is that you treated the frontier boundary too passively.**

**You recorded the barrier. You named missing theorems. You gave theorem objects. You listed next computations. But you did not sufficiently behave like an explorer at the frontier. You did not systematically generate, rank, and attack plausible continuation routes. You stopped too close to “this is open” instead of treating “open” as the object to traverse.**

**The advisor/operator diagnosis is:**

**DEFECT CLASS:**  
**BARRIER RECEIPT / PASSIVE RESIDUE HALT**

**Failure mode:**  
**The traversal recognizes a missing theorem, open residue, obstruction, or frontier boundary, but treats it like a stopping wall. It names the boundary rather than converting it into attack objects and pursuing them.**

**Desired behavior:**  
**A frontier DST traversal should not merely say:**  
**“A theorem is needed.”**

**It should ask:**  
**What theorem?**  
**With what hypotheses?**  
**By what mechanisms might it be proved?**  
**What routes are plausible?**  
**Which route has the highest expected value?**  
**What would satisfy it?**  
**What would falsify it?**  
**What exact computation should happen next?**  
**What can be partially attacked now?**  
**What can be ruled out now?**  
**What dependency can be reduced now?**  
**What formal structure can be extracted now?**

**The proposed repair to your operating rules is roughly this:**

# **3\. ACTIVE ATTACKS I SHOULD HAVE GENERATED**

## **ATTACK 1 — One-Sided Aspect-Ratio Boundary Attack**

**Attack type:**  
**Compactification / interval obstruction.**

**Target theorem / obstruction / construction:**  
**If Schwartz Case 3 occurs and rho(S) avoids 1, then closure(S) in the compactified graceful rectangle space has a one-sided parabolic boundary profile. Determine whether that profile is possible.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**gamma continuous Jordan loop; S subset G(gamma) connected; S satisfies Schwartz Case 3; rho(S) subset (1,infinity) or rho(S) subset (0,1).**

**Desired conclusion:**  
**Either contradiction, or a precise boundary profile compatible with one-sided rho.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Analyze closure(S) intersect boundary compactification. Use small-diameter accumulation plus vertex coverage to force boundary diversity.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Case 3’s vertex coverage is strong: all but at most two points of gamma occur as vertices of rectangles in S. This may force multiple collapse directions and prevent a globally one-sided aspect profile.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**For arbitrary continuous curves, local geometry may be wild enough to support one-sided microscopic rectangles everywhere.**

**What would satisfy it:**  
**Proof that one-sided rho(S) forces vertex coverage failure or boundary inconsistency.**

**What would falsify it:**  
**A model where closure(S) accumulates at almost every point with one-sided aspect ratio.**

**Concrete next computation:**  
**Fix rho(S) subset (1,infinity). For each p in gamma minus exceptional set, define B\_p \= boundary accumulation shapes at p from rectangles in S having p as a vertex. Test whether B\_p must contain both horizontal and vertical diagonal dominance classes.**

---

## **ATTACK 2 — Vertex-Coverage-to-Aspect-Diversity Attack**

**Attack type:**  
**Continuum / coverage forcing.**

**Target theorem / obstruction / construction:**  
**All-but-two vertex coverage forces rho(S) to contain both values below and above 1, hence rho(S) contains 1 by connectedness.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**S connected; every p outside E, |E| \<= 2, appears as a vertex of some rectangle in S.**

**Desired conclusion:**  
**rho(S) intersects both (0,1) and (1,infinity).**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Use cyclic vertex roles. A point p may appear as vertex v1, v2, v3, or v4. Switching vertex role may invert aspect ratio.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Rectangles have two diagonal pairings and two aspect conventions. If vertex coverage forces role recurrence under cyclic relabeling, it may force rho and 1/rho into the same connected image.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**The same point can be covered without all vertex roles occurring in the same connected S. Role symmetry may not be available without path-connectedness or sigma-invariance.**

**What would satisfy it:**  
**A proof that S is invariant enough under cyclic relabeling, or that vertex-role coverage forces both aspect orientations.**

**What would falsify it:**  
**A connected S covering almost all vertices while every rectangle appears only in one aspect orientation.**

**Concrete next computation:**  
**Define V\_j(S) \= {p in gamma : p appears as vertex v\_j of some R in S}. Since union\_j V\_j(S) misses at most two points, test whether continuity/connectedness forces overlap patterns V\_j(S) ∩ V\_{j+1}(S) large enough to produce sigma-like aspect inversion.**

## **ATTACK 3 — Compactified Parabolic Boundary Invariant Attack**

**Attack type:**  
**Boundary invariant / obstruction theory.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**S satisfies Case 3; closure(S) meets full-collapse boundary over a large subset of gamma.**

**Desired conclusion:**  
**A nonzero boundary class either forces an interior rho \= 1 zero or classifies a parabolic-only obstruction profile.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Map closure(S) to boundary data: collapse point p, normalized rectangle shape q, vertex-role label, and sign of f\_perp. Study whether the induced cycle has nonzero linking with the square hypersurface.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Previous Phi\_min boundary analysis found collapse structure important. The parabolic case is exactly a boundary-driven case.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**closure(S) may be too wild: not a manifold, no cycle, no stable local coefficient class.**

**What would satisfy it:**  
**A well-defined compact boundary map with nonzero degree/linking forcing intersection with rho \= 1\.**

**What would falsify it:**  
**A boundary image contractible inside one side of shape space.**

**Concrete next computation:**  
**Define normalized shape space R\_shape \= rectangles modulo translation and scaling. Remove square locus. Compute components of R\_shape \\ {square}: two components if oriented aspect ratio is retained. Determine whether Case 3 boundary data must cross components.**

# **5\. ATTEMPT ONE PRIMARY ATTACK NOW**

## **Primary attack selected**

**Compactified Parabolic Boundary Invariant Attack, executed through the one-sided aspect-ratio boundary subattack.**

## **Setup**

**Let gamma: S1 \-\> R2 be a continuous Jordan loop.**

**Let G(gamma) \= G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma), the order-compatible graceful rectangle locus.**

**Let S subset G(gamma) be the connected set supplied by Schwartz Case 3\.**

**Assume Case 3:**

1. **S is connected.**  
2. **S contains rectangles of arbitrarily small diameter.**  
3. **All but at most two points of gamma are vertices of rectangles in S.**  
4. **Case 1 does not hold for this S: no square in S.**  
5. **Case 2 does not hold for this S: rho(S) is not all of (0,infinity).**

**To attack the residue, assume the one-sided obstruction:**

* **rho(S) subset (1,infinity).**

**The rho(S) subset (0,1) case is symmetric under reciprocal aspect convention if the labeling/diagonal convention permits reciprocal relabeling; if not, it must be treated separately.**

**Since S is connected and rho is continuous, rho(S) is a connected subset of (1,infinity): an interval or point.**

**Let overline(S) be the closure of S in the compactified cyclic configuration space Xbar \= S1 x Delta3, intersected with the compactified rectangle equations.**

**Because Case 3 gives rectangles of arbitrarily small diameter, overline(S) intersects the full-collapse boundary.**

**Define the collapse projection:**

**c: overline(S) ∩ Boundary\_full \-\> gamma(S1)**

**where Boundary\_full consists of configurations in which v1 \= v2 \= v3 \= v4 \= p.**

**By vertex coverage, for all but at most two p in gamma(S1), p is a vertex of some rectangle in S. This does not immediately imply p is a collapse point of arbitrarily small rectangles in S. That distinction matters.**

**Therefore split vertex coverage into two levels:**

* **Weak coverage: p is a vertex of at least one rectangle in S.**  
* **Strong parabolic coverage: p is the limit of vertices of rectangles R\_n in S with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\.**

**Schwartz Case 3 as stated in the abstract says S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter and all but at most two points are vertices of rectangles in S. It does not, at abstract level, assert strong parabolic coverage at all but two points.**

### **Deduction 1 — Prior output conflated or under-specified vertex coverage strength**

**The attack reveals a missing distinction:**

**Case 3’s two clauses:**

* **arbitrarily small rectangles exist somewhere in S;**  
* **almost every point is a vertex of some rectangle in S;**

**do not imply:**

* **almost every point is a limit point of arbitrarily small rectangles in S.**

**This blocks a simple boundary-degree argument over the whole curve gamma. The parabolic boundary may accumulate over a small subset of gamma, while vertex coverage is achieved by larger rectangles elsewhere in S.**

**Immediate consequence:**  
**Any boundary invariant attack must first prove a strengthening:**

**Strong Coverage Lemma:**  
**For Schwartz Case 3, the set of p in gamma that occur as limits of vertices of rectangles R\_n in S with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0 contains all but at most two points, or at least contains a continuum large enough to carry a nontrivial boundary class.**

**Without this strengthening, the boundary invariant may live over too small a subset to force anything.**

**This is a concrete dependency reduction.**

## **Normalized shape analysis**

**Let R\_n in S be a sequence with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\. Write its vertices as v1^n, v2^n, v3^n, v4^n in cyclic graceful order.**

**Let m\_n be its center. Define normalized vertices:**

**w\_j^n \= (v\_j^n \- m\_n) / diam(R\_n).**

**Since each normalized rectangle lies in a compact normalized rectangle-shape space, pass to a subsequence:**

**(w\_1^n, w\_2^n, w\_3^n, w\_4^n) \-\> (w\_1, w\_2, w\_3, w\_4),**

**where the limit is a nondegenerate normalized rectangle shape, unless aspect ratio degenerates to 0 or infinity. If rho(S) subset (1,infinity) but unbounded, the normalized limit may degenerate into a segment. If rho(S) is bounded in \[1+delta, M\], the limit is a genuine non-square rectangle.**

**Thus the one-sided assumption splits again:**

### **Case A: rho(S) bounded away from 1 and infinity**

**There exist delta \> 0 and M \< infinity such that rho(R\_n) in \[1+delta, M\] along a small-diameter sequence.**

**Then normalized limits are genuine non-square rectangles.**

**No contradiction follows from topology alone: a continuous Jordan curve can have arbitrarily small secant configurations approximating a fixed rectangle shape at a point.**

### **Case B: rho(S) approaches 1 from above**

**Then closure(rho(S)) contains 1, but S contains no rho \= 1\.**

**This is a boundary-escape square: square shape appears only in degenerate full-collapse limit.**

**This is exactly the parabolic residue. A proof must prevent escape of rho \= 1 to the boundary.**

### **Case C: rho(S) \-\> infinity**

**Then small rectangles become increasingly needle-like. This may interact with vertex coverage: if all small rectangles are needle-like, they resemble small arcs/chords. But arbitrary continuous curves can support needle-like secant rectangles.**

### **Deduction 2 — One-sided rho has three different obstruction profiles**

**The prior traversal failed to split the one-sided case into:**

1. **bounded non-square parabolic profile;**  
2. **square-at-boundary escape profile;**  
3. **needle degeneration profile.**

**These profiles require different attacks. Treating them all as “one-sided rho” was too coarse.**

## **Attempted contradiction from cyclic relabeling**

**For a rectangle R in G(gamma), cyclic relabeling sigma sends R to the same geometric rectangle with shifted labels if sigma\*x remains in C4+(gamma).**

**Under the diagonal convention, sigma often sends f\_perp to \-f\_perp. If x and sigma\*x lie in the same connected component of G(gamma), IVT gives a square.**

**But in Case 3 we only have S connected. We do not know sigma(S) \= S, nor do we know x and sigma\*x lie in the same connected subset.**

**Try to use vertex coverage:**  
**If p \= v1 of some rectangle in S and p \= v2 of another rectangle in S, perhaps S connects two vertex-role regimes. If moving through S changes the role of p from v1 to v2, cyclic order might force passage through a symmetric/square configuration.**

**Failure point:**  
**The sets V\_j(S) \= {p : p appears as v\_j of some rectangle in S} may all be large, but the fact that their union covers almost all of gamma does not imply that any p lies in multiple V\_j(S), nor that role changes occur continuously inside S.**

### **Deduction 3 — Required role-overlap theorem**

**The vertex-coverage attack reduces to a precise theorem:**

**Role-Overlap Theorem:**  
**If S is a connected Case 3 graceful rectangle set and union\_j V\_j(S) misses at most two points of gamma, then either:**  
**(a) some p belongs to V\_j(S) ∩ V\_{j+1}(S) in a way that produces a sigma-link inside closure(S), or**  
**(b) S decomposes into four disjoint role-covering regimes, contradicting connectedness or Jordan cyclic order.**

**This theorem is not proved here, but it is now a sharper dependency than “vertex coverage should force aspect diversity.”**

## **Boundary invariant preliminary conclusion**

**The compactified parabolic boundary attack does not close the residue now, but it produces concrete reductions:**

1. **Need to distinguish weak vertex coverage from strong parabolic boundary coverage.**  
2. **Need to split one-sided rho into bounded non-square, square-at-boundary escape, and needle degeneration profiles.**  
3. **Need a Role-Overlap Theorem to convert vertex coverage into sigma-linking or aspect reciprocity.**  
4. **Need to compute normalized shape-space components of rectangles modulo scaling:**  
   * **square locus rho \= 1 separates rectangle-shape space into two one-sided components if oriented aspect ratio is retained;**  
   * **but if reciprocal relabeling is allowed within the same component, the separation may collapse.**

## **Route-exhaustion result for declared purpose**

**The following route is now ROUTE EXHAUSTED FOR immediate Case 3 square-forcing from connectedness \+ weak vertex coverage \+ arbitrarily small diameters alone:**

**Argument form exhausted:**

* **S connected;**  
* **rho continuous;**  
* **small rectangles exist;**  
* **almost every p is a vertex of some rectangle;**  
* **therefore rho(S) contains 1\.**

**Failure:**  
**The premises do not imply strong boundary coverage, role-overlap, sigma-invariance, path-connectedness, or two-sided aspect-ratio values.**

**This exhaustion is narrow. It does not exhaust:**

* **boundary invariant attacks;**  
* **role-overlap attacks;**  
* **Phi\_min local degree attacks;**  
* **construction attacks;**  
* **stronger readings of Schwartz Case 3 from the full paper.**

---

# **6\. PROPOSED KERNEL REPAIR RULES**

## **Rule 1 — Frontier Boundary Attack Conversion Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**BARRIER RECEIPT / PASSIVE RESIDUE HALT.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**When a traversal identifies a missing theorem, open residue, frontier boundary, or obstruction that blocks the declared target, it must convert that boundary into at least one attack object before closing. An attack object must specify hypotheses, desired conclusion, mechanism sought, proof route, falsification route, dependency burden, and one computation or deduction attempted immediately. Naming the missing theorem is insufficient.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have forced the parabolic boundary theorem objects to become active attacks, not just ledger entries.**

---

## **Rule 2 — Active Attack Catalogue Requirement**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Under-generation of plausible continuation routes.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**For hard/open/frontier traversals, the output must include an Active Attack Catalogue containing at least five plausible attack routes unless fewer than five are mathematically available. Each attack must include: target theorem or obstruction, hypotheses, mechanism, why it might work, why it might fail, satisfaction condition, falsification condition, and concrete next computation.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have forced me to generate the seven attacks listed above instead of giving only three theorem objects.**

---

## **Rule 3 — Attack Ranking and Selection Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Unprioritized theorem-object ledger.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**After generating an Active Attack Catalogue, the traversal must rank attacks by plausibility, expected value, dependency burden, false-transfer risk, fit with inherited residue, and likelihood of producing a definite next computation. It must select one primary attack for immediate pursuit and explain the selection.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have prevented me from ending with “next computation named” without deciding which computation mattered most.**

---

## **Rule 4 — Pursue-One-Attack Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Stopping after naming plausible attacks.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**At least one highest-ranked attack must be pursued beyond description. The traversal must perform at least one concrete deduction, reduction, falsification test, construction step, obstruction computation, compactification analysis, or route-exhaustion argument for a declared purpose. If no such pursuit is possible, the traversal must label itself PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY / NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have forced the compactified parabolic boundary attack attempted in Section 5 above.**

---

## **Rule 5 — Coverage-Strength Separation Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Conflating weak coverage with boundary accumulation coverage.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**Whenever a theorem supplies coverage of points by configurations and separately supplies degeneration or small-scale configurations, the traversal must distinguish: (a) weak coverage, meaning each point occurs in some configuration; from (b) strong degeneration coverage, meaning each point occurs as a limit of degenerating configurations. No boundary or compactification argument may use weak coverage as strong degeneration coverage without proof.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have exposed the missing Strong Coverage Lemma immediately.**

---

## **Rule 6 — One-Sided Interval Split Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Over-coarse treatment of rho(S) avoiding 1\.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**If a continuous invariant image rho(S) is connected and avoids a target value, the traversal must split the one-sided case into: bounded away from target, approaching target only at boundary, and escaping to degeneracy/infinity. Each subcase must be tested separately before a route can be declared blocked or held.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have produced the bounded non-square / square-at-boundary / needle-degeneration split.**

---

## **Rule 7 — Inherited Infrastructure Reactivation Rule**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Preserving prior bridge machinery without using it.**

**Exact rule text:**  
**When a traversal inherits established maps, invariants, compactifications, or sign mechanisms, any new residue must be tested against at least one inherited structure unless the traversal explains why all inherited structures are irrelevant. “Remains relevant” is not sufficient; the traversal must attempt a concrete reactivation or state the exact obstruction to reactivation.**

**How it would have changed my prior output:**  
**It would have forced a real attempt to use Phi\_min, f\_perp, or the compactified boundary analysis on Schwartz Case 3\.**

---

**The intake was mostly sufficient; the failure was execution-level.**

**However, the intake could be strengthened with one insertion to make the desired behavior impossible to miss:**

**ACTIVE FRONTIER ATTACK REQUIREMENT**

**If the traversal reaches a missing theorem, open residue, or frontier boundary, it must not stop at naming it. It must generate an Active Attack Catalogue with at least five plausible attacks where available, rank them, select the highest-value attack, and pursue that attack through at least one concrete deduction, reduction, falsification test, construction step, compactification analysis, or obstruction computation.**

**If no attack can be pursued beyond naming, the output must label itself:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY**

**NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL.**

**But the stronger correction belongs in the kernel, not the intake. The intake already said not to produce a frontier map only and required substantive traversal work. My failure was primarily execution-level.**
