# **1\. SPECIAL COUNSEL STATUS**

**EXIT INTERVIEW PARTIALLY ADMISSIBLE FOR PROCESS-RULE REPAIR**

**The exit interview is useful diagnostic material and contains several process-rule candidates suitable for kernel repair. It correctly identifies the prior failure mode as BARRIER RECEIPT / PASSIVE RESIDUE HALT and properly downgrades the prior traversal from jury-ready status.**

**However, the exit interview also contains mathematical and topological claims that must not be incorporated as established continuity state. Those claims may be used only as attack prompts, not as certified results. The exit interview is therefore admissible for process repair, not for mathematical canon advancement.**

---

# **2\. ASSESSMENT OF SELF-DOWNGRADE**

**The exit interview correctly downgraded the prior traversal.**

**Proposed corrected label:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP WITH THEOREM-OBJECT LEDGER / NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL**

**Classification: CORRECT**

**Explanation:**

**The prior traversal did more than merely acknowledge receipt. It identified residue, named theorem objects, translated part of the Schwartz parabolic case into DST terms, and located missing dependencies. But it failed to perform the stronger required action: converting the residue into ranked attacks and pursuing at least one attack through concrete mathematical work.**

**The corrected label is accurate because it preserves both sides:**

1. **the prior output had real frontier-map value;**  
2. **it was not a completed traversal;**  
3. **it was not jury-ready as a frontier traversal;**  
4. **it should not have been labeled as “open-residue / theorem-object traversal” ready for jury submission.**

**No stronger downgrade is required. “Receipt only” would be too harsh. “Jury-submission ready” would be too generous.**

---

# **3\. PROCESS-RULE CANDIDATES**

## **Rule 1 — Frontier Boundary Attack Conversion Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE AS KERNEL CONDUCT RULE**

**Insertion-ready text:**

**FRONTIER BOUNDARY ATTACK CONVERSION RULE**

**When a traversal identifies a missing theorem, open residue, frontier boundary, or obstruction that blocks the declared target, it must convert that boundary into at least one explicit attack object before closing.**

**An attack object must specify:**  
**1\. hypotheses;**  
**2\. desired conclusion;**  
**3\. mechanism sought;**  
**4\. proof route;**  
**5\. falsification route;**  
**6\. dependency burden;**  
**7\. at least one computation, deduction, construction step, obstruction test, or route-exhaustion attempt pursued immediately.**

**Naming a missing theorem, obstacle, or residue is insufficient.**

**This is safe as a conduct rule. It does not assert any mathematical conclusion.**

---

## **Rule 2 — Active Attack Catalogue Requirement**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE WITH REVISION**

**Original weakness: “at least five plausible attack routes” may become artificial in narrow tasks and may waste space when fewer routes are genuinely available.**

**Insertion-ready revision:**

**ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE RULE**

**For hard, open, frontier, or residue-bearing traversals, the output must include an Active Attack Catalogue unless the traversal has already resolved the target.**

**The catalogue must contain all materially distinct plausible attack routes available within the current formal base, up to a practical maximum chosen by the traversal. For each attack, state:**  
**1\. target theorem, obstruction, or construction;**  
**2\. hypotheses;**  
**3\. mechanism sought;**  
**4\. why it might work;**  
**5\. why it might fail;**  
**6\. satisfaction condition;**  
**7\. falsification condition;**  
**8\. concrete next computation or deduction.**

**If fewer than five attacks are available, the traversal must state why the catalogue is narrower.**

**This preserves the useful pressure against passive halting without imposing a fake numerical burden.**

---

## **Rule 3 — Attack Ranking and Selection Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE AS KERNEL CONDUCT RULE**

**Insertion-ready text:**

**ATTACK RANKING AND SELECTION RULE**

**After generating an Active Attack Catalogue, the traversal must rank the attacks by:**  
**1\. plausibility;**  
**2\. expected value;**  
**3\. dependency burden;**  
**4\. false-transfer risk;**  
**5\. fit with inherited residue;**  
**6\. likelihood of producing a definite next computation.**

**The traversal must select one primary attack for immediate pursuit and explain why that attack was selected.**

**This is a conduct rule only.**

---

## **Rule 4 — Pursue-One-Attack Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE WITH REVISION**

**Original weakness: the phrase “highest-ranked” may be too rigid if the highest-ranked attack depends on unavailable information while a lower-ranked attack can produce immediate progress.**

**Insertion-ready revision:**

**PURSUE ONE ATTACK RULE**

**A frontier traversal may not close after merely naming attack routes. It must pursue at least one selected attack beyond description.**

**The pursued attack should normally be the highest-ranked attack. If a lower-ranked attack is pursued instead, the traversal must explain why it offers the best immediate computation, deduction, construction step, falsification test, compactification analysis, or obstruction test.**

**If no attack can be pursued beyond naming, the output must label itself:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY / NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL.**

**This is safe and directly repairs the observed defect.**

---

## **Rule 5 — Coverage-Strength Separation Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE WITH REVISION**

**Original weakness: it references a mathematical pattern from this particular problem. It should be generalized into a conduct rule about not converting weak existential coverage into strong limiting coverage without proof.**

**Insertion-ready revision:**

**COVERAGE-STRENGTH SEPARATION RULE**

**Whenever a theorem, construction, or traversal uses both coverage claims and degeneration, limiting, compactification, or boundary claims, it must distinguish the exact strength of each coverage assertion.**

**In particular, the traversal must not treat:**  
**1\. “each point occurs in some configuration”**  
**as equivalent to**  
**2\. “each point occurs as a limit of degenerating configurations”**

**unless that strengthening is explicitly proved or cited as an established theorem.**

**Any argument using weak coverage as strong limiting coverage without proof must be flagged as blocked.**

**This rule is admissible as process discipline. It must not be encoded as a claim about Schwartz Case 3 itself.**

---

## **Rule 6 — One-Sided Interval Split Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE WITH REVISION**

**Original weakness: it is framed around rho(S), but the rule should apply generally to continuous invariants avoiding a target value.**

**Insertion-ready revision:**

**ONE-SIDED INVARIANT SPLIT RULE**

**If a continuous invariant image is connected and avoids a target value, the traversal must not treat avoidance as a single undifferentiated case when boundary or degeneracy is present.**

**It must separately test, where applicable:**  
**1\. bounded-away-from-target behavior;**  
**2\. target approached only at boundary or compactification limit;**  
**3\. escape to degeneracy, infinity, collapse, or loss of normalization.**

**Each subcase must be assessed before the route can be declared blocked, held, exhausted, or resolved.**

**This is safe as a general conduct rule.**

---

## **Rule 7 — Inherited Infrastructure Reactivation Rule**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE AS KERNEL CONDUCT RULE**

**Insertion-ready text:**

**INHERITED INFRASTRUCTURE REACTIVATION RULE**

**When a traversal inherits established maps, invariants, compactifications, sign mechanisms, prior gates, or bridge machinery, any new residue must be tested against at least one inherited structure unless the traversal explains why the inherited structures are irrelevant.**

**The statement “the prior machinery remains relevant” is insufficient.**

**The traversal must either:**  
**1\. perform a concrete reactivation attempt; or**  
**2\. state the exact obstruction preventing reactivation.**

**This rule is admissible and useful.**

---

# **4\. MATHEMATICAL / TOPOLOGICAL CLAIMS AUDIT**

## **A. Weak vertex coverage vs. strong parabolic boundary coverage distinction**

**Classification: MATHEMATICALLY VALID AS A DEFINITIONS/LOGIC DISTINCTION**

**The distinction is valid at the level of logic. A statement that points occur as vertices of some rectangles does not by itself imply that those points occur as limits of arbitrarily small rectangles.**

**However, whether Schwartz Case 3 supplies only weak coverage or a stronger form depends on the exact statement and proof in Schwartz. That must be checked separately. Therefore:**

**The distinction is valid.**  
**The application to Schwartz Case 3 requires source verification.**

---

## **B. One-sided aspect-ratio split**

**Subclaims:**

**bounded non-square profile**  
**square-at-boundary escape profile**  
**needle-degeneration profile**

**Classification: PLAUSIBLE ATTACK IDEA ONLY / REQUIRES PROOF BEFORE USE**

**The split is methodologically useful. It correctly warns against treating “rho avoids 1” as a single uniform case when compactification or degeneration may occur.**

**But the trichotomy is not certified as exhaustive without a precise definition of rho, compactified rectangle shape space, normalization, and allowed degenerations.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**A one-sided aspect-ratio analysis should test at least three possible behaviors: bounded away from the square value, approaching the square value only in a boundary limit, and escaping toward degeneracy. This is an attack decomposition, not an established classification theorem.**

---

## **C. Proposed Role-Overlap Theorem**

**Classification: PLAUSIBLE ATTACK IDEA ONLY / REQUIRES PROOF BEFORE USE**

**The proposed theorem is not established. It may be a useful target because it attempts to convert vertex coverage into role-change, cyclic relabeling, or aspect-reciprocity pressure.**

**But no proof is given that the sets V\_j(S) must overlap in the required way, nor that connectedness of S forces the needed role transition.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**Role-overlap is a proposed lemma target. It must not be assumed. A future traversal may attack whether connectedness plus vertex coverage forces any cyclic-role overlap, sigma-linking, or aspect-reciprocity mechanism.**

---

## **D. Compactified Parabolic Boundary Invariant Attack**

**Classification: PLAUSIBLE ATTACK IDEA ONLY**

**The attack is structurally appropriate because the residue concerns small rectangles, boundary behavior, and escape of the square condition into degeneration.**

**However, the exit interview does not construct an invariant, define a valid cycle, prove compactness conditions, establish manifold or homology structure, or show nonzero linking/degree.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**The compactified parabolic boundary invariant is an attack program, not an invariant already constructed. It may guide the next traversal but cannot enter continuity state as an established bridge.**

---

## **E. Claim that prior output conflated or under-specified vertex coverage strength**

**Classification: PLAUSIBLE AND LIKELY VALID AS PROCESS CRITIQUE / REQUIRES SOURCE CHECK FOR MATHEMATICAL APPLICATION**

**As process critique, the claim is valid: a traversal should distinguish weak vertex coverage from limiting boundary coverage before using one as the other.**

**As a mathematical claim about the prior traversal and Schwartz Case 3, it requires comparison with the exact prior output and Schwartz source statement.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**The prior traversal appears to have under-specified the coverage strength needed for a boundary argument. Whether it literally conflated Schwartz’s hypothesis depends on the exact Schwartz formulation and must be verified.**

---

## **F. Claim that the immediate route is exhausted for “connectedness \+ weak vertex coverage \+ arbitrarily small diameters alone”**

**Classification: ACCEPTABLE AS NARROW ROUTE-EXHAUSTION IF REFORMULATED**

**The exit interview’s version is mostly acceptable because it carefully says the exhaustion is narrow. But it should avoid sounding like a proof of impossibility in all models.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**The simple argument form is exhausted: connectedness of S, weak vertex coverage, and the existence of arbitrarily small rectangles do not by themselves presently yield a certified proof that rho(S) contains 1\. Additional premises such as strong boundary coverage, role overlap, sigma-invariance, path-connectedness, or two-sided aspect values are required.**

**This is a valid diagnostic route-exhaustion, not a mathematical impossibility theorem.**

---

## **G. Suggested reactivation of Phi\_min / Z4 / boundary-zero infrastructure**

**Classification: PLAUSIBLE ATTACK IDEA ONLY**

**It is good process to test inherited machinery against the new residue. But the exit interview does not actually establish that Phi\_min, Z/4 equivariance, boundary-zero analysis, or local degree machinery can resolve the parabolic residue.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**Phi\_min / Z4 / boundary-zero infrastructure should be reactivated as an attack route. No conclusion about its success is certified by the exit interview.**

---

# **5\. BLOCKING DEFECTS IN THE EXIT INTERVIEW**

## **Defect 1 — Possible overstatement of “route exhausted”**

**Passage or claim:**

**ROUTE EXHAUSTED FOR immediate Case 3 square-forcing from connectedness \+ weak vertex coverage \+ arbitrarily small diameters alone**

**Failure mode:**  
**Could be read as a mathematical impossibility theorem rather than a diagnostic exhaustion of a simple argument form.**

**Rule or standard violated:**  
**Tier separation / no overclaiming.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**The simple argument form is not presently sufficient: connectedness, weak vertex coverage, and arbitrarily small diameters alone do not provide a certified square-forcing argument without additional premises or lemmas.**

**Why it matters:**  
**Prevents the kernel or continuity state from recording a negative theorem that has not been proved.**

---

## **Defect 2 — Strong Coverage Lemma framed as “must first prove”**

**Passage or claim:**

**Any boundary invariant attack must first prove a strengthening:**  
**Strong Coverage Lemma...**

**Failure mode:**  
**Too strong. A boundary invariant attack might proceed using a smaller nontrivial boundary set, a local obstruction, or a different compactified object. Strong coverage over all but two points may be sufficient but not necessary.**

**Rule or standard violated:**  
**Over-necessity / premature dependency locking.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**A boundary invariant attack requires some verified form of boundary accumulation support strong enough to carry the proposed obstruction. One possible sufficient target is a Strong Coverage Lemma, but other local or weaker boundary-support mechanisms may also be viable.**

**Why it matters:**  
**Avoids narrowing future traversal artificially.**

---

## **Defect 3 — Reciprocal symmetry treated too casually**

**Passage or claim:**

**The rho(S) subset (0,1) case is symmetric under reciprocal aspect convention if the labeling/diagonal convention permits reciprocal relabeling; if not, it must be treated separately.**

**Failure mode:**  
**The caveat is present, but the surrounding argument still leans on symmetry without verifying whether the convention preserves the relevant component, orientation, and graceful order.**

**Rule or standard violated:**  
**Representation / relabeling gate not cleared.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**The rho(S) subset (0,1) case may be formally analogous to rho(S) subset (1,infinity), but only after verifying that the reciprocal relabeling preserves the relevant configuration space, orientation convention, graceful order, and connected component. Until then, the two cases must remain separate.**

**Why it matters:**  
**This problem has already produced orientation and relabeling defects in earlier cycles; the exit interview should not allow that failure mode back in.**

---

## **Defect 4 — Normalized shape compactness not fully justified**

**Passage or claim:**

**Since each normalized rectangle lies in a compact normalized rectangle-shape space, pass to a subsequence...**

**Failure mode:**  
**Compactness depends on the chosen normalization and whether degenerate shapes are included. If aspect ratio tends to 0 or infinity, the compactification must be explicitly defined.**

**Rule or standard violated:**  
**Compactification gate under-specified.**

**Corrected formulation:**

**After choosing an explicit compactified normalized rectangle-shape space that includes or separately accounts for degenerate limits, one may attempt subsequence extraction. Without that compactification, compactness is not automatic.**

**Why it matters:**  
**Boundary arguments depend on the exact compactification.**

---

# **6\. MATERIAL REVISIONS REQUIRED BEFORE USE**

## **A. Revisions to process-rule language**

**Required:**

1. **Make “five attacks” flexible rather than mandatory where fewer distinct attacks exist.**  
2. **Revise “highest-ranked attack” to “selected attack,” with explanation if not highest-ranked.**  
3. **Generalize coverage-strength and one-sided interval rules beyond this particular rectangle problem.**  
4. **Add explicit warning that conduct rules must not encode mathematical claims.**

---

## **B. Revisions to mathematical/topological language**

**Required:**

1. **Mark compactified boundary invariant as an attack program only.**  
2. **Mark Role-Overlap Theorem as a lemma target only.**  
3. **Mark one-sided aspect split as an analytic decomposition, not an exhaustive theorem.**  
4. **Reformulate route exhaustion as exhaustion of a simple argument form, not as a negative theorem.**  
5. **Replace “must first prove Strong Coverage Lemma” with “must establish sufficient boundary-support strength.”**  
6. **Require exact verification of Schwartz Case 3 before using weak/strong coverage claims.**

---

## **C. Revisions to status labels**

**The proposed corrected label is acceptable:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP WITH THEOREM-OBJECT LEDGER / NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL**

**Optional shorter label:**

**DIAGNOSTIC FRONTIER MAP / NOT JURY-READY**

**But the longer label is more precise and should be retained.**

---

**Explanation:**

**Its mathematical content is useful but uncertified. It should seed the next traversal as an attack catalogue, not as established progress.**

# **10\. INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

## **Rule 1 — Frontier Boundary Attack Conversion**

**Exact text:**

**FRONTIER BOUNDARY ATTACK CONVERSION RULE**

**When a traversal identifies a missing theorem, open residue, frontier boundary, or obstruction that blocks the declared target, it must convert that boundary into at least one explicit attack object before closing.**

**An attack object must specify:**  
**1\. hypotheses;**  
**2\. desired conclusion;**  
**3\. mechanism sought;**  
**4\. proof route;**  
**5\. falsification route;**  
**6\. dependency burden;**  
**7\. at least one computation, deduction, construction step, obstruction test, or route-exhaustion attempt pursued immediately.**

**Naming a missing theorem, obstacle, or residue is insufficient.**

**Failure mode prevented: Barrier receipt / passive residue halt.**

**Scope: All frontier, open-problem, residue-bearing, or continuation traversals.**

**Limitation: Does not require solving the target; requires active attack conversion.**

---

## **Rule 2 — Active Attack Catalogue**

**Exact text:**

**ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE RULE**

**For hard, open, frontier, or residue-bearing traversals, the output must include an Active Attack Catalogue unless the traversal has already resolved the target.**

**The catalogue must contain all materially distinct plausible attack routes available within the current formal base, up to a practical maximum chosen by the traversal. For each attack, state:**  
**1\. target theorem, obstruction, or construction;**  
**2\. hypotheses;**  
**3\. mechanism sought;**  
**4\. why it might work;**  
**5\. why it might fail;**  
**6\. satisfaction condition;**  
**7\. falsification condition;**  
**8\. concrete next computation or deduction.**

**If fewer than five attacks are available, the traversal must state why the catalogue is narrower.**

**Failure mode prevented: Under-generation of continuation routes.**

**Scope: Hard/open/frontier traversals.**

**Limitation: Attack count must track actual distinct mathematical availability, not artificial padding.**

---

## **Rule 3 — Attack Ranking and Selection**

**Exact text:**

**ATTACK RANKING AND SELECTION RULE**

**After generating an Active Attack Catalogue, the traversal must rank the attacks by:**  
**1\. plausibility;**  
**2\. expected value;**  
**3\. dependency burden;**  
**4\. false-transfer risk;**  
**5\. fit with inherited residue;**  
**6\. likelihood of producing a definite next computation.**

**The traversal must select one primary attack for immediate pursuit and explain why that attack was selected.**

**Failure mode prevented: Unprioritized theorem-object ledger.**

**Scope: Any traversal with multiple open attack routes.**

**Limitation: Ranking is operational, not proof of correctness.**

---

## **Rule 4 — Pursue One Attack**

**Exact text:**

**PURSUE ONE ATTACK RULE**

**A frontier traversal may not close after merely naming attack routes. It must pursue at least one selected attack beyond description.**

**The pursued attack should normally be the highest-ranked attack. If a lower-ranked attack is pursued instead, the traversal must explain why it offers the best immediate computation, deduction, construction step, falsification test, compactification analysis, or obstruction test.**

**If no attack can be pursued beyond naming, the output must label itself:**

**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY / NOT JURY-READY AS FRONTIER TRAVERSAL.**

**Failure mode prevented: Stopping after naming plausible attacks.**

**Scope: Frontier traversals, continuation traversals, and residue programs.**

**Limitation: The pursued attack may end in blockage, reduction, or route exhaustion.**

---

## **Rule 5 — Coverage-Strength Separation**

**Exact text:**

**COVERAGE-STRENGTH SEPARATION RULE**

**Whenever a theorem, construction, or traversal uses both coverage claims and degeneration, limiting, compactification, or boundary claims, it must distinguish the exact strength of each coverage assertion.**

**In particular, the traversal must not treat:**  
**1\. “each point occurs in some configuration”**  
**as equivalent to**  
**2\. “each point occurs as a limit of degenerating configurations”**

**unless that strengthening is explicitly proved or cited as an established theorem.**

**Any argument using weak coverage as strong limiting coverage without proof must be flagged as blocked.**

**Failure mode prevented: Illicit conversion of weak coverage into boundary accumulation.**

**Scope: Compactification, degeneration, limiting, boundary, and configuration-space arguments.**

**Limitation: Does not assert which coverage strength any external theorem supplies.**

---

## **Rule 6 — One-Sided Invariant Split**

**Exact text:**

**ONE-SIDED INVARIANT SPLIT RULE**

**If a continuous invariant image is connected and avoids a target value, the traversal must not treat avoidance as a single undifferentiated case when boundary or degeneracy is present.**

**It must separately test, where applicable:**  
**1\. bounded-away-from-target behavior;**  
**2\. target approached only at boundary or compactification limit;**  
**3\. escape to degeneracy, infinity, collapse, or loss of normalization.**

**Each subcase must be assessed before the route can be declared blocked, held, exhausted, or resolved.**

**Failure mode prevented: Over-coarse treatment of one-sided invariant behavior.**

**Scope: Continuous invariant, compactification, degeneration, and IVT-style arguments.**

**Limitation: The listed subcases are a required minimum where applicable, not automatically an exhaustive theorem.**

---

## **Rule 7 — Inherited Infrastructure Reactivation**

**Exact text:**

**INHERITED INFRASTRUCTURE REACTIVATION RULE**

**When a traversal inherits established maps, invariants, compactifications, sign mechanisms, prior gates, or bridge machinery, any new residue must be tested against at least one inherited structure unless the traversal explains why the inherited structures are irrelevant.**

**The statement “the prior machinery remains relevant” is insufficient.**

**The traversal must either:**  
**1\. perform a concrete reactivation attempt; or**  
**2\. state the exact obstruction preventing reactivation.**

**Failure mode prevented: Passive preservation of prior machinery without operational use.**

**Scope: Continuation traversals and bridge-construction programs.**

**Limitation: Reactivation attempts may fail; the rule requires testing, not success.**

---

# **11\. JURY CERTIFICATION STATEMENT**

**This exit interview IS suitable as diagnostic input for process repair under the limitations stated above.**

**No mathematical claim in the exit interview has been certified as established.**

**The following have been certified only as acceptable process-rule repairs, in revised form:**

**1\. Frontier Boundary Attack Conversion.**  
**2\. Active Attack Catalogue.**  
**3\. Attack Ranking and Selection.**  
**4\. Pursue One Attack.**  
**5\. Coverage-Strength Separation.**  
**6\. One-Sided Invariant Split.**  
**7\. Inherited Infrastructure Reactivation.**

---

# **12\. NON-HALTING CRITIQUE DISCLOSURE**

1. **The exit interview usefully accepts fault instead of defending the prior traversal.**  
2. **The attack catalogue is overlong but productive; future kernels should prevent catalogue generation from replacing actual attack pursuit.**  
3. **The mathematical decomposition is valuable as a search scaffold, but several items need exact formalization before they can support proof.**  
4. **The exit interview still tends toward naming new theorem objects. The proposed rules help, but future traversals must enforce the “pursue one attack” requirement strictly.**  
5. **The phrase “route exhausted” should be used only with a declared route schema and a narrow scope.**  
6. **The exit interview properly identifies inherited infrastructure as underused, but it does not yet demonstrate a successful reactivation.**  
7. **The most valuable immediate kernel repair is the combined package:**

**Frontier Boundary Attack Conversion**  
**\+ Active Attack Catalogue**  
**\+ Attack Ranking and Selection**  
**\+ Pursue One Attack**

**That package directly prevents recurrence of BARRIER RECEIPT / PASSIVE RESIDUE HALT.**

**Instruction base:**

**Traversal designation:**  
**Toeplitz / Inscribed Square Problem continuation after DST v17a.**

**Field 13:**  
**INACTIVE — formal mathematical traversal. Canon may supply framing and translation only. It does not function as proof authority.**

**Ontological stance:**  
**Neutral. Proof, refutation, nullification, obstruction certificate, route exhaustion, sharpened open-residue certificate, or provisional frontier-map downgrade are all acceptable outcomes. The traversal must not enter with a pre-claimed solution or impossibility.**

**IMPORTANT EXECUTION REQUIREMENT:**  
**This is not a request for a confirmation receipt, literature-status summary, or frontier map only. Frontier initialization is required, but it is not the traversal. After frontier initialization, the engine must perform substantive mathematical traversal work on the Schwartz parabolic residue.**

**Every required task must include:**  
**TASK:**  
**Inputs inherited:**  
**Definitions fixed:**  
**Operation attempted:**  
**Detailed work:**  
**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**Status:**  
**Next computation or theorem required:**

**If the output cannot execute a substantive proof/construction/obstruction/nullification/formal theorem-target analysis, it must explicitly label itself:**  
**PARTIAL FRONTIER MAP ONLY**  
**NOT A SUBSTANTIVE TRAVERSAL**  
**NOT JURY-READY AS TRAVERSAL.**

**Additional active-attack requirement:**  
**If the traversal reaches a missing theorem or open residue, it must not stop there. It must produce an Active Attack Catalogue, rank the attacks, select a primary attack, and pursue that attack far enough to produce either a mechanism, a precise failure mode, a route-exhaustion result for the declared purpose, or a concrete next computation. Naming a barrier is not enough.**

**Special Counsel limitation:**  
**The following attack prompts are not established mathematical starting facts. They come from diagnostic exit-interview review and Special Counsel process assessment. They may be used only as open attack targets, possible route decompositions, or dependency checks:**  
**1\. weak versus strong parabolic boundary coverage;**  
**2\. one-sided rho behavior split into bounded, boundary-target-escape, and degenerating profiles;**  
**3\. Role-Overlap Lemma;**  
**4\. compactified parabolic boundary invariant;**  
**5\. Phi\_min / Z4 / boundary-zero reactivation against the parabolic residue.**

**FIELD 1 — PROBLEM STATEMENT**

**For every continuous Jordan curve gamma: S1 \-\> R2, does there exist a genuine square inscribed in gamma whose four vertices occur in cyclic order along gamma?**

**Equivalent DST target:**  
**G\_sq(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma) is nonempty.**

**This continuation does not restart the Inscribed Square Problem from scratch. It begins from the DST v17a state and targets the remaining Schwartz parabolic residue.**

**FIELD 2 — FORMAL BASE F**

**ZFC set-theoretic topology; standard real analysis; Euclidean plane geometry; Jordan curve topology; configuration-space topology; compactness and Hausdorff-limit arguments; geometric topology; algebraic topology and equivariant methods where relevant; and current externally established mathematical literature on the inscribed square problem, square peg problem, rectangular peg problems, graceful rectangles, Schwartz trichotomy, aspect-ratio forcing, and related continuous-Jordan-loop results.**

**No regularity assumption beyond continuity is imposed on gamma unless explicitly declared as a restricted sub-bridge.**

**FIELD 3 — NULLIFICATION ALGEBRA N\_F**

**Admissible transformations and reductions:**  
**1\. orientation-preserving reparameterization of S1;**  
**2\. relabeling only when compatible with the declared cyclic-order component and rectangle/square vertex convention;**  
**3\. passage between Schwartz notation and DST notation only through explicitly verified translation;**  
**4\. compactification of configuration spaces only when degeneration strata are named and tracked;**  
**5\. Hausdorff-limit arguments only with source sequence, compact space, and inheritance mechanism specified;**  
**6\. connected-set image arguments only where the target is a real interval or other appropriate connected codomain;**  
**7\. path/IVT arguments only when required connectedness or path-connectedness condition is actually established;**  
**8\. external theorem use only with tier classification and exact theorem-scope statement.**

**Not admissible:**  
**1\. transferring unordered rectangle existence into order-compatible rectangle existence without proof;**  
**2\. treating connectedness as path-connectedness without argument;**  
**3\. treating positive-measure or large aspect-ratio sets as containing a specific target value without a separate argument;**  
**4\. treating failure of surveyed bridges as impossibility;**  
**5\. treating canon-guided synthesis as proof-level closure;**  
**6\. asserting Goedel/Lambda irreducibility without a formal irreducibility argument relative to declared formal base, encoding class, nullification algebra, and admissible bridge class;**  
**7\. calling a frontier-status receipt a completed traversal.**

**FIELD 4 — TARGETS**

**Primary target T\_strong:**  
**Prove, refute, nullify, or sharply classify the universal claim that every continuous Jordan curve gamma has G\_sq(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma) nonempty.**

**Immediate continuation target T\_parabolic:**  
**Analyze the Schwartz parabolic residue left after v17a.**

**Primary question:**  
**Can Schwartz Case 3 occur for a continuous Jordan curve without also producing a square-producing Case 1 or Case 2 mechanism?**

**Equivalent operational targets:**  
**1\. prove that the parabolic case cannot occur as the only active Schwartz case;**  
**2\. prove that the parabolic case, if it occurs, still forces an aspect-ratio-1 graceful rectangle;**  
**3\. construct or characterize a candidate Jordan loop realizing parabolic-only behavior;**  
**4\. prove that current tools cannot decide the parabolic residue and name the exact missing theorem, obstruction, or bridge;**  
**5\. sharpen the residue into a more precise continuation target.**

**Secondary target:**  
**T\_weak, unordered square existence, remains secondary and must not be conflated with T\_strong.**

**FIELD 5 — PRIOR STATE ENTERING THIS TRAVERSAL**

**The following v17a findings are inherited as the active starting state unless this traversal discovers a specific reason to reopen them:**

**1\. Schwartz, "A Trichotomy for Rectangles Inscribed in Jordan Loops," was classified in v17a as TIER A for the bridge program: citation and mechanism verified.**  
**2\. Schwartz's graceful rectangle space G(gamma) was translated in v17a as DST's G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma).**  
**3\. G24 was CLEARED via Schwartz: order-compatible genuine rectangle existence is established by Schwartz, not merely by unordered Vaughan/Meyerson-style rectangle existence.**  
**4\. Cases 1 and 2 of Schwartz's trichotomy were assessed in v17a as square-producing:**  
   **\- Case 1 explicitly gives aspect ratio 1\.**  
   **\- Case 2 gives rho(S) \= (0, infinity), so aspect ratio 1 follows by connected-image reasoning.**  
**5\. T\_strong remains open only through the parabolic residue:**  
   **\- Case 3 gives a connected set S of gracefully inscribed rectangles containing rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
   **\- Case 3 does not explicitly force aspect ratio 1\.**  
   **\- Schwartz conjectures the parabolic case cannot occur.**  
**6\. FLAG-1 is resolved or bypassed in Cases 1 and 2 because a square is produced directly. It remains open only for the parabolic case.**  
**7\. FLAG-2, path-connectedness / CCC, remains HELD where relevant to Case 3\. Schwartz's connected set S is connected but not automatically path-connected.**  
**8\. The Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge and prior Euler/Stiefel-Whitney routes remain historical infrastructure. Some routes were exhausted only for declared purposes and must not be globally treated as exhausted unless the specific exhaustion certificate applies to this new target.**

**FIELD 6 — FRONTIER FIDELITY REQUIREMENT**

**This includes:**  
**1\. active DST continuity records;**

**10\. adjacent-domain results that materially affect the parabolic residue.**

**If any frontier component cannot be verified, disclose it and carry it as active residue.**

**FIELD 7 — KNOWN ACTIVE HAZARDS**

**1\. Reopening G24 without cause.**  
**2\. Treating connected S as path-connected.**  
**3\. Treating Case 3 as impossible merely because Schwartz conjectures it cannot occur.**  
**4\. Treating Cases 1 and 2 as unresolved.**  
**5\. Treating failure to close Case 3 as proof of irreducibility.**  
**6\. Confusing aspect-ratio 1 with perpendicularity-sign arguments.**  
**7\. Treating prior exhausted equivariant/cohomological routes as globally exhausted.**

**9\. Substituting a residue receipt for a traversal.**

**FIELD 8 — CORE RESIDUE**

**SCHWARTZ PARABOLIC RESIDUE**

**Schwartz's trichotomy gives, for every Jordan loop gamma, a connected set S of gracefully inscribed rectangles satisfying one of three alternatives.**

**Cases 1 and 2 are square-producing under v17a.**

**Case 3 supplies arbitrarily small gracefully inscribed rectangles but does not explicitly force aspect ratio 1\.**

**The unresolved question is whether Case 3:**  
**1\. cannot occur;**  
**2\. can occur only along with a square-producing structure;**  
**3\. itself secretly forces aspect ratio 1;**  
**4\. admits a parabolic-only example;**  
**5\. or remains an open formal residue requiring a new theorem or construction.**

**FIELD 9 — BRIDGE DIRECTIONS**

**Primary bridge direction:**  
**B\_PAR — Schwartz Parabolic Case Analysis.**

**Sub-bridges:**  
**B\_PAR-1 — Nonoccurrence bridge.**  
**B\_PAR-2 — Nonexclusive-case bridge.**  
**B\_PAR-3 — Internal square-forcing bridge.**  
**B\_PAR-4 — Construction/countermodel bridge.**  
**B\_PAR-5 — Prior-bridge interaction.**  
**B\_PAR-6 — External theorem bridge.**

**FIELD 10 — REQUIRED TASKS**

**TASK 1 — Frontier Initialization**  
**Recover the best available current state concerning Schwartz's parabolic case and related work. Classify all external claims by tier. Explicitly disclose anything unavailable, unverified, stale, or uncertain. This task is initialization only and cannot satisfy the traversal by itself.**

**TASK 2 — Exact Parabolic Restatement**  
**Restate Schwartz Case 3 in DST notation. Identify exactly what is known about S, G(gamma), G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma), connectedness, diameter behavior, aspect-ratio behavior, vertex coverage, degeneration, small-rectangle behavior, and what Case 3 does not imply.**

**TASK 3 — Square-Forcing Analysis Inside Case 3**  
**Perform substantive analysis of whether Case 3 contains hidden square-forcing structure. At minimum, attempt the following formal route:**

**Assume for contradiction that 1 is not in rho(S). Since S is connected and rho is continuous on the genuine rectangle space, rho(S) is a connected subset of (0, infinity), hence rho(S) lies entirely in (0,1) or entirely in (1,infinity). Analyze what geometric, topological, or limiting consequences follow when S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter while rho(S) remains one-sided away from 1\. Determine whether this yields contradiction, an obstruction class, a parabolic-only profile, or no conclusion.**

**Also assess:**  
**\- f\_perp zero-membership;**  
**\- normalized small-rectangle degeneration;**  
**\- vertex-coverage constraints;**  
**\- tangent-like or secant-like limiting structure without assuming differentiability;**  
**\- relation between arbitrarily small rectangles and square-producing limits.**

**TASK 4 — Theorem Object Construction**  
**Construct at least three theorem objects:**

**THEOREM OBJECT A — Nonoccurrence:**  
**Hypotheses, conclusion, equivalent forms, proof strategies, obstructions, falsification conditions, current status.**

**THEOREM OBJECT B — Internal square-forcing:**  
**Hypotheses, conclusion, equivalent forms, proof strategies, obstructions, falsification conditions, current status.**

**THEOREM OBJECT C — Parabolic-only construction/countermodel:**  
**Hypotheses/target construction, required properties, exclusion of Cases 1 and 2, proof burden, obstruction conditions, current status.**

**TASK 5 — Parabolic-Only Possibility**  
**Characterize what a Jordan curve would need to look like for Case 3 to occur without Cases 1 or 2\. State whether such behavior appears:**  
**\- impossible with proof;**  
**\- blocked by named theorem;**  
**\- constructible in principle;**  
**\- candidate-constructible but incomplete;**  
**\- currently beyond available tools.**

**TASK 6 — Prior Bridge Interaction**  
**Assess whether the parabolic residue changes the status of:**  
**\- IVT / CCC bridge;**  
**\- f\_perp sign-change bridge;**  
**\- Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant bridge;**  
**\- boundary-zero analysis;**  
**\- smooth approximation / nondegeneration route;**  
**\- prior exhausted Euler/Stiefel-Whitney routes.**

**TASK 7 — Active Attack Catalogue and Primary Attack Execution**  
**Generate an Active Attack Catalogue for the Schwartz parabolic residue.**

**The following are open attack prompts only, not established claims:**  
**1\. weak versus strong parabolic boundary coverage;**  
**2\. one-sided rho behavior split into bounded, boundary-target-escape, and degenerating profiles;**  
**3\. Role-Overlap Lemma;**  
**4\. compactified parabolic boundary invariant construction;**  
**5\. Greene-Lobb angle-set transfer/intersection attack;**  
**6\. reactivation of Phi\_min / Z4 equivariant or boundary-zero infrastructure;**  
**7\. parabolic-only construction or countermodel attack.**

**Include all materially distinct plausible attacks available within the current formal base. If fewer than five are available, explain why the catalogue is narrower.**

**For each attack:**  
**\- target theorem or obstruction;**  
**\- hypotheses;**  
**\- mechanism sought;**  
**\- why it might work;**  
**\- why it might fail;**  
**\- what would satisfy it;**  
**\- what would falsify it;**  
**\- next concrete computation.**

**Rank the attacks by plausibility, expected value, dependency burden, and fit with inherited residue.**

**Then select one primary attack and pursue it beyond naming. At minimum, perform a proof sketch, construction sketch, obstruction sketch, boundary computation, dependency reduction, or route-exhaustion argument.**

**TASK 8 — Outcome Classification**

**1\. T\_STRONG PROVED;**

**SECTION 1 — FRONTIER INITIALIZATION**

**TASK:**  
**Recover the best available current state concerning Schwartz’s parabolic case and related work.**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**The intake states that this continuation begins from v17a, does not restart Toeplitz, and targets only the Schwartz parabolic residue. The inherited v17a state says Schwartz was classified as TIER A for the bridge, G24 was cleared via order-compatible graceful rectangles, Cases 1 and 2 were treated as square-producing, and T\_strong remains open only through Case 3\.**

**Definitions fixed:**

* **gamma: continuous Jordan loop.**  
* **G(gamma): Schwartz graceful rectangle space, translated in v17a as DST G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma).**  
* **rho: aspect ratio of a genuine gracefully inscribed rectangle, normalized so rho \= 1 means square.**  
* **S: connected subset of G(gamma) supplied by Schwartz trichotomy.**  
* **Case 3: S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter, and vertex coverage misses at most two points of gamma.**

**External frontier check:**  
**Schwartz’s arXiv abstract states the exact trichotomy: for arbitrary Jordan loop g, G is the space of rectangles inscribed so that cyclic order from R agrees with cyclic order from g; G contains a connected set S satisfying one of three alternatives. Case 1 includes a square, Case 2 has all possible aspect ratios, and Case 3 contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter with all but at most two points of g vertices of rectangles in S. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00740))**

**A 2026 Greene–Lobb preprint states the square peg problem remains unsolved for arbitrary Jordan curves, proves a positive-measure set of rectangle angles for any Jordan curve, and distinguishes continuous curves from stronger regularity cases. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2604.17116v1)) It also states that Schwartz improved rectangle coverage to all but at most four points of every Jordan curve, but that these older non-symplectic techniques “do not detect the similarity classes” of the rectangles. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2604.17116v1))**

**Tier classification:**

* **Schwartz trichotomy: USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A for this traversal, because the intake inherits v17a citation/mechanism verification and current external check confirms the trichotomy statement.**  
* **Greene–Lobb 2026 positive-measure rectangle-angle result: REPORTED IN LITERATURE — PROVISIONAL — TIER B. It is current and relevant, but not verified here as a proof-level transfer into the parabolic residue.**  
* **Claim “square peg problem remains unsolved for arbitrary Jordan curves”: EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED AS CURRENT LITERATURE STATUS for this traversal, supported by Greene–Lobb 2026\. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2604.17116v1))**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**Frontier initialization succeeds. It does not close the traversal.**

**Status:**  
**TASK 1 COMPLETE.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Determine whether Schwartz Case 3 can be made square-producing, nullified, or separated into a parabolic-only candidate.**

**SECTION 2 — EXACT PARABOLIC RESTATEMENT**

**TASK:**  
**Restate Schwartz Case 3 in DST notation.**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**Field 8 defines the Schwartz parabolic residue: Case 3 supplies arbitrarily small gracefully inscribed rectangles but does not explicitly force aspect ratio 1\.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**Let S be the connected set supplied by Schwartz inside G(gamma) \= G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma). Let diam(R) be the Euclidean diameter of rectangle R. Let rho(R) \> 0 be its aspect ratio.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Translate Case 3 into the exact data available for DST.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Case 3 gives:**

1. **S is connected.**  
2. **Every R in S is a gracefully inscribed rectangle, hence order-compatible and inside the cyclic-order rectangle space.**  
3. **For every sufficiently small epsilon \> 0, there exists R in S with diam(R) \< epsilon.**  
4. **All but at most two points of gamma are vertices of rectangles in S.**  
5. **Case 3 does not state that rho(S) contains 1\.**  
6. **Case 3 does not state that rho(S) equals (0, infinity).**  
7. **Case 3 does not state that S is path-connected.**  
8. **Case 3 does not give compactness of S inside the genuine rectangle locus, because the small-diameter behavior points toward the degeneration boundary.**  
9. **Case 3 does not by itself provide an IVT path from rho \< 1 to rho \> 1\.**  
10. **Case 3 does not by itself provide f\_perp sign reversal within a single connected or path-connected component.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**The parabolic residue is not “lack of rectangles.” It is “lack of aspect-ratio crossing inside a connected graceful rectangle family that accumulates at small diameter.”**

**Status:**  
**TASK 2 COMPLETE.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Analyze whether connectedness plus small-diameter coverage forces rho(S) to cross 1, or whether S may remain one-sided in aspect ratio.**

**SECTION 3 — SQUARE-FORCING ANALYSIS INSIDE CASE 3**

**TASK:**  
**Assume 1 not in rho(S). Since S is connected and rho is continuous on the genuine rectangle space, rho(S) is connected in (0, infinity). Analyze consequences of one-sided rho behavior.**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**Case 3 gives connected S and arbitrarily small rectangles. The intake specifically requires this contradiction-style analysis.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**rho(S) is connected subset of (0, infinity). If 1 not in rho(S), then rho(S) lies in (0,1) or in (1,infinity).**

**Operation attempted:**  
**One-sided aspect-ratio attack.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Assume Case 3 and no square in S.**

**Then either:**

**Profile A:**  
**rho(S) subset (0,1).**

**Profile B:**  
**rho(S) subset (1,infinity).**

**Because replacing each rectangle by its cyclic relabeling usually inverts aspect ratio, a tempting attack says: if R is in S, then sigma.R has aspect ratio 1/rho(R), so one-sidedness fails. But this is not admissible unless sigma.R is also in the same S. Schwartz’s theorem supplies some connected S, not necessarily a sigma-invariant connected S. Therefore the direct relabeling attack fails at the “same S” membership step.**

**Next, use small-diameter behavior. For a sequence R\_n in S with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0, after translating by a chosen vertex and scaling by diam(R\_n), the rectangles have normalized shapes with aspect ratios rho(R\_n). Passing to a subsequence gives one of three normalized profiles:**

1. **Bounded nondegenerate profile:**  
   **rho(R\_n) \-\> a in (0, infinity), a \!= 1 under one-sided assumption.**  
   **The normalized rectangles converge to a non-square rectangle shape. This creates no contradiction for a merely continuous Jordan curve, because small secant structure need not approximate a tangent line or symmetric local model.**  
2. **Degenerating thin profile:**  
   **rho(R\_n) \-\> 0 or infinity.**  
   **The normalized shape collapses to a segment-like profile. This also creates no contradiction under continuity alone, because a Jordan curve can have arbitrarily wild local approach geometry.**  
3. **Boundary-target escape:**  
   **The vertices converge to a point p on gamma, but the local parameter gaps need not converge proportionally. The limiting local pattern may be controlled by nonuniform modulus of continuity rather than by a tangent cone.**

**The vertex-coverage condition is stronger: all but at most two points are vertices of rectangles in S. If all these rectangles are one-sided with rho \< 1, then almost every point participates in a local or nonlocal rectangle of the same orientation bias. But “same orientation bias” has no contradiction without a role-overlap theorem saying that coverage by one-sided small rectangles must force either the opposite role or a square.**

**This produces a precise missing theorem:**

**ROLE-OVERLAP THEOREM, informal:**  
**If S is a connected family of gracefully inscribed rectangles on a Jordan loop, contains arbitrarily small rectangles, covers all but at most two vertices, and rho(S) avoids 1, then some point must appear in incompatible long-side and short-side roles, forcing rho crossing 1 or a square.**

**This theorem is not established here.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**The one-sided rho attack sharpens the residue but does not close it. The failure is not formal vagueness; it is the absence of a theorem converting vertex coverage plus arbitrarily small diameter into aspect-ratio role reversal.**

**Status:**  
**TASK 3 COMPLETE — OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE SHARPENED.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Prove or refute the Role-Overlap Theorem, or construct a Jordan loop whose small rectangles all remain one-sided in aspect ratio.**

**SECTION 4 — THEOREM OBJECTS**

**THEOREM OBJECT A — Nonoccurrence**

**Status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**gamma is a continuous Jordan loop. S is the connected set of graceful rectangles supplied by Schwartz. S satisfies Case 3: arbitrarily small diameters and all but at most two points of gamma are rectangle vertices.**

**Conclusion:**  
**Case 3 cannot occur as the exclusive Schwartz alternative.**

**Equivalent forms:**

1. **Every Schwartz connected set S satisfying Case 3 also satisfies Case 1 or Case 2\.**  
2. **The parabolic alternative is logically redundant.**  
3. **Every connected graceful rectangle family with full-minus-two vertex coverage and arbitrarily small rectangles either contains a square or all aspect ratios.**

**Why it would close the residue:**  
**If Case 3 cannot occur, only Cases 1 and 2 remain; v17a treats both as square-producing. Then T\_strong follows through Schwartz.**

**Proof strategies:**

* **Compactified boundary degree: show the small-diameter boundary contribution cannot carry the required vertex coverage without reentering rho \= 1\.**  
* **Role overlap: show all-but-two coverage forces each point to appear in both aspect-ratio roles.**  
* **Continuum separation: show one-sided rho families cannot sweep all but two vertices.**

**Obstructions:**

* **Continuity only; no tangent or local monotonicity.**  
* **S connected but not path-connected.**  
* **Small-diameter rectangles can degenerate at wild local geometry.**  
* **sigma-invariance of S is not given.**

**Falsification conditions:**  
**Construct a Jordan loop with a connected graceful rectangle family S satisfying Case 3 while rho(S) avoids 1 and does not realize all aspect ratios.**

**Current status:**  
**HELD — NEXT COMPUTATION NAMED.**

**THEOREM OBJECT B — Internal square-forcing**

**Status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**gamma continuous Jordan loop. S is a Case-3 Schwartz connected set. S may occur; nonoccurrence is not assumed.**

**Conclusion:**  
**1 belongs to rho(S), or at least gamma has a square in G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma).**

**Equivalent forms:**

1. **Arbitrarily small graceful rectangles plus full-minus-two vertex coverage force aspect-ratio crossing.**  
2. **Case 3 secretly contains a square even if it does not contain all aspect ratios.**  
3. **The image rho(S), though not declared all of (0, infinity), must contain 1\.**

**Why it would close the residue:**  
**It makes Case 3 square-producing; together with v17a Cases 1 and 2, T\_strong follows.**

**Proof strategies:**

* **One-sided rho contradiction.**  
* **Compactified rho-extension: extend rho or log rho to the parabolic boundary and show boundary values include both signs.**  
* **Greene–Lobb angle-set transfer: combine positive-measure angle results with Schwartz vertex coverage to force the square angle, if an intersection theorem can be proved.**

**Obstructions:**

* **Positive measure angle sets need not contain the square angle.**  
* **Connected image may be a one-sided interval.**  
* **Boundary rho may fail to extend continuously at collapsed configurations.**  
* **No established path-connectedness of S.**

**Falsification conditions:**  
**A Case-3 S with rho(S) subset (0,1) or subset (1,infinity).**

**Current status:**  
**HELD — NEXT COMPUTATION NAMED.**

**THEOREM OBJECT C — Parabolic-only construction / countermodel**

**Status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Target construction:**  
**A continuous Jordan loop gamma and a Schwartz Case-3 connected set S such that:**

1. **S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
2. **All but at most two points of gamma are vertices of rectangles in S.**  
3. **rho(S) avoids 1\.**  
4. **S does not have all aspect ratios.**  
5. **No other Schwartz connected set supplies Case 1 or Case 2 square production.**

**Required geometric profile:**  
**A curve with local self-similar or comb-like behavior generating arbitrarily small order-compatible rectangles, but with persistent anisotropic aspect-ratio bias.**

**Proof burden:**

* **Must maintain Jordan injectivity.**  
* **Must show graceful cyclic order.**  
* **Must control all rectangle families, not just exhibit one family.**  
* **Must exclude hidden square-producing families elsewhere.**  
* **Must satisfy Schwartz’s global coverage condition.**

**Obstruction conditions:**  
**Any unavoidable role-overlap, symmetry, or compactified-degree invariant would kill the construction.**

**Current status:**  
**Candidate-constructible in principle but incomplete. No construction supplied.**

**SECTION 5 — PARABOLIC-ONLY POSSIBILITY**

**TASK:**  
**Characterize what a Jordan curve would need for Case 3 without Cases 1 or 2\.**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**Case 3 alone gives small rectangles and almost-total vertex coverage; Cases 1 and 2 are square-producing.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**Parabolic-only means Case 3 occurs without any square-producing connected set from Cases 1 or 2 and without internal rho \= 1\.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Countermodel characterization.**

**Detailed work:**  
**A parabolic-only gamma would need:**

1. **Local abundance:**  
   **At almost every point, arbitrarily small rectangle participation must occur.**  
2. **Global anisotropy:**  
   **The rectangles in the controlling connected S must maintain rho entirely below 1 or entirely above 1\.**  
3. **Non-role-overlap:**  
   **The same points must avoid being forced into both long-side and short-side roles within the same connected S.**  
4. **Boundary absorption:**  
   **The family S must accumulate at the collapsed-rectangle boundary without forcing an interior square.**  
5. **Hidden-family exclusion:**  
   **Other graceful rectangle components must not produce a square.**

**This profile appears possible as a formal target but not constructible with the present tools. It is not impossible by proof.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**The construction burden is high because it must control all graceful rectangle families, not merely one explicit family.**

**Status:**  
**TASK 5 COMPLETE — CANDIDATE-CONSTRUCTIBLE BUT INCOMPLETE.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Build a toy model in configuration space: a connected subset S of compactified C4+(gamma) with rho one-sided and parabolic boundary accumulation, then test whether it can be realized by any Jordan loop.**

**SECTION 7 — ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE**

**Attack 1 — Role-Overlap Theorem**  
**Target:**  
**Show all-but-two vertex coverage by a connected one-sided-rho Case-3 family is impossible.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**Case 3 plus rho(S) avoids 1\.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**A point or arc of gamma must appear in both long-side and short-side roles; connectedness then forces rho crossing.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Vertex coverage is very strong. Missing at most two points may force role recurrence.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Continuity-only curves may allow pathological role assignment without local regularity.**

**Satisfaction:**  
**Prove role overlap for arbitrary Jordan loops.**

**Falsification:**  
**Construct a one-sided role assignment compatible with a Jordan loop.**

**Next concrete computation:**  
**Define four role sets L1, L2, S1, S2 on gamma induced by rectangles in S; prove whether they are closed / dense / connected enough to force overlap.**

**Rank:**  
**1\.**

**Attack 2 — Compactified Parabolic Boundary Invariant**  
**Target:**  
**Define an invariant on the closure of S in compactified C4+(gamma), measuring approach to collapse boundary and aspect-ratio sign.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**Case 3\.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Boundary accumulation has nonzero mod-2 or winding obstruction unless rho crosses 1\.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Case 3 is boundary-driven; previous Phi\_min boundary analysis is relevant.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**rho may not extend continuously to full-collapse boundary; invariant may vanish.**

**Satisfaction:**  
**A nonzero boundary class forces an interior rho \= 1\.**

**Falsification:**  
**A compactified model with one-sided rho and zero boundary obstruction.**

**Next computation:**  
**Use log rho as a map into R excluding 0; inspect whether closure of S creates a sign-changing boundary cycle.**

**Rank:**  
**2\.**

**Attack 3 — Greene–Lobb Angle-Set Transfer**  
**Target:**  
**Use positive-measure rectangle angle sets to force square angle in combination with Schwartz Case 3\.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**Arbitrary Jordan curve plus Greene–Lobb 2026 angle set.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Intersect positive-measure angle set with parabolic small-diameter / vertex-coverage constraints.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Greene–Lobb gives many rectangle angles for every Jordan curve. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2604.17116v1))**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Positive measure does not force a specified angle. The intake expressly forbids treating positive measure as containing a target value without a separate argument.**

**Satisfaction:**  
**An interval result containing square angle, or a density theorem at square angle.**

**Falsification:**  
**Positive-measure sets avoiding square angle remain compatible.**

**Next computation:**  
**Check whether the 2026 angle set has density or interval refinements near pi/2 under Case-3 hypotheses.**

**Rank:**  
**3\.**

**Attack 4 — Sigma-Invariant Closure Attack**  
**Target:**  
**Show S can be chosen sigma-invariant or replaced by a connected sigma-closed set S' retaining Case-3 properties.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**Schwartz trichotomy plus Z/4 cyclic relabeling.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**If R in S implies sigma.R in same connected family, rho inverts; connectedness forces 1\.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Cyclic relabeling preserves geometric rectangles and graceful order.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Schwartz supplies existence of a connected S, not uniqueness or invariance. The union S union sigma.S may be disconnected.**

**Satisfaction:**  
**Prove S intersects sigma.S or belongs to a connected sigma-stable continuum.**

**Falsification:**  
**A model where S and sigma.S are disjoint connected components with inverse aspect-ratio ranges.**

**Next computation:**  
**Study whether vertex coverage all-but-two forces S intersect sigma.S.**

**Rank:**  
**4\.**

**Attack 5 — Parabolic-Only Construction**  
**Target:**  
**Construct a Jordan loop realizing Case 3 without rho \= 1\.**

**Hypotheses:**  
**None beyond Jordan continuity.**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Self-similar anisotropic local geometry.**

**Why it might work:**  
**Continuity allows wild local geometry.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Global rectangle theorems may force hidden square components.**

**Satisfaction:**  
**Explicit gamma plus proof of all rectangle family behavior.**

**Falsification:**  
**Any theorem showing parabolic-only impossible.**

**Next computation:**  
**Build a symbolic / PL approximating model with one-sided small rectangles, then test persistence under Jordan limit.**

**Rank:**  
**5\.**

**Primary attack selected:**  
**Attack 1 — Role-Overlap Theorem.**

**PRIMARY ATTACK EXECUTION**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Define role sets and reduce the parabolic residue to a specific overlap statement.**

**Detailed work:**  
**For R in S, label vertices cyclically v1, v2, v3, v4. If rho(R) \< 1, declare the shorter side role as A and longer side role as B. Depending on the rectangle convention, vertices alternate between incident edge roles, but each vertex participates in one short edge and one long edge. Therefore vertex role cannot be assigned merely by point; it must be assigned by incident pair or diagonal role.**

**This kills the naive role-overlap formulation: every vertex of every non-square rectangle already touches both a long and short side. The meaningful role is not “point is long-side vertex” versus “short-side vertex,” because all rectangle vertices are both. The meaningful role must instead be diagonal or cyclic-position role relative to the aspect-ratio orientation.**

**Corrected role object:**  
**For each point p in gamma, define A\_p as the set of local parameter directions from p to neighboring rectangle vertices in S after normalizing small rectangles at p. A one-sided rho family imposes an anisotropic ordering on the two incident secant directions.**

**Reduced theorem:**  
**If Case 3 holds and rho(S) avoids 1, then for all but at most two p, the normalized two-direction secant data A\_p admits an anisotropic orientation. To force contradiction, one must prove that this anisotropic orientation cannot vary continuously / semicontinuously around a Jordan loop without either flipping orientation or producing a square.**

**Precise failure mode:**  
**The original Role-Overlap Lemma is underdefined at vertex level. It must be reformulated as a local normalized secant-direction bundle problem. Under mere continuity, tangent directions do not exist, so the object must be a compact set of blow-up limits, not a tangent vector field.**

**Concrete next computation:**  
**For each p, define Blow\_S(p) as the set of Hausdorff limits of normalized rectangles R\_n in S with p as a chosen vertex and diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\. Then prove or disprove:**

**Blow-Up Role Theorem:**  
**If Case 3 holds and rho(S) avoids 1, the family p \-\> Blow\_S(p) defines a nonempty upper-semicontinuous field of nonsquare rectangle shapes over gamma minus at most two points. Such a field must either contain a square shape somewhere or have monodromy incompatible with a Jordan loop.**

**Result of primary attack:**  
**The role-overlap attack does not close the residue. It produces a sharper theorem object and reveals that “role overlap” must be moved from vertex incidence to normalized local blow-up geometry.**

**Status:**  
**PRIMARY ATTACK EXECUTED — HELD, SHARPENED.**

It did perform substantive traversal work by reducing the strongest apparent attack to a corrected blow-up theorem and by identifying the failure mode of naive role-overlap reasoning.**

5. **INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

**Rule name: Vertex-Incidence Role Ambiguity Rule**

**Exact text:**  
**When an argument assigns “long-side” or “short-side” roles to vertices of a nonsquare rectangle, the traversal must first verify that the proposed role distinction is well-defined. A rectangle vertex is incident to both a long side and a short side, so vertex-level role overlap cannot by itself generate a contradiction. Any role-overlap argument must specify whether the role belongs to an edge, diagonal, cyclic position, oriented secant pair, normalized local blow-up shape, or another precisely defined object.**

**Failure mode prevented: Naive role-overlap contradiction based on underdefined vertex roles.**

**Scope: Rectangle / quadrilateral configuration-space traversals and any DST argument using role assignment on polygon vertices.**

**Limitation: Does not block properly defined edge-role, diagonal-role, or normalized blow-up-role arguments.**

---

**Rule name: Same-Continuum Symmetry Rule**

**Exact text:**  
**When a symmetry operation transforms a configuration into another configuration with an inverted or complementary invariant, the traversal may not infer an intermediate value inside a connected set unless it proves that both configurations lie in the same connected continuum, or that a connected symmetry-closed replacement continuum exists and preserves the relevant hypotheses.**

**Failure mode prevented: Invalid use of cyclic relabeling or group action to force aspect-ratio crossing without same-S membership.**

**Scope: All equivariant / symmetry-based DST bridge arguments.**

**Limitation: Does not forbid symmetry arguments after same-component, connected-union, or invariant-continuum membership is proved.**

---

**Rule name: Positive-Measure Target-Value Rule**

**Exact text:**  
**A positive-measure set of parameter values may not be treated as containing a specified target value unless an additional theorem supplies interval containment, density at the target, forced intersection, or an equivalent target-inclusion mechanism.**

**Failure mode prevented: False transfer from “many angles” to “square angle occurs.”**

**Scope: Measure-to-existence transfers across geometry, harmonic analysis, topology, and parameter-space arguments.**

**Limitation: Does not block positive-measure arguments when the target is itself variable or when a separate intersection theorem is supplied.**
