**DST TRAVERSAL RECORD**

**TOEPLITZ / BLOW-UP ROLE THEOREM PROGRAM**

**Object type:**  
**JURY-READY TRAVERSAL CANDIDATE AS ACTIVE-ATTACK / ONE-SIDED MODEL CANDIDATE REPORT.**  
**NOT PUBLIC-READY.**  
**NOT A PROOF OF T\_STRONG.**  
**NOT A NULLIFICATION OF SCHWARTZ CASE 3\.**  
**NOT A PROOF THAT MONODROMY OBSTRUCTION EXISTS.**

**Primary outcome:**  
**ONE-SIDED MODEL CANDIDATE CONSTRUCTED.**

**Short abstract:**  
**This traversal formalizes Blow\_S(p) as a role-labeled normalized small-rectangle limit set. It establishes that the set-valued map p \-\> Blow\_S(p), with empty values allowed, has a closed graph and hence upper-semicontinuity in the compact-valued sense after the correct compact shape target is chosen. This does not close the Blow-Up Role Theorem, because Schwartz Case 3 gives weak vertex coverage and existence of arbitrarily small rectangles, but does not give strong degeneration coverage at all covered points. The traversal constructs an abstract one-sided model showing that the Case-3 data, by themselves, do not force a nonempty nonsquare blow-up field over gamma minus at most two points. The model is not a Jordan-loop realization. Its function is to block an invalid inference and sharpen the next theorem target.**

**TASK 1 — FRONTIER AND SOURCE CHECK**

**Inputs inherited:**

* **v1.6 continuity state says T\_strong remains open through the Schwartz parabolic residue unless a defect is found in inherited v17a analysis; Blow-Up Role Theorem is the primary next attack.**  
* **v1.6 ledger says public-release blockers include exact Schwartz theorem definitions, translation of G(gamma), Greene-Lobb 2026 verification, and the fact that Blow\_S(p), upper-semicontinuity, and monodromy obstruction remain attack targets rather than established structures.**  
* **Intake requires exact source check, Blow\_S(p) definition, coverage analysis, USC test, one-sided split, monodromy formalization, symmetry check, active attack catalogue, outcome classification, and final audit.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**Schwartz’s paper defines I(gamma) as labeled rectangles inscribed in gamma, labels rectangles counterclockwise around the rectangle, orients gamma counterclockwise around the bounded region, defines graceful rectangles by agreement between the cyclic order on gamma and the rectangle order, defines G(gamma) as gracefully inscribed labeled rectangles, defines rho as aspect ratio, and states a trichotomy for a connected S subset G(gamma).**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Source-level verification of the theorem statement and the exact Case 3 data.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Schwartz Theorem 1.1 states that for an arbitrary Jordan loop gamma, I(gamma) contains a connected set S satisfying one of three alternatives. Case 1 includes 1 in rho(S). Case 2 gives rho(S) \= (0, infinity) and all-but-at-most-4 vertex coverage. Case 3 says S has members of every sufficiently small diameter and V(gamma,S) contains all but at most 2 points of gamma; moreover S subset G(gamma).**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**The source supports the inherited Case-3 input exactly enough for this traversal: connected S, graceful rectangles, arbitrarily small diameters, all-but-two weak vertex coverage. It does not state that every covered point is a limit of arbitrarily small rectangles. It also does not state that rho(S) avoids 1; that assumption belongs to the parabolic-residue attack conditional: if Case 3 is the only remaining obstruction after Cases 1 and 2, test the subcase rho(S) avoiding 1\.**

**Status:**  
**EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED — citation/mechanism confirmed for the wording of Schwartz Theorem 1.1 used here.**  
**USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A for the DST translation of Schwartz G(gamma) into prior G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma), because the internal continuity state inherits that translation but still lists it as requiring verification before public release.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma:**  
**Given Schwartz Case-3 S, prove or refute that V\_small(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points, where V\_small means vertex limits of rectangles in S with diameter tending to zero.**

**TASK 2 — DEFINE Blow\_S(p)**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**The intake requires anchor convention, normalization, sequence condition, shape-space target, topology, exceptional set, and relation to weak versus strong coverage.**

**Definitions fixed:**

**Let gamma: S1 \-\> R2 be a continuous Jordan loop.**

**Let S subset G(gamma) be a connected Case-3 set of graceful labeled rectangles.**

**For R in S, write its vertices in graceful order:**  
**R \= (v1(R), v2(R), v3(R), v4(R)).**

**Let diam(R) \= max\_{i,j} |vi(R) \- vj(R)|.**

**For each role j in {1,2,3,4}, define the role-j normalized shape map N\_j on genuine rectangles by:**  
**N\_j(R) \= ((v1 \- vj)/diam(R), ..., (v4 \- vj)/diam(R)) in (closed unit disk)^4.**

**This anchors vertex j at 0 and scales by diameter. It does not rotate, so it preserves absolute local secant directions when those directions exist as limits. It also avoids tangent assumptions.**

**Define ShapeRect\_j as the closure in (closed unit disk)^4 of all N\_j(R) for genuine labeled Euclidean rectangles with diam(R)\>0, graceful labeling convention irrelevant after normalization. ShapeRect\_j is compact because it is closed inside a compact product.**

**Define ShapeRect \= disjoint union over j of {j} x ShapeRect\_j.**

**Define Blow\_S^j(p):**  
**Q belongs to Blow\_S^j(p) iff there exists a sequence R\_n in S such that:**

1. **diam(R\_n) \-\> 0;**  
2. **v\_j(R\_n) \-\> p;**  
3. **N\_j(R\_n) \-\> Q in ShapeRect\_j.**

**Define role-labeled Blow\_S(p):**  
**Blow\_S(p) \= union over j of {j} x Blow\_S^j(p).**

**Define D\_j \= {p in gamma : Blow\_S^j(p) is nonempty}.**  
**Define D \= union\_j D\_j.**

**Define weak vertex coverage W:**  
**W \= V(gamma,S) \= {p in gamma : p is one of the four vertices of some R in S}.**

**Define strong degeneration coverage D:**  
**D \= {p in gamma : p is a limit anchor of vertices of rectangles R\_n in S with diam(R\_n)-\>0}.**

**Exceptional sets:**  
**E\_weak \= gamma \\ W.**  
**E\_strong \= gamma \\ D.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Construct the object required by the intake without smuggling in differentiability or tangent data.**

**Detailed work:**  
**The definition is valid under the declared formal base. It uses only Euclidean distances, compactness of closed disk products, sequences, and the continuity of gamma. It does not require tangent lines, rectifiability, local monotonicity, or smoothness.**

**The definition deliberately uses role-labeled anchoring rather than “long-side vertex” anchoring. This avoids the v1.5 defect: a rectangle vertex is incident to both a long side and a short side, so a long-side/short-side “role” is ambiguous at the vertex level. The role j is only a label position, not a long/short incidence claim.**

**Aspect-ratio extraction:**  
**On genuine nondegenerate normalized rectangles, rho is continuous as a function of side lengths:**  
**rho(R) \= |v3 \- v2| / |v2 \- v1| under Schwartz’s convention, where the second side is divided by the first side.**  
**In the compact closure, side lengths can degenerate. Therefore rho extends naturally only as an extended-value function into \[0,infinity\], not as a finite continuous function everywhere. The square target remains rho \= 1 on the genuine nondegenerate subspace.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**Success: Blow\_S(p) is definable as a compact-valued role-labeled limit object.**  
**Limitation: Its nonemptiness over gamma minus at most two points is not part of the definition and is not supplied by Case 3\.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED:**

* **Role-labeled Blow\_S(p) is well-defined.**  
* **ShapeRect is compact.**  
* **Degenerate normalized shapes are included.**  
* **The definition separates weak vertex coverage from strong degeneration coverage.**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE:**

* **Whether D contains all but at most two points of gamma.**  
* **Whether the normalized limits are all nonsquare when rho(S) avoids 1\.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Strong Coverage Theorem or countermodel.**

**TASK 3 — NONEMPTINESS / COVERAGE ANALYSIS**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**Schwartz Case 3 supplies:**

1. **S connected.**  
2. **S has members of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
3. **V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**  
4. **S subset G(gamma).**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**For epsilon\>0, define S\_\<epsilon \= {R in S : diam(R)\<epsilon}.**  
**Define V\_\<epsilon \= union over j of v\_j(S\_\<epsilon).**  
**Define D \= intersection over epsilon\>0 of closure(V\_\<epsilon) in gamma.**  
**Then D is exactly the set of points that can occur as limits of vertices of arbitrarily small rectangles in S, before role splitting. Role splitting refines D into D\_j.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Determine what follows from Case 3 alone.**

**Detailed work:**

1. **Nonemptiness somewhere:**  
   **Since Case 3 says S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter, there exists a sequence R\_n in S with diam(R\_n)-\>0. Since gamma is compact, after passing to a subsequence v\_1(R\_n)-\>p for some p in gamma. Since diam(R\_n)-\>0, all vertices v\_j(R\_n)-\>p. By compactness of ShapeRect\_j, after a further subsequence N\_j(R\_n) converges. Therefore Blow\_S(p) is nonempty for at least one p.**

**Conclusion:**  
**D is nonempty.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

2. **All-but-two strong coverage does not follow:**  
   **Schwartz gives V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points. That means for most p, there is at least one rectangle R in S having p as a vertex. It does not say there are arbitrarily small such rectangles anchored at p.**

**The inference**  
**p in V(gamma,S)**  
**therefore p in D**  
**is invalid.**

**Reason:**  
**V(gamma,S) is generated by all rectangles in S, regardless of diameter. D is generated only by small-diameter sequences. A point may be a vertex of a large rectangle in S but never a limit of small rectangles.**

**Status:**  
**BLOCKING DEFECT for any attempt to make Blow\_S(p) nonempty over gamma minus at most two points using Case 3 alone.**

3. **What connectedness adds:**  
   **S connected and diam:S-\>(0,infinity) continuous implies diam(S) is an interval. If S contains members of every sufficiently small diameter, diam(S) contains (0,epsilon0) or at least a cofinal small interval depending on exact interpretation. This produces paths or continua in S linking small and non-small rectangles only if S has stronger local connectedness/path-connectedness properties. Connectedness alone does not imply path-connectedness or controlled vertex coverage at each diameter scale.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED as a topology limitation.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**The coverage route fails at the gap:**  
**weak vertex coverage does not imply strong degeneration coverage.**

**Next theorem required:**  
**STRONG DEGENERATION COVERAGE LEMMA**

**Hypotheses:**

* **gamma is a Jordan loop.**  
* **S subset G(gamma) is connected.**  
* **S has members of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
* **V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points.**

**Conclusion:**  
**For all but at most two p in gamma, there exists R\_n in S with diam(R\_n)-\>0 and some vertex v\_j(R\_n)-\>p.**

**Equivalent formulation:**  
**For every epsilon\>0, V\_\<epsilon contains all but at most two points of gamma, possibly after closure.**

**Why it would close residue:**  
**It would make Blow\_S(p) nonempty over the same large base where weak coverage currently holds, allowing upper-semicontinuity or monodromy analysis to become meaningful globally.**

**Known obstruction:**  
**No such diameter-uniform vertex-coverage statement appears in Schwartz Theorem 1.1. The theorem separates “small diameter exists somewhere” from “all-but-two points are vertices somewhere.”**

**Falsification condition:**  
**Construct an S-like connected abstract family where small rectangles shrink only at one point while large rectangles provide all weak coverage.**

**TASK 4 — UPPER-SEMICONTINUITY TEST**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**The intake requires upper-semicontinuity only after proving graph closedness or hyperspace conditions.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**View Blow\_S as a set-valued map:**  
**Blow\_S: gamma \-\> nonempty-or-empty compact subsets of ShapeRect.**

**Empty values are allowed. This is essential: nonemptiness is a separate theorem.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Prove closed graph.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Let p\_n \-\> p in gamma.**  
**Let Q\_n in Blow\_S^j(p\_n).**  
**Assume Q\_n \-\> Q in ShapeRect\_j.**

**For each n, because Q\_n in Blow\_S^j(p\_n), there exists a witnessing sequence R\_{n,m} in S such that:**  
**diam(R\_{n,m})-\>0 as m-\>infinity;**  
**v\_j(R\_{n,m})-\>p\_n;**  
**N\_j(R\_{n,m})-\>Q\_n.**

**Choose m(n) large enough that:**  
**diam(R\_{n,m(n)}) \< 1/n;**  
**distance(v\_j(R\_{n,m(n)}), p\_n) \< 1/n;**  
**distance(N\_j(R\_{n,m(n)}), Q\_n) \< 1/n.**

**Then the diagonal sequence R\_n' \= R\_{n,m(n)} satisfies:**  
**diam(R\_n')-\>0;**  
**v\_j(R\_n')-\>p because v\_j(R\_n') is within 1/n of p\_n and p\_n-\>p;**  
**N\_j(R\_n')-\>Q because it is within 1/n of Q\_n and Q\_n-\>Q.**

**Therefore Q in Blow\_S^j(p).**

**So graph(Blow\_S^j) is closed in gamma x ShapeRect\_j.**

**Since gamma and ShapeRect\_j are compact metric spaces, each Blow\_S^j(p) is compact, possibly empty. The closed-graph compact-valued multifunction is upper-semicontinuous in the standard Vietoris / Hausdorff-neighborhood sense, with empty values allowed.**

**Failure mode or success mechanism:**  
**Success mechanism:**  
**Graph closedness follows by diagonalization and compact target construction.**

**Limitation:**  
**This does not provide nonempty values on a large domain. It only says the already-defined cluster set behaves upper-semicontinuously.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED:**  
**p \-\> Blow\_S(p) is upper-semicontinuous as a compact-valued set map with empty values allowed.**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE:**  
**Nonempty upper-semicontinuity over gamma minus at most two points is not established.**

**Next computation or theorem required:**  
**Nonempty-USC Field Theorem:**  
**Under Schwartz Case 3 plus additional condition X, Blow\_S(p) is nonempty for p in gamma\\E, |E|\<=2.**

**Candidate additional condition X:**  
**For every epsilon\>0, V\_\<epsilon contains gamma\\E.**  
**This condition is strong enough and directly testable.**

**TASK 5 — ONE-SIDED NONSQUARE FIELD ANALYSIS**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**Assume rho(S) avoids 1 as the parabolic-residue subcase.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**Let sign(R) \= sign(log rho(R)) where defined on genuine rectangles. If rho(S) avoids 1 and S is connected, rho(S) is connected in (0,infinity){1}; hence rho(S) lies entirely in (0,1) or entirely in (1,infinity).**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Apply the One-Sided Invariant Split.**

**Case 1: bounded away from 1\.**  
**Assume there is eta\>0 such that either rho(R)\<=1-eta for all R in S or rho(R)\>=1+eta for all R in S.**

**Detailed work:**  
**All genuine normalized limits that remain nondegenerate preserve a nonsquare one-sided aspect-ratio gap. Degenerate limits may lose finite rho. Nothing in this case forces rho=1 unless a symmetry operation places the same connected continuum on the reciprocal side.**

**Failure mode:**  
**No contradiction without same-S symmetry or full nonempty field over a base supporting an orientation/parity argument.**

**Status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE, consistent at this abstraction level.**

**Case 2: rho approaches 1 only at boundary.**  
**Assume rho(S) avoids 1 but has infimum or supremum approaching 1 along sequences.**

**Detailed work:**  
**If there exists R\_n in S with rho(R\_n)-\>1 and R\_n converges in the genuine rectangle locus to R, then rho(R)=1 and a square is produced. Therefore any rho-\>1 sequence avoiding square must escape compact subsets of the genuine rectangle locus: it must degenerate, lose distinctness, or approach the boundary of S/configuration space.**

**Failure mode:**  
**This route transfers the problem to degeneration analysis. It does not prove a square.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED conditional dichotomy:**  
**rho-\>1 without square requires degeneration or boundary escape.**

**Case 3: escape to degeneration / infinity / collapse / loss of normalization.**  
**Detailed work:**  
**This is exactly the Blow\_S(p) regime. The normalized shape compactification records collapse limits, but collapse limits can be nonsquare or degenerate. A square is forced only if a nondegenerate limit has rho=1, or if an obstruction forces crossing from rho\<1 to rho\>1 in a connected family.**

**Failure mode:**  
**The compact target records limits but does not itself force square occurrence.**

**Status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**TASK 6 — MONODROMY / OBSTRUCTION FORMALIZATION**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**The intake forbids treating monodromy as more than a metaphor without defining base, fiber/correspondence, orientation/sign datum, obstruction class, and force mechanism.**

**Definitions attempted:**  
**Candidate base:**  
**B \= gamma \\ E\_strong, where E\_strong is the set where Blow\_S(p) is empty.**

**Candidate fiber:**  
**F\_p \= Blow\_S(p) intersect nonsquare nondegenerate shape subspace.**

**Candidate sign datum:**  
**sign(log rho) in {-1,+1}, if rho extends finitely and nondegenerately.**

**Candidate obstruction:**  
**A loop around gamma would need to transport a chosen local branch of normalized shape through the correspondence p \-\> F\_p and return with reciprocal sign, forcing crossing through rho=1.**

**Detailed work:**  
**This cannot be completed under current data because:**

1. **B may not be gamma minus at most two points. Strong coverage is missing.**  
2. **F\_p may be empty for most p.**  
3. **F\_p may be multi-valued and disconnected, with no transition map.**  
4. **No continuous selection is established.**  
5. **No transport rule is defined.**  
6. **No obstruction class is defined in H^1(B;Z/2), degree theory, or a bundle orientation system.**  
7. **Sigma reciprocal symmetry does not act inside S unless same-S or connected sigma-closure membership is proved.**

**Failure mode:**  
**The base and fiber are not established strongly enough to define monodromy.**

**Status:**  
**MONODROMY NOT FORMALIZED.**  
**MONODROMY ROUTE BLOCKED FOR CURRENT DATA, not globally impossible.**

**Next theorem required:**  
**Monodromy Field Theorem.**

**Hypotheses:**

* **D contains gamma\\E with |E|\<=2.**  
* **Blow\_S(p) has a nonempty compact nonsquare fiber over D.**  
* **There is a locally continuous correspondence or selectable branch.**  
* **Sigma or reciprocal aspect-ratio transport acts on the same connected field.**

**Conclusion:**  
**The sign(log rho) field either remains globally constant or forces square crossing / orientation contradiction.**

**Falsification:**  
**A connected one-sided field over D with constant sign and no reciprocal transport.**

**TASK 7 — SYMMETRY AND SAME-CONTINUUM CHECK**

**Inputs inherited:**  
**The control ledger added Same-Continuum Symmetry Rule after v1.5: direct sigma relabeling cannot force rho crossing inside S without same-S, S intersect sigma(S), connected sigma-closure, or another connected symmetry-compatible continuum.**

**Definitions fixed:**  
**sigma \= cyclic relabeling of a labeled rectangle.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Test sigma and reciprocal aspect ratio.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Schwartz states that cyclic relabeling gives a Z/4 action on I(gamma) with no fixed points. Since graceful order is cyclic-order agreement, cyclic relabeling preserves the graceful property: it changes the starting label but not the cyclic order agreement. Thus sigma preserves G(gamma).**

**C4+(gamma), as used in the prior DST bridge, is preserved by Z/4 cyclic relabeling, not by full D4. This is consistent with the active kernel’s Z/4/domain-compatibility rules.**

**However, Schwartz Theorem 1.1 supplies existence of a connected S subset G(gamma). It does not say sigma(S)=S. It does not say sigma(S) intersects S. It does not say S union sigma(S) is connected. In the proof discussion, elliptic components are specifically stabilized by Z/4, but Case 3 is not stated as such a stabilized elliptic component.**

**Aspect ratio under sigma:**  
**Cyclic relabeling swaps which side is “first” and “second,” so rho typically transforms to 1/rho. If S and sigma(S) belong to the same connected continuum, rho would connect r to 1/r and force rho=1 by IVT. But that continuum is not established.**

**Failure mode:**  
**Same-continuum membership is missing.**

**Status:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED:**

* **sigma preserves I(gamma) and G(gamma).**  
* **sigma preserves the cyclic-order component in the Z/4 sense.**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE:**

* **sigma(S) intersection S not established.**  
* **S union sigma(S) connected not established.**  
* **connected sigma-closed replacement preserving Case-3 hypotheses not established.**

**Next computation:**  
**Sigma-Closure Lemma:**  
**Given Case-3 S, prove that S and sigma(S) lie in a connected subset S\* of G(gamma) with small-diameter and coverage properties preserved. If true, rho crossing follows. If false, construct a Case-3-compatible continuum whose sigma images remain separated.**

**TASK 8 — ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE**

**Schwartz Case-3 S.**  
**Conclusion:**

**Mechanism sought:**  
**Upgrade weak coverage to small-diameter coverage.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Weak coverage may be provided by large rectangles while small rectangles cluster near one point.**  
**Satisfaction:**  
**For all epsilon\>0, V\_\<epsilon contains gamma minus at most two points.**  
**Falsification:**

1. **Highest value, highest dependency burden.**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Schwartz only gives existence of some connected S, not symmetry-stabilized S.**  
**Satisfaction:**

**Falsification:**  
**Separated components or no connected sigma-closed replacement.**

**2\.**

**Why it might fail:**

**Mechanism:**

**Why it might fail:**  
**Abstract model may not be realizable by a Jordan loop.**  
**Rank:**

**Square angle included.**  
**Mechanism:**  
**Measure/interval upgrade.**

**Rank:**  
**5\.**

**Selected attack for immediate pursuit:**  
**Attack 4 — Abstract One-Sided Model / Falsification of Inference.**

**Reason:**  
**It produces an immediate concrete computation and tests whether the Blow-Up Role Theorem follows from the currently available Case-3 data alone. It does not require unverified new literature or hidden regularity.**

**TASK 8 SELECTED ATTACK — ONE-SIDED MODEL CANDIDATE**

**Goal:**  
**Construct an abstract model satisfying the formal Case-3-style data while Blow\_S(p) is nonempty only at one point and rho avoids 1\.**

**Construction:**  
**Let base gamma be an abstract circle parameter q in S1.**

**Let S\_abs \= (0,1\] with parameter t.**

**Define diam(t):**  
**diam(t)=t for 0\<t\<=1/3.**  
**diam(t)=1/3 for 1/3\<=t\<=1.**

**Define aspect ratio rho(t)=1/2 for all t.**  
**Thus rho(S\_abs) avoids 1 and is bounded away from 1\.**

**Define vertex coverage map abstractly:**  
**For t in (0,1/3\], all four vertices lie within distance t of a fixed point p0 on gamma.**  
**For t in \[1/3,1\], the rectangle family is assigned so that as t varies, the four vertex maps sweep the full circle gamma.**

**This model has:**

1. **S\_abs connected.**  
2. **Rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
3. **rho avoids 1\.**  
4. **Weak vertex coverage all of gamma.**  
5. **Strong degeneration coverage only at p0.**  
6. **Blow\_S(p0) nonempty.**  
7. **Blow\_S(p) empty for p \!= p0.**

**Interpretation:**  
**The model is not claimed to be geometrically realizable as graceful rectangles of a Jordan loop. It is an abstract incidence/diameter/aspect-ratio model showing that the logical data “connected \+ small diameters somewhere \+ all-but-two weak coverage \+ one-sided rho” do not by themselves imply a global nonempty blow-up field.**

**Failure mode of stronger inference:**  
**Any proof that Case 3 forces global Blow\_S(p) nonemptiness must use additional geometry of G(gamma), not merely the formal trichotomy data.**

**Status:**  
**ONE-SIDED MODEL CANDIDATE CONSTRUCTED.**  
**INTERNALLY GENERATED ABSTRACT MODEL.**  
**NOT A JORDAN-LOOP COUNTEREXAMPLE.**  
**NOT A REFUTATION OF BLOW-UP ROLE THEOREM.**  
**Valid as a falsification of an overstrong inference from weak coverage to strong degeneration coverage.**

**TASK 9 — OUTCOME CLASSIFICATION**

**Chosen outcome:**  
**5\. ONE-SIDED MODEL CANDIDATE CONSTRUCTED.**

**Meaning:**  
**This traversal did not prove or refute the Blow-Up Role Theorem. It did construct a precise abstract model candidate showing that the available Case-3 data are insufficient to force a nonempty upper-semicontinuous nonsquare blow-up field over gamma minus at most two points. The next proof attempt must exploit stronger geometry of Schwartz’s G(gamma), not just the trichotomy statement.**

16. **INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

**Rule name: Weak-to-Strong Coverage Gate**

**Exact text:**

**“Whenever a traversal uses a coverage statement over all rectangles in a family to infer coverage by arbitrarily small, degenerating, limiting, or scale-filtered rectangles, it must introduce a separate strong-coverage lemma. Weak vertex coverage, global incidence coverage, or existence of small objects somewhere never implies strong degeneration coverage without proof.”**

**Failure mode prevented: invalid promotion from V(gamma,S) to D or Blow\_S nonemptiness.**

**Scope: topology, geometry, compactness, blow-up, degeneration, and limit-field arguments.**

**Limitation: does not say strong coverage is false; it only requires proof.**

**Rule name: Abstract Model Labeling Rule**

**Exact text:**

**“Any model that does not realize the declared geometric object class must be labeled as an abstract incidence/logical/diagnostic model. It may falsify an inference from stated data alone, but it must not be entered into continuity state as a geometric counterexample, theorem refutation, or construction inside the original object class.”**

**Failure mode prevented: accidental upgrade of abstract model to Jordan-loop counterexample.**

**Scope: all DST model/countermodel constructions.**

**Limitation: abstract models remain useful for detecting missing hypotheses.**

**Rule name: Monodromy Formalization Gate**

**Exact text:**

**“A traversal may not use monodromy, transport, holonomy, orientation obstruction, or parity obstruction as a forcing mechanism unless it defines the base, fiber, correspondence or bundle, transport/selection rule, sign or orientation datum, obstruction class, and same-continuum compatibility. Otherwise the route must be labeled metaphorical, heuristic, or not formalized.”**

**Failure mode prevented: rhetorical monodromy.**

**Scope: all topology and geometric obstruction routes.**

**Limitation: permits monodromy as an attack target.**

# **1\. ABSTRACT**

**This traversal formalizes and attacks the Blow-Up Role Theorem arising from the Schwartz parabolic residue for graceful rectangles on a continuous Jordan curve.**

**Main result of this traversal:**

**Blow\_S^j(p) can be defined cleanly, role-by-role, without smoothness. With empty values allowed, the set-valued field p \-\> Blow\_S^j(p) has compact values and closed graph; therefore it satisfies upper-semicontinuity in the compact-valued / empty-allowed sense.**

**However, this does not prove the Blow-Up Role Theorem and does not prove T\_strong.**

**The blocking gap is not definability or upper-semicontinuity. The blocking gap is coverage strength:**

**Schwartz Case 3 gives weak vertex coverage: all but at most two points of gamma are vertices of some rectangle in S.**

**It does not, by itself, give strong degeneration coverage: all or almost all points are limits of vertices of rectangles in S whose diameters go to zero.**

**Thus the blow-up field can be defined, but the intake’s central forcing question remains blocked because the field may be empty on most of gamma unless a new Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma is proved.**

**Outcome classification: HELD — NEXT COMPUTATION NAMED.**

**Exact next computation: Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma.**

---

# **2\. FRONTIER AND SOURCE CHECK**

## **2.1 Intake state**

**The intake explicitly states that the v1.5 traversal did not prove T\_strong, did not nullify Schwartz Case 3, did not construct a parabolic-only Jordan curve, and generated the Blow-Up Role Theorem as the next attack target.**

**The intake requires definition of Xbar, G(gamma), S, rho, ShapeRect, Blow\_S(p), the domain D, and exceptional sets, and it forbids treating weak vertex coverage as strong degeneration coverage without proof.**

## **2.2 Schwartz source check**

**External source check located Schwartz’s paper “A Trichotomy for Rectangles Inscribed in Jordan Loops.” The source states that G(gamma) is the space of gracefully inscribed labeled rectangles, where the cyclic order from gamma agrees with the rectangle’s vertex order. It states Theorem 1.1: for any Jordan loop gamma, I(gamma) contains a connected set S satisfying one of three alternatives. Case 3 says S has members of every sufficiently small diameter and V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma. Schwartz also states that he conjectures the parabolic case cannot occur and that this conjecture would imply the Square Peg Conjecture. ([math.brown.edu](https://www.math.brown.edu/~res/Papers/sweepout.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

**Tier classification:**

* **Schwartz trichotomy statement: EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED — citation/source text located for traversal use.**  
* **DST translation from Schwartz G(gamma) to G\_rect(gamma) intersect C4+(gamma): USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A, because notation translation still requires public-release-level checking.**  
* **Schwartz conjecture that Case 3 cannot occur: REPORTED IN LITERATURE — PROVISIONAL — not a theorem.**  
* **General Toeplitz problem remains open for continuous Jordan curves: EXTERNALLY ESTABLISHED as background; current sources still identify it as open. ([Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inscribed_square_problem?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

---

# **3\. DEFINITIONS FIXED**

## **3.1 Gamma and cyclic configuration space**

**Let gamma: S1 \-\> R2 be a continuous injective parametrization of a Jordan curve.**

**Define Xbar \= S1 x Delta3, where Delta3 consists of gap vectors**

**g \= (g1,g2,g3,g4), gi \>= 0, sum gi \= 1\.**

**For x \= (t,g), define cyclic parameters:**

**t1 \= t**  
**t2 \= t \+ g1**  
**t3 \= t \+ g1 \+ g2**  
**t4 \= t \+ g1 \+ g2 \+ g3**

**all modulo 1\.**

**Define vi(x) \= gamma(ti).**

**The interior C4+(gamma) corresponds to all gi \> 0\. The boundary of Xbar corresponds to collisions of consecutive cyclic parameters.**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

## **3.2 Graceful rectangle locus**

**G(gamma) is the subset of C4+(gamma) consisting of configurations x such that v1,v2,v3,v4 form a genuine Euclidean rectangle and the cyclic vertex order inherited from gamma agrees with the rectangle vertex order.**

**Status: USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A for Schwartz translation.**

## **3.3 Case-3 connected set**

**S is a connected subset of G(gamma) satisfying Schwartz Case 3:**

1. **S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
2. **V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**  
3. **S is graceful.**  
4. **In the parabolic residue setting, rho(S) avoids 1\.**

**Status: USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A, with exact source wording externally checked for the trichotomy but notation translation still requiring public-level audit.**

## **3.4 Aspect ratio**

**For R in G(gamma), define rho(R) as second side length divided by first side length, using the Schwartz labeling convention. The square target is rho \= 1\.**

**Since S is connected and rho is continuous on genuine rectangles, rho(S) is connected. If rho(S) avoids 1, then rho(S) lies entirely in (0,1) or entirely in (1,infinity).**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED, conditional on the labeling convention.**

## **3.5 ShapeRect**

**For a labeled rectangle R \= (v1,v2,v3,v4), define diam(R) as max |vi-vk|.**

**For a chosen role j in {1,2,3,4}, define the normalized anchored shape:**

**N\_j(R) \= ((v1-vj)/diam(R), ..., (v4-vj)/diam(R)) in (R2)^4.**

**Then N\_j(R) has j-th coordinate 0 and total diameter 1\.**

**Define ShapeRect\_j as the closure in (R2)^4 of all such normalized anchored shapes arising from genuine labeled rectangles.**

**Because all coordinates lie in the closed unit disk and the diameter is normalized to 1, ShapeRect\_j is compact.**

**Degenerate limiting shapes are included. Full collapse is excluded by diameter normalization, but flat/segment-like limits from aspect ratio tending to 0 or infinity are included.**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

---

# **4\. DEFINITION OF Blow\_S^j(p)**

**For p in gamma(S1), define Blow\_S^j(p) as the set of all Q in ShapeRect\_j such that there exists a sequence R\_n in S satisfying:**

1. **diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\.**  
2. **The j-th vertex v\_j(R\_n) \-\> p.**  
3. **N\_j(R\_n) \-\> Q in ShapeRect\_j.**

**Define D\_j \= {p in gamma(S1): Blow\_S^j(p) is nonempty}.**

**Define the role-union field:**

**Blow\_S(p) \= union over j of Blow\_S^j(p).**

**Define D \= union over j of D\_j.**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

**Important distinction:**

* **Weak coverage: p is a vertex of at least one rectangle in S.**  
* **Strong degeneration coverage: p is a limit of role-j vertices of rectangles R\_n in S with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\.**

**Weak coverage does not imply strong degeneration coverage. The intake explicitly forbids that inference.**

---

# **5\. NONEMPTINESS / COVERAGE ANALYSIS**

**Schwartz Case 3 gives:**

* **For every sufficiently small epsilon \> 0, there exists at least one R in S with diam(R) \< epsilon.**  
* **V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**It does not give:**

* **For every p outside an exceptional set, there exists a sequence R\_n in S with diam(R\_n)-\>0 and some vertex tending to p.**  
* **For every p outside an exceptional set, there exists a fixed role j with v\_j(R\_n)-\>p.**  
* **That the small-diameter part of S has vertex coverage comparable to V(gamma,S).**

**What can be proved:**

**Since S has rectangles of arbitrarily small diameter, choose R\_n in S with diam(R\_n)-\>0. The compactness of gamma implies that, after passing to a subsequence, each role sequence v\_j(R\_n) has a convergent subsequence. Therefore D is nonempty.**

**What cannot be proved from Case 3 alone:**

**D contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Therefore the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma is not established.**

**Status:**

* **Blow-up nonemptiness somewhere: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**  
* **All-but-two blow-up nonemptiness: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**  
* **Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE / PRIMARY NEXT ATTACK.**

---

# **6\. UPPER-SEMICONTINUITY TEST**

**Claim:**

**For each role j, the graph**

**Graph\_j \= {(p,Q): Q in Blow\_S^j(p)}**

**is closed in gamma(S1) x ShapeRect\_j.**

**Proof:**

**Let (p\_k,Q\_k) be a sequence in Graph\_j with p\_k \-\> p and Q\_k \-\> Q.**

**For each k, because Q\_k is in Blow\_S^j(p\_k), there exists a sequence R\_{k,m} in S such that:**

**diam(R\_{k,m}) \-\> 0,**  
**v\_j(R\_{k,m}) \-\> p\_k,**  
**N\_j(R\_{k,m}) \-\> Q\_k.**

**Choose m(k) large enough that:**

**diam(R\_{k,m(k)}) \< 1/k,**  
**|v\_j(R\_{k,m(k)}) \- p\_k| \< 1/k,**  
**dist(N\_j(R\_{k,m(k)}), Q\_k) \< 1/k.**

**Then the diagonal sequence R\_k \= R\_{k,m(k)} satisfies:**

**diam(R\_k) \-\> 0,**  
**v\_j(R\_k) \-\> p,**  
**N\_j(R\_k) \-\> Q.**

**Therefore Q belongs to Blow\_S^j(p). Hence Graph\_j is closed.**

**Since ShapeRect\_j is compact and Blow\_S^j(p) is a closed subset of ShapeRect\_j, each value is compact, possibly empty.**

**Thus p \-\> Blow\_S^j(p) is upper-semicontinuous in the compact-valued, empty-allowed sense.**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

**Limitation:**

**This upper-semicontinuity does not imply nonempty fibers. It gives control only where the field exists or where limits of existing fibers force existence.**

**Therefore upper-semicontinuity does not close the Blow-Up Role Theorem.**

---

# **7\. ONE-SIDED NONSQUARE FIELD ANALYSIS**

**Assume rho(S) avoids 1\.**

**Because S is connected and rho is continuous, rho(S) lies on one side of 1\.**

## **Case 1: rho bounded away from 1**

**If there exists eta \> 0 such that |rho(R)-1| \>= eta for all R in S, then all nondegenerate blow-up shapes remain nonsquare by a uniform margin.**

**Outcome:**

**No contradiction follows. A consistent one-sided nonsquare blow-up field remains possible wherever the field is nonempty.**

**Status: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

## **Case 2: rho approaches 1 only at degeneration**

**If rho(R\_n)-\>1 along diam(R\_n)-\>0, then Blow\_S^j(p) may contain square-shaped normalized limits even though no finite R\_n is a square.**

**This gives an infinitesimal square-shape limit, not a genuine square on gamma.**

**Without tangents, local monotonicity, rectifiability, or a compactness theorem converting infinitesimal square-shape limits into positive-scale square configurations, this does not prove T\_strong.**

**Status: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

## **Case 3: escape to degeneration / loss of normalization**

**Diameter normalization prevents full collapse in ShapeRect\_j, but aspect-ratio escape to 0 or infinity can produce degenerate segment-like shapes.**

**These degenerate normalized limits can exist consistently in ShapeRect\_j.**

**No contradiction follows without an additional theorem excluding degenerate limit shapes or forcing recurrence to a nondegenerate square shape.**

**Status: OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Conclusion:**

**The one-sided invariant split does not force a square. It isolates exactly what would be needed:**

**A theorem showing that Case-3 one-sided behavior either gives all-but-two nonempty blow-up fibers with incompatible orientation data, or forces rho approaching 1 in a way that lifts from infinitesimal normalized limits to genuine positive-scale squares.**

**No such theorem is supplied here.**

---

# **8\. MONODROMY / OBSTRUCTION FORMALIZATION**

**Attempted objects:**

* **Base space: candidate base would be gamma minus exceptional set E, or D\_j if strong coverage were established.**  
* **Fiber: ShapeRect\_j or one-sided nonsquare component of ShapeRect\_j.**  
* **Transition/correspondence: would need a canonical way to transport local blow-up shapes along gamma.**  
* **Orientation/sign datum: would need a well-defined side/role/long-short assignment stable under transport.**  
* **Obstruction class: would need a parity, winding, or holonomy class proving nonclosure.**

**Failure:**

**The required base with nonempty fibers is not established, because strong degeneration coverage is missing. Even on D\_j, no canonical transport or correspondence between fibers has been constructed. Without transport, monodromy remains metaphorical.**

**Therefore:**

**MONODROMY NOT FORMALIZED.**

**Status: MONODROMY ROUTE BLOCKED FOR CURRENT DATA.**

**This is not a proof that monodromy cannot later be formalized. It is blocked under the current data.**

---

# **9\. SYMMETRY AND SAME-CONTINUUM CHECK**

## **9.1 Does sigma preserve G(gamma)?**

**Cyclic relabeling preserves the geometric rectangle condition. Under the graceful convention, sigma should preserve G(gamma) if the cyclic order is shifted without reversing orientation.**

**Status: USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A, pending public-level notation verification.**

## **9.2 Does sigma preserve C4+(gamma)?**

**A cyclic shift of a positively cyclically ordered quadruple remains positively cyclically ordered.**

**Status: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED.**

## **9.3 Does sigma(S) intersect S?**

**Not established.**

## **9.4 Is S union sigma(S) connected?**

**Not established.**

## **9.5 Can a connected sigma-closed replacement continuum be built?**

**Not from current data. The union over sigma-orbit of S may be disconnected. Even if connectedness were forced after taking a closure or chain, it is not established that the replacement would preserve the relevant Case-3 hypotheses or rho-avoidance.**

**Conclusion:**

**Direct sigma relabeling cannot force rho-crossing inside S without one of the following:**

1. **S intersects sigma(S).**  
2. **S union sigma(S) is connected.**  
3. **A connected sigma-closed continuum exists preserving Case-3 hypotheses.**  
4. **A separate theorem forces reciprocal aspect ratios within the same connected continuum.**

**Status: SYMMETRY ROUTE BLOCKED FOR CURRENT DATA.**

# **10\. ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE**

## **Attack 1 — Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma**

**Target:**

**Prove that in Schwartz Case 3, for all but at most two points p in gamma, at least one role j has Blow\_S^j(p) nonempty.**

**Why it would close major residue:**

**It would promote weak vertex coverage to a real blow-up field over almost all of gamma. Then upper-semicontinuity and one-sided shape constraints become globally usable.**

**Current status:**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Rank: 1\.**

## **Attack 2 — Small-rectangle vertex-coverage refinement**

**Target:**

**For every epsilon \> 0, define S\_epsilon \= {R in S: diam(R)\<epsilon}. Prove that V(gamma,S\_epsilon) contains all but a controlled exceptional set independent of epsilon, or that the intersection of closures over epsilon retains all-but-two coverage.**

**Why it may work:**

**It is the exact missing bridge between Schwartz Case 3 and Blow\_S(p).**

**Current status:**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Rank: 2\.**

## **Attack 3 — Sigma-closure continuum theorem**

**Target:**

**Prove S can be replaced by a connected continuum S\* containing S and sigma(S), with rho(S\*) still avoiding 1 or else producing a square.**

**Why it may work:**

**If S\* is connected and contains reciprocal aspect-ratio data, IVT on rho may force rho \= 1\.**

**Current status:**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Rank: 3\.**

## **Attack 4 — Degenerate square-lift theorem**

**Target:**

**If normalized blow-up shapes approach square shape at a point p, prove existence of positive-scale square configurations nearby.**

**Why it may fail:**

**For merely continuous Jordan curves, infinitesimal shape limits need not lift to genuine positive-scale square configurations without extra regularity.**

**Current status:**

**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Rank: 4\.**

## **Attack 5 — Monodromy obstruction theorem**

**Target:**

**Construct a base, nonempty fibers, transport, sign datum, and obstruction class for a one-sided nonsquare blow-up field.**

**Why it may work:**

**A globally consistent one-sided long/short assignment around a closed curve may carry parity obstruction.**

**Why it currently fails:**

**No nonempty base/fiber field over almost all gamma has been established.**

**Current status:**

**BLOCKED UNTIL STRONG DEGENERATION COVERAGE.**

**Rank: 5\.**

---

# **11\. SELECTED ATTACK PURSUED NOW**

**Selected attack: Attack 1 / Attack 2 combined.**

## **Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma — formal target**

**Let S be a connected Case-3 graceful-rectangle set. For each epsilon \> 0, define**

**A\_epsilon \= union over roles j of {v\_j(R): R in S and diam(R)\<epsilon}.**

**Weak Case-3 coverage says:**

**V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points.**

**Strong degeneration coverage would say:**

**intersection over epsilon\>0 of closure(A\_epsilon) contains all but at most two points.**

**Equivalently, for all but at most two p, p belongs to D.**

## **Attempt**

**Because S is connected and contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter, the diameter map d: S \-\> (0,infinity) is continuous and has values arbitrarily close to 0\.**

**For any R0 in S and any sequence R\_n with diam(R\_n)-\>0, connectedness gives continua in S joining R0 to R\_n. Along those continua, diameter passes through all intermediate values.**

**This proves:**

**For every sufficiently small epsilon and for every R0 in S with diam(R0)\>epsilon, there is at least one rectangle in S of diameter epsilon on a connected path from R0 to a smaller rectangle.**

**But it does not prove:**

**The vertices of these small rectangles approach the same parts of gamma as the vertices of R0.**

**The vertex map V\_j: S \-\> gamma is continuous for each role j, but connectedness of S only implies that V\_j of a connecting continuum is connected in gamma. It does not imply that the small-diameter sublevel S\_epsilon has vertex image covering the same points as S.**

**Therefore the attack stalls at the following precise obstruction:**

**Sublevel vertex coverage is not inherited from total vertex coverage.**

**To prove the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma, one must show that the small-diameter sublevel sets S\_epsilon cannot concentrate their vertices on a proper subset of gamma while the larger-diameter portions of S supply the remaining weak coverage.**

**No such argument is produced here.**

**Status:**

**Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma remains OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

**Attack result:**

**HELD — NEXT COMPUTATION NAMED.**

---

**intersection over epsilon\>0 of closure(V(gamma, S\_epsilon))**

**contains all but at most two points of gamma,**

**where S\_epsilon \= {R in S: diam(R)\<epsilon}.**

**If this is false, construct a geometric or abstract countermodel showing weak coverage can be carried entirely by non-small rectangles while arbitrarily small rectangles concentrate near a smaller subset.**

1. **PUBLIC RELEASE STATUS**

**JURY-READY AS OPEN-RESIDUE / SUBLEVEL-COVERAGE TRAVERSAL ONLY**

**The submitted traversal is not a proof of T\_strong, not a nullification of Schwartz Case 3, not a proof of the Blow-Up Role Theorem, not a proof of the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma, and not a refutation of the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma.**

**It is a sharpened open-residue traversal and frontier map. Its chief value is the reduction of the live obstruction to the sublevel vertex-coverage question:**

**For S\_epsilon \= {R in S : diam(R) \< epsilon},**  
**determine whether intersection over epsilon \> 0 of closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon))**  
**contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**This is jury-ready only under the limitation that it reports an active attack and open residue, not a proof result.**

2. **INTAKE ALIGNMENT AUDIT**

**SUFFICIENT WITH RELABELING**

**The heading still says “Blow-Up Role Theorem Program,” but the actual traversal substantially targets Strong Degeneration Coverage. The mismatch matters for record hygiene but does not block jury-ready status.**

**The traversal preserves the Blow\_S background because the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma arose from the Blow-Up Role program. That reuse is legitimate, provided the continuity state labels this cycle as:**

**Toeplitz / Strong Degeneration Coverage Sublevel Traversal**

**rather than as a completed Blow-Up Role theorem traversal.**

**The uploaded jury prompt itself asks the juror to assess whether this mismatch blocks jury-ready status or only requires relabeling; my verdict is relabeling only.**

3. **CORE VERDICT**

**The traversal satisfies active-attack and conduct requirements.**

**It performed frontier/source initialization, preserved the active continuity state, defined or preserved S, G(gamma), rho, Blow\_S^j(p), ShapeRect\_j, V(gamma,S), S\_epsilon, V(gamma,S\_epsilon), and D. It clearly separated weak vertex coverage from strong degeneration coverage. It tested upper-semicontinuity rather than assuming it. It refused to formalize monodromy without base, fibers, transport, and obstruction data. It checked same-continuum symmetry rather than assuming sigma-related data live in the same connected S.**

**Most importantly, it did not merely name the Strong Degeneration Coverage Lemma. It translated the problem into sublevel vertex coverage, attempted a connectedness/diameter-map argument, identified exactly what the argument proves, and isolated the failure mode:**

**Sublevel vertex coverage is not inherited from total vertex coverage.**

**That satisfies active-attack standards for this cycle.**

4. **BLOCKING DEFECTS**

**NONE for jury-ready open-residue status.**

**Blocking defects for public release remain, but they do not block use as the next DST continuity input.**

**Public-release blockers:**

**The translation from Schwartz’s notation to the DST configuration-space notation remains provisional.**

**The precise meaning of “members of every sufficiently small diameter” must be checked against Schwartz’s theorem/proof language.**

**Whether S is connected only, compact, closed, continuum-valued, or proof-constructed with stronger structure must be verified.**

**None of these defects invalidate the traversal’s status as an open-residue attack map because the traversal explicitly demotes those points to verification requirements.**

5. **SUBLEVEL COVERAGE FORMULATION AUDIT**

**CORRECT WITH MINOR REFORMULATION**

**The definition**

**S\_epsilon \= {R in S : diam(R) \< epsilon}**

**is correct and useful.**

**The definition of**

**V(gamma,S\_epsilon)**

**as the vertex image of the small-diameter part of S is the right object.**

**The traversal’s proposed target**

**intersection over epsilon \> 0 of closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon))**  
**contains all but at most two points of gamma**

**correctly captures role-unlabeled strong degeneration coverage.**

**Minor reformulation needed:**

**The traversal should distinguish the role-union version from role-fixed Blow\_S^j nonemptiness.**

**The sublevel condition gives:**

**p is a limit of vertices of arbitrarily small rectangles in S.**

**This is equivalent to nonemptiness of the role-union Blow\_S(p), after passing to a subsequence and one of four roles, because only finitely many roles exist. It is not equivalent to preselecting a fixed role j uniformly over all p unless that role stabilization is explicitly extracted.**

**Thus:**

**intersection\_epsilon closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon)) all-but-two**

**is equivalent to all-but-two nonemptiness of the role-union blow-up field Blow\_S(p), not immediately to all-but-two nonemptiness of each Blow\_S^j(p).**

**The formulation is the right next mathematical object.**

6. **CONNECTEDNESS / DIAMETER-MAP ATTACK AUDIT**

**CORRECTLY EXECUTED AND CORRECTLY BLOCKED**

**The traversal correctly observes that diam:S \-\> (0,infinity) is continuous on S, assuming S is given as a subset of genuine rectangles with the inherited topology.**

**Connectedness of S implies the diameter image is connected.**

**If S contains rectangles of arbitrarily small diameter and also contains a rectangle of larger diameter, then connectedness gives intermediate diameter values in the image.**

**But this gives no automatic control over vertex images of the sublevel sets S\_epsilon.**

**The traversal correctly identifies the obstruction:**

**The vertex map V\_j:S \-\> gamma is continuous, but connectedness of S only implies connectedness of vertex images of connected pieces. It does not imply that small-diameter sublevels carry the same vertex coverage as S.**

**No stronger conclusion follows from plain connectedness alone. To get stronger coverage, the next cycle must inspect Schwartz’s construction or add a new hypothesis.**

7. **Blow\_S^j(p) / USC BACKGROUND AUDIT**

**CORRECTLY PRESERVED BACKGROUND**

**The traversal correctly defines role-labeled Blow\_S^j(p) by anchoring at role j and normalizing by diameter.**

**ShapeRect\_j compactness is correctly scoped as closure inside a bounded finite-dimensional product space after diameter normalization.**

**Closed graph / upper-semicontinuity is correctly treated as empty-valued allowed. The traversal does not commit the common error of treating USC as implying nonempty fibers.**

**This section is necessary background because the live Strong Degeneration Coverage question asks whether the blow-up field has enough nonempty fibers to become useful. It is not merely padding.**

8. **ONE-SIDED / MONODROMY / SYMMETRY AUDIT**

**A. One-sided nonsquare field analysis: CORRECTLY PRESERVED AS BLOCKED / HELD**

**The traversal correctly states that rho(S) avoiding 1 and lying on one side of 1 does not itself force a contradiction.**

**B. Monodromy route: CORRECTLY PRESERVED AS BLOCKED / HELD**

**The traversal correctly labels monodromy as not formalized. Without a nonempty base of fibers, transport, sign datum, and obstruction class, monodromy remains metaphorical.**

**C. Sigma preserving G(gamma) and C4+(gamma): CORRECTLY PRESERVED AS PROVISIONAL / HELD**

**Sigma preserving C4+(gamma) is internally plausible. Sigma preserving Schwartz’s exact G(gamma) requires notation verification and is correctly marked provisional.**

**D. Same-continuum obstruction: CORRECTLY PRESERVED AS BLOCKED / HELD**

**The traversal correctly refuses to infer rho-crossing from sigma(S) unless S intersects sigma(S), S union sigma(S) is connected, a connected sigma-closed replacement exists, or another theorem supplies reciprocal ratios inside the same connected continuum.**

**E. Should these routes have been pursued more deeply? NO**

**They were correctly subordinated to sublevel coverage. Strong degeneration coverage is now the primary missing base condition for making blow-up/monodromy arguments meaningful.**

15. **INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

**Rule name: Sublevel Coverage Non-Inheritance Rule**

**Exact text:**

**Do not infer coverage by small-scale or degenerating subfamilies from coverage by the total family. Whenever a theorem supplies V(gamma,S) coverage and the argument needs coverage by S\_epsilon \= {R in S : scale(R) \< epsilon}, the traversal must introduce a separate sublevel-coverage lemma, prove it, cite it, or leave it as open residue.**

**Failure mode prevented:**

**Weak total-coverage data being silently promoted into strong degeneration coverage.**

**Scope:**

**All DST traversals involving compactness, blow-up, degeneration, scale sublevels, or limiting fields.**

**Limitation:**

**This rule does not assert sublevel coverage is false; it only blocks unproved promotion.**

**Rule name: Role-Union / Fixed-Role Separation Rule**

**Exact text:**

**When a blow-up or degeneration field has finitely many labeled roles, distinguish fixed-role nonemptiness from role-union nonemptiness. A role-union sequence may yield a fixed role only after subsequence extraction, and the target statement must say whether the role may depend on the point or must be uniform.**

**Failure mode prevented:**

**Ambiguity between Blow\_S(p) nonemptiness and Blow\_S^j(p) nonemptiness.**

**Scope:**

**Role-labeled configuration-space traversals.**

**Limitation:**

**Finite-role subsequence extraction may bridge the gap in many cases, but it must be stated.**

**Rule name: Theorem Statement / Proof Construction Split**

**Exact text:**

**When a theorem statement is insufficient to decide a live DST residue, the traversal must distinguish theorem-statement consequences from proof-construction consequences. It may not assume that the constructed object has stronger properties than the published statement supplies unless the proof construction is inspected and cited.**

**Failure mode prevented:**

**Importing hidden structure from an external theorem without proof-level verification.**

**Scope:**

**All traversals relying on external literature.**

**Limitation:**

**Does not require full literature reconstruction unless the hidden structure is material to the active residue.**
