**DST TRAVERSAL — TOEPLITZ / SCHWARTZ PROOF-STRUCTURE REVIEW FOR STRONG DEGENERATION COVERAGE**

**Status:**  
**JURY-SUBMISSION READY AS SOURCE-PROOF RESIDUE TRAVERSAL.**  
**NOT PUBLIC-READY.**  
**NOT A PROOF OF T\_STRONG.**  
**NOT A NULLIFICATION OF SCHWARTZ CASE 3\.**  
**NOT A PROOF OR REFUTATION OF STRONG DEGENERATION COVERAGE.**  
**NOT A JORDAN-LOOP COUNTEREXAMPLE.**

**OUTCOME CLASSIFICATION**

**Chosen Task 8 classification:**

4. **SCHWARTZ PROOF DOES NOT SUPPLY SUBLEVEL COVERAGE — SOURCE RESIDUE CERTIFIED.**

**Precise scope:**  
**This traversal inspected the accessible Schwartz source text and found that the Case 3 proof supplies weak all-but-two vertex coverage for the full connected/extensive set A, together with small-diameter existence somewhere in A, but does not supply a mechanism tying small-diameter rectangles to all-but-two vertex coverage at the sublevel sets A\_epsilon or S\_epsilon.**

**Route status:**  
**ROUTE EXHAUSTED FOR proving Strong Degeneration Coverage from the inspected Schwartz proof passages as written, namely Theorem 1.1, Lemma 2.3, Lemma 2.6, Lemma 2.7, and the Case 3 paragraph of Section 2.6.**

**Not exhausted:**  
**A new theorem using additional geometry of graceful rectangles, a strengthened reading from another version of the source, or an independent sublevel-coverage lemma remains open.**

1. **SOURCE ACQUISITION AND SCOPE**

**Source acquired:**  
**Richard Evan Schwartz, “A Trichotomy for Rectangles Inscribed in Jordan Loops,” PDF hosted on Brown University’s math site, dated February 6, 2020\. The PDF text was accessible and inspected. Schwartz defines I(gamma) as labeled inscribed rectangles, labels rectangle vertices counterclockwise, orients gamma counterclockwise, defines graceful rectangles as those whose cyclic order on gamma coincides with the rectangle ordering, and defines G(gamma) as the space of gracefully inscribed labeled rectangles.**

**Theorem statement located:**  
**Theorem 1.1 states that for every Jordan loop gamma, I(gamma) contains a connected set S satisfying one of three alternatives, with Case 3 saying S has members of every sufficiently small diameter and V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma; moreover S is contained in G(gamma).**

**Proof passages located:**  
**The proof reduces the trichotomy from generic polygonal approximations and global components; Schwartz states that Theorem 1.7 is obtained for generic polygons and that Theorem 1.1 follows by taking a suitable limit. The relevant Case 3 proof passage says the remaining case is that Gamma contains an extensive set A without a positive lower diameter bound; Lemma 2.3 then gives all-but-two vertex coverage, and the absence of the positive lower bound gives members of every sufficiently small diameter.**

**Source-access status:**  
**SOURCE ACCESS SUFFICIENT FOR THIS TRAVERSAL’S DECLARED PURPOSE.**  
**Not public-ready because a full publication-version comparison and page-stable citation verification remain required.**

2. **DEFINITIONS FIXED**

**I(gamma):**  
**Schwartz’s space of all labeled rectangles inscribed in gamma. He labels rectangles so their vertices go counterclockwise around the rectangle.**

**G(gamma):**  
**Schwartz’s graceful rectangle space, consisting of labeled inscribed rectangles whose rectangle-vertex cyclic order matches the cyclic order induced by gamma.**

**V(gamma,S):**  
**For S subset I(gamma), V(gamma,S) is the subset of gamma consisting of points that occur as vertices of rectangles in S.**

**Circular quadrilateral space Sigma:**  
**Schwartz defines Sigma as distinct labeled quadruples on S1 going counterclockwise around S1, with arcs alpha\_k between successive vertices.**

**Circular invariant Lambda:**  
**Schwartz defines Lambda(sigma) \= (|alpha\_0| \+ |alpha\_2|) / (|alpha\_1| \+ |alpha\_3|), and says that when sigma is the vertices of a rectangle, Lambda is the rectangle’s aspect ratio.**

**Extensive set:**  
**Schwartz defines A subset Sigma as extensive if A is connected and Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity).**

**S in Case 3:**  
**In the Case 2/3 proof, Schwartz obtains an extensive set A contained in Gamma, then lets S subset G(gamma) be the rectangle set corresponding to A.**

**S\_epsilon:**  
**For this traversal, S\_epsilon \= {R in S : diam(R) \< epsilon}. On the Sigma side, write A\_epsilon for the corresponding cyclic quadrilaterals whose associated rectangles have diameter \< epsilon.**

3. **THEOREM STATEMENT / PROOF CONSTRUCTION SPLIT**

**Ledger item: S exists.**

**Theorem statement:**  
**There is a connected set S subset G(gamma) satisfying one of the three alternatives. In Case 3, S has members of every sufficiently small diameter and V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Proof construction:**  
**Case 3 starts with Gamma containing an extensive set A without a positive lower diameter bound. S is the subset of G(gamma) corresponding to A. Lemma 2.3 supplies all-but-two coverage from extensiveness plus arbitrarily small diameter; the “small diameter” clause is then transferred from A to S.**

**Traversal finding:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED: the proof construction gives A extensive and no positive lower diameter bound, but the proof passage does not define or analyze A\_epsilon, S\_epsilon, or vertex coverage restricted to those sublevel sets.**

**Ledger item: Connectedness.**

**Theorem statement:**  
**S is connected.**

**Proof construction:**  
**A is built as a nested union of connected Hausdorff limits A(K) in the hyperbolic case; nested union connectedness gives A connected. In the wobbly elliptic case, the same proof works after showing the approximating sets have circular invariants 1/n and n.**

**Traversal finding:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED: the construction gives connected A. It does not give path-connectedness in the limit. Schwartz’s own preliminary lemma remarks that path-connected approximants can have a connected limit that is not path-connected.**

**Ledger item: Diameter.**

**Theorem statement:**  
**Case 3 says S has members of every sufficiently small diameter.**

**Proof construction:**  
**The proof describes Case 3 as the remaining case where A lacks a uniform positive lower diameter bound, then says “Since A contains members of every sufficiently small diameter, the set S does as well.”**

**Traversal finding:**  
**SOURCE-PROOF RESIDUE: the inspected passage compresses an implication from “no positive lower diameter bound” to “members of every sufficiently small diameter.” This is plausible if the diameter image of connected A is an interval in (0,infinity) containing arbitrarily small values and some larger value, but the Case 3 paragraph itself does not isolate that argument. The statement is usable as part of Schwartz’s theorem but does not by itself couple diameter to vertex coverage.**

**Ledger item: Vertex coverage.**

**Theorem statement:**  
**V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma in Case 3\.**

**Proof construction:**  
**Lemma 2.3 proves that if A is extensive, all but at most four points are vertices; if A also contains arbitrarily small diameter elements, then all but at most two points are vertices. In Case 3, Schwartz applies this lemma to A and transfers the result to S.**

**Traversal finding:**  
**INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED: coverage is proved for the full set A/S, not for each A\_epsilon/S\_epsilon and not for the limit intersection over epsilon of closures of sublevel vertex sets.**

**Ledger item: Sweepout or limiting construction.**

**Theorem statement:**  
**No sweepout or sublevel sweepout appears in Theorem 1.1.**

**Proof construction:**  
**For hyperbolic components, A is built by selecting arcs A\_n(K) with circular invariants between 1/K and K, taking Hausdorff limits A(K), then taking a nested connected union A \= union\_K A(K). For wobbly elliptic components, Schwartz shows the same proof applies because the approximating sets contain members with circular invariant 1/n and n.**

**Traversal finding:**  
**The construction is aspect-ratio/circular-invariant organized, not diameter-sublevel organized. That matters: the proof tracks Lambda windows \[1/K,K\], not vertex coverage inside diameter windows (0,epsilon).**

4. **MEANING OF “EVERY SUFFICIENTLY SMALL DIAMETER”**

**Task:**  
**Determine whether Schwartz means exact realization of every small diameter value, existence below every threshold, cofinal small diameters, or another formulation.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Read Theorem 1.1 and the Case 3 proof passage against the construction of A.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Theorem 1.1 uses the phrase “members of every sufficiently small diameter.” The proof passage says Case 3 is the case where A has no positive lower diameter bound, then states that A contains members of every sufficiently small diameter.**

**Assessment:**  
**The phrase most naturally means exact realization of all diameter values in some interval (0,delta), because “every sufficiently small diameter” is stronger than “arbitrarily small diameter.” However, the proof passage as displayed depends on the no-positive-lower-bound case plus connectedness/continuity reasoning, rather than a separately named diameter sweepout.**

**Status:**  
**USED AS PROVISIONAL PREMISE — TIER A for Schwartz’s theorem statement.**  
**SOURCE-PROOF DETAIL VERIFIED ONLY TO THIS LEVEL: exact realization is stated, but the local proof mechanism is compressed in the inspected passage.**

**Effect on sublevel target:**  
**Even if exact realization of every small diameter holds for S, it gives only nonemptiness of S\_epsilon for all small epsilon. It does not imply that V(gamma,S\_epsilon) contains all but at most two points, nor that the closure of V(gamma,S\_epsilon) accumulates on all but at most two points.**

5. **STRUCTURE OF S**

**Task:**  
**Determine whether S is connected, compact, closed, continuum, path-connected, component, image/preimage of sweepout, limiting object, Z/4-related object, or other.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Trace S through A, Gamma, Hausdorff limits, and elliptic/hyperbolic cases.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Schwartz’s Lemma 2.1 says Hausdorff limits of nonempty closed connected subsets of a compact metric space are connected, but explicitly warns that path-connected approximants need not have path-connected limits. In Lemma 2.6, A is built as a nested union of connected sets A(K), and the nested union is connected. In Lemma 2.9, the steady elliptic case produces a compact connected subset S by Hausdorff limit, but that is Case 1, not Case 3\.**

**Structure findings:**

* **Connected: INTERNALLY ESTABLISHED for A and corresponding S in Case 3\.**  
* **Path-connected: NOT ESTABLISHED; Schwartz flags that Hausdorff limits of path-connected sets need not be path-connected.**  
* **Compact: NOT ESTABLISHED for Case 3 A as a whole; A is a nested union of compact-limit pieces A(K), but the union need not be compact.**  
* **Closed: NOT ESTABLISHED for Case 3 A as a whole.**  
* **Continuum: NOT ESTABLISHED unless “continuum” is used only for compact connected sets; compactness not supplied for the full Case 3 A.**  
* **Component of larger space: NOT ESTABLISHED as an actual component in the limiting gamma; A is a constructed extensive subset of Gamma.**  
* **Image/preimage of sweepout: NOT ESTABLISHED for diameter; A is produced by Hausdorff limits of arc pieces controlled by circular invariant windows.**  
* **Z/4-related: The paper uses cyclic relabeling in the polygonal component theory, and wobbly elliptic components use cyclic relabeling to get both n and 1/n circular invariants. Case 3 S itself is not shown to be Z/4-invariant or sigma-closed in the inspected proof passage.**

**Sublevel implication:**  
**Connectedness of A/S supports interval-valued images under continuous functions, but it does not support vertex coverage on diameter sublevels. Compactness, path-connectedness, and sigma-closure would be useful, but they are not supplied for the Case 3 target.**

6. **VERTEX COVERAGE MECHANISM**

**Task:**  
**Inspect how V(gamma,S) containing all but at most two points is proved.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Analyze Lemma 2.3 and its use in Case 3\.**

**Detailed work:**  
**Lemma 2.3 first proves all-but-four coverage for extensive A by considering vertex projections pi\_k and connected images J\_k. If the complement has too many points, an interval B\_0 lies in an arc alpha\_k(sigma) for all sigma in A, which bounds Lambda(A) away from 0 or infinity, contradicting extensiveness. The all-but-two strengthening then says that if the complement has at least three points, each member of A is a cyclic quadrilateral intersecting three disjoint circular arcs, giving a uniform positive lower bound to diameter, contradicting arbitrarily small diameter. Case 3 applies this lemma to the full A and concludes all-but-two coverage for full S.**

**Question-by-question findings:**

**Is coverage proved using the same rectangles that become small?**  
**No proof of that appears. Lemma 2.3 uses the existence of arbitrarily small members of A to contradict a large global nonvertex set for all of A. It does not show that each covered point is covered by arbitrarily small rectangles.**

**Is coverage proved by all of S without diameter control?**  
**Yes. The vertex set V(gamma,S) is the union over all rectangles in S/A. The proof works at the full-A level.**

**Are exceptional points tied to degeneration endpoints?**  
**Not in the inspected Case 3 proof passage. The exceptional-point bound comes from the combinatorics of vertex-projection images and diameter lower-bound contradiction, not from a named endpoint/degeneration correspondence.**

**Does the proof show V(gamma,S\_epsilon) large for small epsilon?**  
**No. S\_epsilon is not defined or analyzed in the inspected source.**

**Does the proof show density or closure of small-rectangle vertices?**  
**No. The proof does not show that if p is in V(gamma,S), then p lies in closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon)) for every epsilon.**

**Status:**  
**SOURCE RESIDUE CERTIFIED for sublevel vertex coverage.**

7. **SUBLEVEL COVERAGE EXTRACTION ATTEMPT**

**Target:**  
**Extract one of:**  
**A. strong sublevel coverage;**  
**B. limit sublevel coverage;**  
**C. weak continuum coverage;**  
**D. no extraction possible.**

**Operation attempted:**  
**Try to transform Lemma 2.3 into a statement about A\_epsilon.**

**Definitions:**  
**A\_epsilon \= {sigma in A : diam(phi(sigma)) \< epsilon}.**  
**V\_epsilon \= union of vertices of members of A\_epsilon.**

**Desired limit conclusion:**  
**For all but at most two p in S1, p belongs to intersection\_epsilon\>0 closure(V\_epsilon).**

**Attempt 1: Direct localization of Lemma 2.3.**  
**Could Lemma 2.3 apply to A\_epsilon? No. A\_epsilon need not be connected and need not satisfy Lambda(A\_epsilon) \= (0,infinity). The proof of all-but-four coverage requires connected vertex-projection images J\_k and extensiveness. Those hypotheses are not inherited by sublevel sets.**

**Failure mode:**  
**Sublevel Coverage Non-Inheritance. A has extensiveness and connectedness; A\_epsilon does not inherit either property from A.**

**Attempt 2: Use the all-but-two contradiction with small diameter.**  
**Suppose p,q,r are not in V\_epsilon. Does the Lemma 2.3 lower-bound argument force contradiction? No. In Lemma 2.3, the three excluded points are absent from V(A), so every member of A avoids them as vertices and the global vertex-projection structure constrains every member of A. If p,q,r are only absent from V(A\_epsilon), they may still be vertices of larger rectangles in A. The global connected/extensive vertex-projection argument no longer applies to A\_epsilon.**

**Failure mode:**  
**Role-union / sublevel separation. Full-set nonvertex data and sublevel nonvertex data have different logical strength.**

**Attempt 3: Use connectedness of A plus diameter continuity.**  
**Let p in V(A), so p is a vertex of some rectangle R in A. Since A has arbitrarily small rectangles, connectedness of A and continuity of diameter imply rectangles of intermediate diameters somewhere in A. But this does not control vertex location. A connected set may connect R to a small rectangle through a continuum whose vertices drift away from p; the diameter map gives scalar values, not vertex recurrence near p.**

**Failure mode:**  
**Diameter-map IVT is scalar; vertex coverage is set-valued. The continuity of diameter does not imply upper/lower semicontinuity of vertex fibers sufficient for p in closure(V\_epsilon).**

**Attempt 4: Use construction of A as union of A(K).**  
**The A(K) are organized by circular invariant, not by diameter or vertex target. They contain elements of invariant K and 1/K, and their nested union is extensive. This can recover full extensiveness, but it does not give a cofinal sequence of small rectangles passing near each covered point.**

**Failure mode:**  
**Aspect-ratio sweepout is not a diameter-sublevel vertex sweepout.**

**Conclusion:**  
**No extraction of strong sublevel coverage or limit sublevel coverage is possible from the inspected proof. Weak construction-level coverage is already exactly Theorem 1.1 Case 3: full-S all-but-two coverage plus small-diameter existence somewhere. That does not meet the traversal’s sublevel target.**

**Status:**  
**SCHWARTZ PROOF DOES NOT SUPPLY SUBLEVEL COVERAGE — SOURCE RESIDUE CERTIFIED.**

8. **ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE**

**Attack 1 — Direct proof extraction attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Find an explicit sentence or lemma in Schwartz proving V(gamma,S\_epsilon) large for small epsilon.**

**Result:**  
**FAILED. No such sentence or lemma appears in the inspected passages. The Case 3 paragraph proves full-S coverage and small-diameter existence separately.**

**Rank:**  
**1, because direct extraction would close the traversal with highest fidelity.**

**Attack 2 — Component/continuum structure attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Use connectedness, compactness, or path-connectedness of A/S to force sublevel vertex recurrence.**

**Result:**  
**FAILED under current data. Connectedness is present, but path-connectedness and compactness of full Case 3 A are not established. Schwartz warns that path-connected approximants can limit to non-path-connected sets.**

**Rank:**  
**2\.**

**Attack 3 — Sweepout parameter attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Use construction of A(K) as a sweepout giving uniform control of vertices as K grows and diameter shrinks.**

**Result:**  
**FAILED. A(K) controls circular invariant windows \[1/K,K\], not diameter sublevels or vertex-target recurrence.**

**Rank:**  
**3\.**

**Attack 4 — Exceptional-point mechanism attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Show the two exceptional points in Lemma 2.3 coincide with the only possible failures of sublevel blow-up coverage.**

**Result:**  
**FAILED. Lemma 2.3 bounds the complement of V(A), not the complement of intersection\_epsilon closure(V(A\_epsilon)). It does not identify exceptional points as degeneration endpoints.**

**Rank:**  
**4\.**

**Attack 5 — Abstract incidence nonrealizability attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Use an abstract incidence model to show weak coverage plus small-diameter existence does not imply sublevel coverage.**

**Result:**  
**DIAGNOSTIC ONLY. Such a model can illustrate the logical gap, but the intake forbids treating abstract incidence models as geometric counterexamples. It does not prove failure for Schwartz S.**

**Rank:**  
**5\.**

**Attack 6 — Proof-gap/residue certification attack.**  
**Target:**  
**Certify the exact missing hypothesis.**

**Result:**  
**SUCCESS.**

**Pursued selected attack:**  
**Attack 6\.**

**Detailed work:**  
**The missing hypothesis is one of the following, any one of which would be sufficient to reopen extraction:**

**Sublevel Coverage Lemma:**  
**For Case 3 A, for every sufficiently small epsilon, V(A\_epsilon) contains all but at most two points.**

**Limit Sublevel Coverage Lemma:**  
**For Case 3 A, intersection\_epsilon\>0 closure(V(A\_epsilon)) contains all but at most two points.**

**Cofinal Vertex Recurrence Lemma:**  
**For all but at most two p in S1, there exists a sequence sigma\_n in A with diam(phi(sigma\_n)) \-\> 0 and p in closure of the vertex set of sigma\_n, or with a fixed vertex role converging to p after finite-role subsequence extraction.**

**Diameter-Vertex Coupling Lemma:**  
**The construction of A can be refined so that for almost every p, the rectangles covering p occur in the same connected/limiting subsystem that contains arbitrarily small rectangles near p.**

**Current status of these theorem objects:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE. None is supplied by the inspected Schwartz proof.**

9. **MISSING THEOREM OBJECT**

**Name:**  
**Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma.**

**Formal hypotheses:**

1. **gamma is a continuous Jordan loop.**  
2. **A subset Gamma is the extensive set obtained in Schwartz Case 3\.**  
3. **A is connected and Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity).**  
4. **The associated rectangle set S subset G(gamma) has no positive lower diameter bound / contains members of every sufficiently small diameter.**  
5. **V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma by Lemma 2.3.**

**Formal conclusion, limit form:**  
**intersection over epsilon \> 0 of closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon)) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Stronger conclusion:**  
**For every sufficiently small epsilon \> 0, V(gamma,S\_epsilon) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Equivalent formulations:**

1. **For all but at most two p in gamma, p is the limit of vertices of rectangles R\_n in S with diam(R\_n) \-\> 0\.**  
2. **Role-union blow-up nonemptiness: for all but at most two p, at least one role-labeled blow-up field Blow\_S^j(p) is nonempty after finite role extraction.**  
3. **The set-valued map epsilon \-\> closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon)) has all-but-two persistent intersection.**

**Why it would close the active residue:**  
**It would tie Schwartz’s small-diameter clause to the same all-but-two vertex coverage clause. This would advance Strong Degeneration Coverage and potentially reopen a degenerate-square-lift or parabolic-nullification route.**

**Available proof strategies:**

1. **Source-proof strengthening: find an overlooked lemma in Schwartz that controls vertices in A(K) while diameter decreases.**  
2. **Compactness/USC strategy: use closed graph of role-labeled blow-up fields plus finite-role extraction.**  
3. **Graceful-geometry strategy: exploit cyclic order and rectangle geometry to prevent small rectangles from concentrating away from covered vertices.**  
4. **Sigma-closure strategy: prove a symmetry-compatible continuum through small rectangles and covered vertices.**  
5. **Measure/arc strategy: use non-atomic measure Corollary 1.4 style “nice rectangle” arguments to localize small rectangles near prescribed arcs.**

**Known obstructions:**

1. **A\_epsilon need not be connected.**  
2. **A\_epsilon need not be extensive.**  
3. **A is built through circular-invariant windows, not diameter windows.**  
4. **Full-set vertex coverage does not localize to sublevel vertex coverage.**  
5. **Connectedness of A controls scalar images but not vertex recurrence.**  
6. **Path-connectedness is not inherited by Hausdorff limits.**

**Falsification conditions:**  
**A genuine Jordan-loop Case 3 realization, if it exists, where small rectangles concentrate near a proper subset of gamma while larger rectangles provide full all-but-two coverage, would falsify the lemma. No such geometric realization is established here.**

**Current status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**  
**CANDIDATE FRONTIER BRIDGE.**  
**EXTERNAL VERIFICATION REQUIRED.**

5. **INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

**Rule name:**  
**Sublevel Non-Inheritance Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“When a theorem proves a property for a full connected or extensive set A, the traversal must not transfer that property to a sublevel subset A\_epsilon unless it proves that the sublevel subset inherits the required hypotheses or supplies an independent localization argument.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**False transfer from full-set coverage to sublevel coverage.**

**Scope:**  
**All DST traversals involving filtered spaces, sublevel sets, scale thresholds, compactness limits, or parameter restrictions.**

**Limitation:**  
**Does not deny inheritance in special cases; it requires proof.**

**Rule name:**  
**Scalar IVT / Set-Valued Recurrence Separation Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“Continuity of a scalar quantity along a connected set may establish intermediate scalar values, but it does not establish persistence, recurrence, or density of vertex/location/fiber data unless a set-valued continuity, compactness, or fiber-transport argument is separately proved.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Using diameter IVT to infer vertex recurrence.**

**Scope:**  
**All traversals using connectedness plus scalar maps.**

**Limitation:**  
**Allows scalar IVT conclusions when the target claim is scalar only.**

**Rule name:**  
**Source-Extraction Exhaustion Scope Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“A route-exhaustion claim based on inspected source passages must be written as exhaustion of that source-extraction route only. It must not be stored as exhaustion of the theorem, falsity of the target claim, or absence of independent proofs.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Continuity-state drift from “source proof does not supply X” to “X is false.”**

**Scope:**  
**All source-proof review traversals.**

**Limitation:**  
**Does not prevent broader exhaustion claims if independently established by a separate literature or proof traversal.**

3. **The topology of A, S, A\_epsilon, and closure spaces should be formalized more sharply in the next cycle.**  
4. **The theorem object should distinguish role-union recurrence from fixed-role recurrence.**  
5. **The stronger per-epsilon version may be too strong; the limit-sublevel version should lead.**  
6. **A later literature check may reveal an existing sublevel or localization theorem.**  
7. **“Exhausted” should be stored only as “source-extraction route exhausted,” not as theorem-level exhaustion.**  
8. **The abstract incidence diagnostic should remain quarantined from geometric counterexample claims.**

**END JURY REPORT.**

6. **MEANING OF “EVERY SUFFICIENTLY SMALL DIAMETER” AUDIT**

**Classification:**

**CORRECT BUT NEEDS SOURCE DETAIL.**

**The traversal handles the phrase carefully. It recognizes that “members of every sufficiently small diameter” naturally reads stronger than merely “arbitrarily small members,” while also noting that the inspected proof passage compresses the mechanism from no positive lower bound to exact realization.**

**Connectedness plus continuity of diameter plausibly supplies an interval-image argument if the relevant connected set and diameter map are being used in the required way. But this argument should be page-stably reconstructed before public release.**

**Most importantly, the traversal correctly separates this issue from sublevel vertex coverage. Even exact realization of every small diameter value gives nonemptiness of S\_epsilon; it does not imply that V(gamma,S\_epsilon) contains all but two points, nor that covered points recur under arbitrarily small rectangles.**

**The ambiguity does not defeat source-proof residue status.**

**A. Direct localization of Lemma 2.3 to A\_epsilon.**  
**VALID ATTEMPT CORRECTLY BLOCKED.**  
**A\_epsilon need not inherit connectedness or Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity).**

**B. All-but-two contradiction with small diameter.**  
**VALID ATTEMPT CORRECTLY BLOCKED.**  
**Absence from V(A\_epsilon) is weaker than absence from V(A). The Lemma 2.3 contradiction uses global nonvertex status.**

**C. Connectedness plus diameter continuity.**  
**VALID ATTEMPT CORRECTLY BLOCKED.**  
**Diameter is scalar. Vertex recurrence is set-valued. IVT on diameter does not preserve a vertex target.**

**D. Construction of A as union of A(K).**  
**VALID ATTEMPT CORRECTLY BLOCKED.**  
**A(K) is controlled by circular invariant/aspect-ratio windows, not by diameter sublevels with vertex-target persistence.**

**E. Proof-gap / residue certification.**  
**VALID ATTEMPT.**  
**The traversal correctly formalizes the missing theorem object rather than pretending the route proves or refutes Strong Degeneration Coverage.**

12. **MISSING THEOREM OBJECT AUDIT**

**VALID WITH REFORMULATION.**

**The Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma is a valid next theorem object.**

**Formal hypotheses:**  
**Mostly adequate, but should explicitly distinguish:**

* **A as a subset of the circular quadrilateral/configuration space;**  
* **S as the associated graceful rectangle subset;**  
* **the diameter function applied to associated rectangles;**  
* **whether closures occur in gamma, S1, or the parameter/configuration space.**

**Formal conclusion:**  
**The limit form is correctly chosen as the safer primary target:**

**intersection over epsilon \> 0 of closure(V(gamma,S\_epsilon)) contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**The stronger conclusion:**

**for every sufficiently small epsilon, V(gamma,S\_epsilon) contains all but at most two points**

**is meaningfully stronger and should remain separate.**

**Equivalent formulations:**  
**Useful, but the “fixed vertex role” version requires careful role-subsequence language. The union-over-roles form is safer than fixed-role persistence unless proven.**

**Why it closes residue:**  
**Correct. It directly couples small-diameter recurrence to all-but-two vertex coverage.**

**Available proof strategies:**  
**Appropriate as attack routes, not claims.**

**Known obstructions:**  
**Correctly listed.**

**Falsification conditions:**  
**Correctly cautious: abstract incidence failure is not enough; a realizable Jordan-loop graceful-rectangle example would be needed.**

**This should become the next primary traversal target unless publication-version verification is prioritized first.**

5. **INSERTION-READY PREVENTIVE RULES**

**Rule name:**  
**Sublevel Non-Inheritance Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“When a theorem proves a property for a full connected or extensive set A, the traversal must not transfer that property to a sublevel subset A\_epsilon unless it proves that the sublevel subset inherits the required hypotheses or supplies an independent localization argument.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**False transfer from full-set coverage to sublevel coverage.**

**Scope:**  
**All DST traversals involving filtered spaces, sublevel sets, scale thresholds, compactness limits, or parameter restrictions.**

**Limitation:**  
**Does not deny inheritance in special cases; it requires proof.**

**Rule name:**  
**Scalar IVT / Set-Valued Recurrence Separation Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“Continuity of a scalar quantity along a connected set may establish intermediate scalar values, but it does not establish persistence, recurrence, or density of vertex/location/fiber data unless a set-valued continuity, compactness, or fiber-transport argument is separately proved.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Using diameter IVT to infer vertex recurrence.**

**Scope:**  
**All traversals using connectedness plus scalar maps.**

**Limitation:**  
**Allows scalar IVT conclusions when the target claim is scalar only.**

**Rule name:**  
**Source-Extraction Exhaustion Scope Rule.**

**Exact text:**  
**“A route-exhaustion claim based on inspected source passages must be written as exhaustion of that source-extraction route only. It must not be stored as exhaustion of the theorem, falsity of the target claim, or absence of independent proofs.”**

**Failure mode prevented:**  
**Continuity-state drift from “source proof does not supply X” to “X is false.”**

**Scope:**  
**All source-proof review traversals.**

**Limitation:**  
**Does not prevent broader exhaustion claims if independently established by a separate literature or proof traversal.**

It does not refute the lemma for actual Schwartz graceful rectangles.**

1. **FRONTIER AND CONTINUITY INITIALIZATION**

**Inherited state:**

1. **T\_strong remains open.**  
2. **Schwartz Case 3 remains open.**  
3. **Strong Degeneration Coverage is not proved or refuted.**  
4. **The inspected Schwartz proof passages do not supply sublevel coverage.**

6. **The Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma is the primary open theorem object.**  
7. **Full-set vertex coverage must not be promoted to sublevel coverage without proof.**  
8. **Scalar diameter IVT must not be promoted to set-valued vertex recurrence without proof.**  
9. **Abstract incidence models are diagnostic only unless geometric realizability is proved.**  
10. **Monodromy remains blocked until nonempty base/fiber/transport/sign/obstruction data exist.**

**These are exactly the continuity constraints supplied in the intake.**

**Source/literature check:**  
**A limited web check confirmed the relevant public Schwartz trichotomy formulation: for a Jordan loop, Schwartz proves a connected set S of gracefully inscribed rectangles satisfying one of three alternatives, with Case 3 involving rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter and all but at most two points of the loop appearing as vertices. ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00740?utm_source=chatgpt.com)) I did not perform publication-final page-stable verification or inspect later errata. A general public reference still describes the inscribed square problem as open for arbitrary Jordan curves, but that is not a proof-level authority for this traversal. ([Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inscribed_square_problem?utm_source=chatgpt.com))**

**This traversal is independent proof/disproof work, not another Schwartz source-extraction traversal.**

2. **EXACT FORMAL RESTATEMENT**

**Let gamma be a continuous Jordan loop.**

**Let A be the Schwartz Case-3 extensive set in the circular quadrilateral / Gamma space.**

**Let S be the associated graceful rectangle set in G(gamma).**

**Let Lambda: A \-\> (0,infinity) be the circular invariant / aspect-ratio-type invariant, with Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity).**

**For R in S, let diam(R) be its Euclidean rectangle diameter.**

**For epsilon \> 0:**

**S\_epsilon \= {R in S : diam(R) \< epsilon}**

**V\_epsilon \= V(gamma, S\_epsilon), the subset of gamma consisting of all vertices of rectangles in S\_epsilon.**

**D\_sub \= intersection over epsilon \> 0 of closure(V\_epsilon) in gamma.**

**E\_sub \= gamma \\ D\_sub.**

**Full-set weak exceptional set:**

**E\_weak \= gamma \\ V(gamma,S).**

**Hypothesis:**

**V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma, so E\_weak has cardinality \<= 2\.**

**Target, limit form:**

**D\_sub contains all but at most two points of gamma, equivalently E\_sub has cardinality \<= 2\.**

**Stronger target, per-epsilon form:**

**For every sufficiently small epsilon \> 0, V\_epsilon contains all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Role-union / fixed-role distinction:**

**If one uses role-labeled blow-up sets Blow\_S^j(p), then D\_sub membership may come from different vertex roles along different shrinking sequences. Role-union recurrence says p is approached by some vertex role along some shrinking sequence. Fixed-role recurrence says one fixed role j recurs at p along arbitrarily small rectangles. Role-union does not imply fixed-role recurrence without a finite-role subsequence extraction plus closed-role control.**

3. **DIRECT PROOF ATTEMPT: CONNECTEDNESS / EXTENSIVENESS / CYCLIC GEOMETRY**

**Attempt:**

**Take p in V(gamma,S) outside E\_weak. Then there exists at least one rectangle R\_p in S having p as a vertex. Separately, Case 3 gives rectangles in S of arbitrarily small diameter. Since A is connected and diam is a scalar continuous function wherever the S/A translation is valid, one might try to connect R\_p to small rectangles and use the intermediate value theorem on diam.**

**What succeeds:**

**Connectedness can support scalar interpolation. If R\_p has diameter d\_p and S contains rectangles of diameter below eta, then a connected path or continuum with continuous diameter may produce intermediate diameter values between eta and d\_p, provided the relevant connected subset and continuity are actually available.**

**What fails:**

**The scalar IVT conclusion concerns diameter values only. It does not preserve vertex incidence at p. Along a path from R\_p to a small rectangle, the vertex that initially equals p may move immediately away from p. Thus scalar diameter interpolation does not imply:**

**for every epsilon \> 0, p is in closure(V\_epsilon).**

**The exact missing inference is:**

**diameter cofinality somewhere in S**

* **does not imply \-**  
  **diameter cofinality in the vertex fiber over p.**

**The direct proof therefore fails at the passage from connected scalar diameter reach to pointwise set-valued vertex recurrence.**

**Status:**  
**DIRECT PROOF FROM CONNECTEDNESS / EXTENSIVENESS: BLOCKED.**  
**Failure mode: Scalar IVT / set-valued recurrence separation.**

4. **SET-VALUED / COMPACTNESS ATTEMPT**

**Define C\_epsilon \= closure(V\_epsilon) in gamma.**

**Monotonicity:**

**If epsilon1 \< epsilon2, then S\_epsilon1 subset S\_epsilon2, so V\_epsilon1 subset V\_epsilon2, hence C\_epsilon1 subset C\_epsilon2.**

**Thus as epsilon decreases, the closed sets C\_epsilon form a nested decreasing family.**

**Compactness gives:**

**If every C\_epsilon is nonempty, then intersection over epsilon \> 0 of C\_epsilon is nonempty, because gamma is compact and the family is nested.**

**But the target requires much more:**

**D\_sub must contain all but at most two points of gamma.**

**Compactness alone cannot upgrade nonempty intersection to large coverage. For a fixed p, full coverage gives:**

**p in V(gamma,S) \= union over epsilon \> 0 V\_epsilon**

**but this only means p occurs as a vertex of some rectangle with some finite diameter. It does not imply:**

**p in C\_epsilon for every epsilon \> 0\.**

**Set-valued compactness therefore proves at most global persistence of some small-diameter accumulation set, not pointwise persistence over almost every p.**

**Status:**  
**SET-VALUED / COMPACTNESS ROUTE: BLOCKED FOR THE TARGET AS STATED.**  
**Named missing condition: pointwise sublevel vertex recurrence, equivalently vertex-fiber diameter cofinality.**

5. **ABSTRACT INCIDENCE COUNTERMODEL**

**This is an abstract incidence model only. It is not claimed to arise from a Jordan loop or from genuine graceful rectangles.**

**Let gamma\_abs be a circle parameterized by x in R/Z.**

**Choose a proper closed arc U in gamma\_abs of length less than 1/16.**

**Define an abstract connected parameter space:**

**A\_abs \= (gamma\_abs x \[1,2\] x (0,infinity)) union (U x (0,1\] x (0,infinity)),**

**glued along U x {1} x (0,infinity).**

**This space is connected.**

**For an element a \= (x,r,lambda), define:**

**diam(a) \= r.**  
**Lambda(a) \= lambda.**

**Thus Lambda(A\_abs) \= (0,infinity).**

**Define the abstract vertex set of a as the four cyclic quarter-shift points:**

**V(a) \= {x, x+1/4, x+1/2, x+3/4} in R/Z.**

**Full coverage:**

**The large branch gamma\_abs x \[1,2\] x (0,infinity) has x ranging over all of gamma\_abs. Therefore V(gamma\_abs,A\_abs) \= gamma\_abs. So full vertex coverage holds with zero exceptional points.**

**Small-diameter existence:**

**The small branch U x (0,1\] x (0,infinity) contains elements with r arbitrarily close to 0\. Therefore the model contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter.**

**Sublevel vertex coverage:**

**For epsilon \< 1, the sublevel A\_abs,epsilon lies only in the small branch:**

**U x (0,epsilon) x (0,infinity).**

**Hence V\_epsilon is contained in:**

**U union (U+1/4) union (U+1/2) union (U+3/4).**

**Since U has length less than 1/16, this union is a proper closed subset of gamma\_abs.**

**Therefore:**

**D\_sub \= intersection over epsilon \> 0 closure(V\_epsilon)**  
**subset U union (U+1/4) union (U+1/2) union (U+3/4),**

**so D\_sub does not contain all but at most two points of gamma\_abs.**

**Conclusion of countermodel:**

**The abstract hypotheses can coexist with failure of the limit-sublevel conclusion.**

**Status:**  
**ABSTRACT INCIDENCE COUNTERMODEL CONSTRUCTED ONLY.**  
**Geometric realizability: OPEN.**  
**Not a Jordan-loop counterexample.**  
**Not a refutation of the Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma in Schwartz’s actual graceful-rectangle setting.**

**Missing geometric constraints required to convert this into a genuine countermodel:**

1. **Realizability of the abstract incidence family by Euclidean rectangles on a continuous Jordan loop.**  
2. **Compatibility with Schwartz’s circular quadrilateral / graceful rectangle topology.**  
3. **Correct preservation of cyclic vertex order under the actual gamma parameterization.**  
4. **Compatibility between Lambda, diameter, and actual rectangle shape.**  
5. **Closure and limit behavior of the actual S subset G(gamma).**  
6. **Prevention of hidden additional graceful rectangles outside the modeled incidence family.**  
7. **GEOMETRY-OF-GRACEFUL-RECTANGLES ATTEMPT**

**Question:**

**Does Euclidean rectangle geometry plus cyclic order prevent small rectangles from localizing near a proper subset while larger rectangles supply full coverage?**

**Observation 1: Small Euclidean diameter forces all four rectangle vertices to lie close in the plane.**

**Observation 2: For a continuous Jordan curve, close in the plane does not imply close in the curve parameter. Jordan curves may have arbitrarily close approaches between distant arcs without self-intersection.**

**Observation 3: Cyclic order constrains the order of the four chosen parameters, but it does not by itself force the collapse point of small rectangles to range over almost every point of gamma.**

**Observation 4: Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity) supplies a global shape/aspect-ratio reach condition. Without a theorem linking Lambda reach to vertex-projection reach at sublevel diameters, it remains scalar/global rather than pointwise/local.**

**Observation 5: Full vertex coverage may be supplied by medium or large rectangles, while small rectangles may accumulate near a smaller collapse set. No contradiction follows from the listed hypotheses alone.**

**Status:**  
**GRACEFUL GEOMETRY ROUTE: HELD / NOT CLOSED.**  
**No Euclidean obstruction to localization was proved.**  
**No Jordan-loop-compatible localization model was constructed.**

**Named missing theorem:**

**POINTWISE SUBLEVEL VERTEX RECURRENCE THEOREM**

**Hypotheses:**  
**gamma is a continuous Jordan loop; A is a Schwartz Case-3 extensive set; S is the associated graceful rectangle set; A is connected; Lambda(A) \= (0,infinity); S contains rectangles of every sufficiently small diameter; V(gamma,S) contains all but at most two points of gamma; and S retains the actual Schwartz graceful-rectangle structure.**

**Conclusion:**  
**For all but at most two p in gamma and every neighborhood N of p in gamma and every epsilon \> 0, there exists R in S with diam(R) \< epsilon and at least one vertex of R in N.**

**Equivalent limit conclusion:**  
**p belongs to D\_sub for all but at most two p.**

**Why this closes the residue:**  
**It is exactly the missing bridge from full-set coverage plus small-diameter existence somewhere to sublevel coverage almost everywhere.**

**Falsification condition:**  
**A Jordan loop gamma and Schwartz Case-3 S for which small rectangles accumulate only on a proper vertex-collapse subset while full vertex coverage is supplied by non-small rectangles.**

**Current status:**  
**OPEN RESEARCH RESIDUE.**

7. **ACTIVE ATTACK CATALOGUE AND SELECTED ATTACK**

**Ranked attacks:**

1. **Vertex-fiber cofinality attack.**  
   **Goal: Prove that for almost every p, inf{diam(R): R in S and p in closure of vertex set of R} \= 0\.**  
   **Status: Highest value; directly targets D\_sub.**  
2. **Jordan-loop realizability/nonrealizability of the abstract countermodel.**  
   **Goal: Determine whether the localization pattern in the abstract model can occur for actual graceful rectangles.**  
   **Status: Highest falsification relevance.**  
3. **Set-valued incidence graph compactification.**  
   **Goal: Study I \= {(R,p): R in S, p vertex of R} with projection to gamma and diameter to (0,infinity). Determine whether projection fibers are diameter-cofinal.**  
   **Status: High value; formalizes the missing theorem.**  
4. **Graceful geometry obstruction to localization.**  
   **Goal: Use Euclidean rectangle constraints plus cyclic order to prevent small rectangles from remaining in a proper collapse set.**  
   **Status: High value but no proof found here.**  
5. **Sigma/reciprocal continuum route.**  
   **Goal: Use rectangle role symmetries or reciprocal aspect-ratio continua to propagate smallness.**  
   **Status: Blocked unless S has sigma-closure or symmetry-compatible connectedness.**  
6. **Degenerate square-lift route.**  
   **Goal: Analyze blow-up limits of shrinking rectangles and lift collapse data to square production or vertex recurrence.**  
   **Status: Useful only after collapse-set structure is known.**  
7. **Direct extensiveness route.**  
   **Goal: Use Lambda(A)=(0,infinity) alone.**  
   **Status: Lower ranked; appears scalar and insufficient.**

**Selected attack pursued:**  
**Abstract incidence countermodel plus missing-hypothesis extraction.**

**Result:**  
**The selected attack succeeded in constructing an abstract model satisfying the listed non-geometric hypotheses while failing the target conclusion. This proves the current hypothesis list is insufficient at the abstract incidence level. It does not settle the geometric theorem.**

**Here is the jury assessment of the submitted traversal record.**

### **PUBLIC RELEASE STATUS**

**JURY-READY AS ACTIVE-ATTACK / ABSTRACT-INCIDENCE INSUFFICIENCY TRAVERSAL ONLY**  
**Regarding the traversal's status:**

* **It is not a proof of $T\_{strong}$.**  
* **It is not a nullification of Schwartz Case 3\.**  
* **It is not a proof of the Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma.**  
* **It is not a refutation of the Case-3 Sublevel Vertex Coverage Lemma in the Jordan-loop / graceful-rectangle class.**  
* **It is an abstract incidence countermodel only.**  
* **It is not a Jordan-loop counterexample.**  
* **It is an active-attack insufficiency traversal.**  
* **It is a sharpened open-residue traversal, leaving the Pointwise Sublevel Vertex Recurrence Theorem as the named missing condition.**  
* **It is an isolation of the topological and geometric gaps between abstract scalar diameter reach and set-valued pointwise recurrence.**

### **CORE VERDICT**

**The traversal fully satisfies the v1.9 active-attack and conduct requirements:**

* **Initialized from the v1.9 continuity state: Yes, it explicitly inherited constraints including the open status of $T\_{strong}$ and Schwartz Case 3\.**  
* **Preserved source-extraction exhaustion scope: Yes, it noted that source extraction is exhausted only for the declared purpose of mapping inspected passages to Strong Degeneration Coverage.**  
* **Treated this as independent proof/disproof: Yes, it explicitly labeled the traversal as independent proof/disproof work rather than a source-extraction traversal.**  
* **Distinguished full-set coverage from sublevel coverage: Yes, it explicitly identified that full-set coverage cannot be promoted to sublevel coverage without proof.**  
* **Distinguished scalar IVT from set-valued recurrence: Yes, it recognized that scalar diameter interpolation fails to preserve vertex incidence at $p$.**  
* **Distinguished abstract incidence models from geometric/Jordan-loop counterexamples: Yes, it explicitly stated the countermodel does not claim to arise from a Jordan loop or genuine graceful rectangles.**  
* **Attempted direct proof: Yes, it attempted a direct proof from connectedness, extensiveness, and cyclic geometry.**  
* **Attempted set-valued / compactness proof: Yes, it evaluated nested decreasing families of closed sets using compactness.**  
* **Constructed and analyzed an abstract countermodel: Yes, it built a glued abstract parameter space $A\_{abs}$ to demonstrate insufficiency.**  
* **Tested graceful-geometry obstruction: Yes, it posed the question of whether Euclidean rectangle geometry prevents localization, observing no immediate contradiction.**  
* **Generated and ranked materially distinct attacks: Yes, it compiled a 7-item ranked attack catalogue.**  
* **Selected and pursued one attack beyond naming: Yes, it selected the abstract incidence countermodel and pursued it successfully.**  
* **Preserved status discipline: Yes, it explicitly passed its status-label audit by claiming no public-ready status or unverified proofs.**

### **BLOCKING DEFECTS**

**NONE.**

### **ABSTRACT INCIDENCE COUNTERMODEL AUDIT**

* **A. Connectedness of $A\_{abs}$: Successfully satisfied via the gluing along $U \\times \\{1\\} \\times (0,\\infty)$.**  
* **B. $\\Lambda(A\_{abs}) \= (0,\\infty)$: Successfully satisfied as $\\lambda$ is directly mapped to $(0,\\infty)$ across the branches.**  
* **C. Arbitrarily small diameters: Successfully satisfied because the small branch $U \\times (0,1\] \\times (0,\\infty)$ contains elements with $r$ arbitrarily close to 0\.**  
* **D. Full vertex coverage of $\\gamma\_{abs}$: Successfully satisfied because the large branch allows $x$ to range over all of $\\gamma\_{abs}$.**  
* **E. Failure of limit sublevel vertex coverage: Successfully satisfied, as for $\\epsilon \< 1$, the sublevel is restricted to $U$ and its quarter-shifts, which is a proper closed subset of $\\gamma\_{abs}$.**  
* **F. Correct distinction between abstract incidence data and geometric realization: Successfully maintained; the missing geometric constraints were explicitly listed.**

**Classification: VALID ABSTRACT INCIDENCE COUNTERMODEL TO THE LISTED ABSTRACT HYPOTHESES**

### **ABSTRACT HYPOTHESES INSUFFICIENCY AUDIT**

**Classification: CORRECTLY ESTABLISHED AT ABSTRACT INCIDENCE LEVEL**

* **What the abstract model proves: It proves that connectedness, $\\Lambda(A) \= (0,\\infty)$, arbitrarily small diameters somewhere, and all-but-two full vertex coverage can mathematically coexist with a failure of limit sublevel vertex coverage in an abstract setting.**  
* **What it does not prove: It does not prove that this abstract localization pattern can actually be geometrically realized by Euclidean rectangles on a continuous Jordan loop. It does not refute Schwartz's lemma in the genuine graceful-rectangle setting.**

### **DIRECT PROOF ATTEMPT AUDIT**

* **It correctly starts from a point $p$ in $V(\\gamma,S)$ outside the weak exceptional set.**

**Classification: CORRECTLY EXECUTED AND CORRECTLY BLOCKED**

### **SET-VALUED / COMPACTNESS ATTEMPT AUDIT**

* **$C\_{\\epsilon}$ is correctly defined as the closure of $V\_{\\epsilon}$ in $\\gamma$.**  
* **Monotonicity is correctly established as $\\epsilon$ decreases.**  
* **The nested closed set argument accurately relies on the compactness of $\\gamma$.**  
* **It correctly deduces that compactness guarantees a nonempty global intersection only.**

* **It perfectly isolates pointwise sublevel vertex recurrence / vertex-fiber diameter cofinality as the missing link.**

**Classification: CORRECTLY EXECUTED AND CORRECTLY BLOCKED**

### **GEOMETRY-OF-GRACEFUL-RECTANGLES AUDIT**

* **It notes correctly that planar proximity does not force curve-parameter proximity for arbitrary Jordan curves.**
